باب نكاح اهل الشرك
ترجمه مشرکین کے نکاح کے بیان میں
کسی کافر نے بغیر گواہوں کے یا کسی کافر کی عدت میں نکاح کیا اور یہ ان کے دین میں جائز ہے پھر دونوں مسلمان ہو گئے پہلا نکاح برقرار ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
و اذا تزوج الكافر بغير شهود او فى عدة كافر و ذلك فى دينهم جائز ثم اسلما أقر عليه وهذا عند ابي حنيفةً و قال زفر النكاح فاسد في الوجهين الا انه لا يتعرض لهم قبل الاسلام والمرافعة الى الحكام وقال ابويوسف و محمد رحمهما الله فى الوجه الاول كما قال ابو حنيفة وفى الوجه الثانى كما قال زفر رحمه الله له ان الخطابات عامة على مامر من قبل فتلزمهم وانما لا يتعرض لهم لذمتهم اعراضا لاتقرير او اذا ترافعوا او اسلموا والحرمة قائمة وجب التفريق ولهما ان حرمة نكاح المعتدة مجمع عليها فكانوا ملتزمين لها وحرمة النكاح بغير شهود مختلف فيه ولم يلتزموا احكامنا بجميع الاختلافات ولابي حنيفة ان الحرمة لا يمكن اثباتها حقا للشرع لانهم لا يخاطبون بحقوقه ولاوجه الى ايجاب العدة حقا للزوج لانه لا يعتقده بخلاف ما اذا كانت تحت مسلم لانه يعتقده واذاصح النكاح فحالة المرافعة والاسلام حالة البقاء و الشهادة ليست شرط فيها وكذا العدة لا تنافيها كالمنكوحة اذاو طئت بشبهة
ترجمہ اور اگر کافر نے بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح کیا یا کافر کی عدت میں تھی حالانکہ یہ ان کے دین میں جائز ہے پھر دونوں مرد و عورت مسلمان ہو گئے۔ تو اسی نکاح پر باقی رکھے جائیں گے اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ نکاح دونوں صورتوں میں فاسد ہے مگر یہ کہ ان سے تعرض نہ کرے۔ اسلام اور مرافعہ الی الحکام سے پہلے اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے فرمایا پہلی صورت میں جیسا کہ ابو حنیفہ نے کہا اور دوسری صورت میں جیسا کہ امام زفر نے کہا۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خطابات شرع عام ہیں۔ چنانچہ پہلے گذر چکا تو وہ کافروں کو بھی لازم ہوں گے اور ان کے ذمہ کی وجہ سے ان سے تعرض نہ کرنا اعراض کے طور پر ہے کہ برقرار رکھنے کے طور پر اور جب انہوں نے (حکام کے پاس) مرافعہ کیا یا مسلمان ہو گئے اور حرمت موجود ہے تو تفریق واجب ہو گئی اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معتدہ کے نکاح کا حرام ہونا متفق علیہ ہے۔ پس کفار ا سکے ماننے کا التزام کرنے والے ہوں گے۔ اور بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح کی حرمت مختلف فیہ ہے اور انہوں نے تمام اختلافات کے ساتھ ہمارے احکام کا التزام نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حرمت کو ثابت کرنا بطور حق شرع کے ممکن نہیں ۔ اسلئے کہ وہ حقوق شرع کے مخاطب نہیں ہیں اور کوئی وجہ نہیں عدت واجب کرنا بطور حق زوجہ کے ۔ اسلئے کہ زوج اس کا اعتقاد نہیں رکھتا ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے جب ( کتابیہ عورت ) کسی مسلمان کے تحت ہو کیونکہ مسلمان اس کا اعتقاد رکھتا ہے
اور جب نکاح صحیح ہو گیا تو مرافعہ اور اسلام کی حالت بقائے نکاح کی حالت ہے۔ اور شہادت حالت بقاء میں شرط نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی عدت حالت بقاء کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ جیسے منکوحہ جبکہ شبہ کے ساتھ وطی کی گئی۔
تشریح مشرک وہ ہے جو خداوند تعالیٰ کے ساتھ کسی کو شریک بنائے جیسے نصرانی بت پرست بشر طیکہ خدا کا اقرار کرتا ہوں۔ لیکن یہاں اہل شرک سے مطلقاً کا فرمراد ہے جو مشرک اور منکر خدا سب کو شامل ہے۔ نکاح اہل شرک کو نکاح رقیق کے بعد بیان کیا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ مشرک مرتبہ میں رقیق سے ادون اور اخس ہے۔ حق جل مجدہ کا ارشاد ہے ولعبد مؤمن خير من مشرک
اس باب کے مسائل تین اصول پر مبنی ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ جو نکاح دو مسلمانوں کے درمیان صحیح ہوتا ہے وہ دو کافروں میں بھی صحیح ہوگا۔ اسی معنی میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول وارد ہے ولدت من نکاح لامن سفاح یعنی میں نکاح سے پیدا ہوا ہوں نہ کہ زنا سے۔ دوسرا اصول یہ ہے کہ جو نکاح دو مسلمانوں میں شرط وغیرہ فوت ہونے سے فاسد یا باطل ہو جاتا ہے کافروں میں اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ کفار بھی اس کو ممنوع سمجھتے ہیں تو وہ ممنوع ہوگا ۔ اور اگر کفار اس کو جائز سمجھتے ہیں تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کافروں کے حق میں نکاح ہو گا حتی کہ اگر دونوں مسلمان ہو گئے تو اسی نکاح پر باقی رکھے جائیں گے۔ تیسرا اصول یہ کہ جو نکاح محل حرام ہونے کی وجہ سے حرام ہو مثلاً بہن وغیرہ کے ساتھ نکاح کیا تو وہ ان کے اعتقاد پر جائز واقع ہوگا۔ اور مشائخ عراق کے قول پر فاسد ہوگا۔
صورت مسئلہ
ایک کافر نے کسی کافر عورت سے بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح کیا یا کسی کا فر کی عدت میں تھی اس سے نکاح کیا اور یہ ان کے دین میں جاڑ بھی ہے۔ پھر دونوں مسلمان ہو گئے تو اس بارے میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ دونوں کو سابقہ مذہب پر باقی رکھا جائے گا اور امام زور نے فرمایا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں نکاح فاسد ہے۔ البتہ ان کے ساتھ تعرض نہیں کریں گے یہاں تک کہ وہ مسلمان ہو جائیں یا مسلمان عادل حاکم کے پاس مرافعہ کریں۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ پہلی صورت یعنی نکاح بغیر شہود میں وہ حکم ہے جو امام صاحب نے فرمایا اور دوسری صورت یعنی کافر کی معتدہ سے نکاح کرنے کی صورت میں وہ حکم ہے جو امام زفر نے فرمایا ۔
امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خطابات شرع عام ہیں، مثلاً باری تعالیٰ کا قول و لا تـعـزمـوا عـقــدة النكاح حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجلہ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول لا نكاح الا بشهود یعنی تم تعلق نکاح کا ارادہ بھی مت کرو یہاں تک کہ عدت مقررہ اپنی ختم کو پہنچ جائے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح نہیں ہوتا ہے ) لہذا حکم بھی علی العموم ثابت ہوگا اور چونکہ خطابات عام ہیں اسلئے وہ کافروں کو بھی لا زم ہوں گے۔ البتہ کفار کے ساتھ تعرض نہیں کریں گے۔ اسلئے کہ ان کے ساتھ تعرض نہ کرنے کا عقد ذمہ کر رکھا ہے۔ لیکن یہ تعرض نہ کرنا اسلئے نہیں کہ ہم ان کے ان افعال کو درست سمجھتے ہیں بلکہ ان سے اعراض کرتے ہوئے ان کے ساتھ تعرض نہیں کیا جائے گا جیسا کہ وہ بت پرستی کرتے ہیں اور ہم بطور اعراض کے ان سے تعرض نہیں کرتے۔ البتہ جب وہ اپنا معاملہ مسلمان حاکم کے پاس لے گئے یا اسلام قبول کر لیا درانحالیکہ حرمت نکاح بھی موجود ہے تو اب تفریق لازم ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے و ان احكم بينهم بما انزل الله ولا تتبع اهوائهم آیت میں بینھم کی ضمیر کفار کی طرف راجع ہے ترجمہ ہوگا اور تو فیصلہ کر کفار کے درمیان اس کے مطابق جو اللہ نے اتارا اور ان کی خواہشات کا اتباع مت کر اس آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مسلمان حاکم شریعت کے مطابق فیصلہ دے گا۔
Chapter on the marriage of polytheists. Translation: Concerning the marriage of polytheists. A disbeliever married without witnesses or during the 'iddah of a disbeliever, and that is permissible in their religion, then both became Muslims; is the first marriage valid or not? Statements of the jurists. And if the disbeliever marries without witnesses or during the 'iddah of a disbeliever, and that is permissible in their religion, then they both embrace Islam, it is confirmed (the marriage remains valid) according to Abu Hanifa. Zufar said: The marriage is invalid in both cases, except that they are not interfered with before Islam and taking the case to the rulers. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: In the first case, as Abu Hanifa said; in the second case, as Zufar said. (Zufar's proof:) The addresses of the Shari'ah are general, as previously mentioned, so they bind them. They are not interfered with due to their dhimmah as a matter of turning away, not as confirmation. When they take the case (to Muslim rulers) or embrace Islam and the prohibition exists, separation becomes obligatory. (The Sahibayn's proof:) The prohibition of marrying a woman in 'iddah is agreed upon, so they (the disbelievers) are committed to it. The prohibition of marriage without witnesses is disputed, and they did not commit to our rulings with all differences. (Abu Hanifa's proof:) The prohibition cannot be established as a right of the Shari'ah because they are not addressed by its rights. There is no way to make 'iddah obligatory as a right of the husband because he does not believe in it, unlike when a (scriptuary woman) is under a Muslim because he believes in it. When the marriage is valid, then the state of taking to court and embracing Islam is a state of continuance. Testimony is not a condition for continuance, nor does 'iddah conflict with it, like a married woman who is intercourse with under a shubhah. Explanation: A polytheist (mushrik) is one who associates partners with Allah, like a Christian idol-worshipper [؟] who acknowledges God. But here, 'people of shirk' means absolute disbelievers, including polytheists and deniers of God. The marriage of polytheists is mentioned after the marriage of a slave because the polytheist is lower and more contemptible in rank than a slave. Allah said: 'And a believing slave is better than a polytheist' (Quran 2:221). The issues of this chapter are based on three principles: First, the marriage that is valid between two Muslims is also valid between two disbelievers. In this meaning, the Prophet said: 'I was born from marriage, not from fornication.' Second, the marriage that becomes invalid or void due to missing a condition etc. between two Muslims has two forms among disbelievers: if the disbelievers also consider it prohibited, then it is prohibited; if they consider it permissible, then according to Abu Hanifa it is a valid marriage for the disbelievers, and if they both become Muslim, they are left on that marriage. Third principle: The marriage that is forbidden due to the object being prohibited, e.g., marrying a sister, is valid according to their belief, and according to the scholars of Iraq, it is invalid. The case: A disbeliever married a disbelieving woman without witnesses or while she was in the 'iddah of a disbeliever, and that is permissible in their religion, then both become Muslims. According to Abu Hanifa, they are left on their previous marriage. Zufar said the marriage is invalid in both cases, but they are not interfered with until they become Muslims or take the case to a just Muslim ruler. The Sahibayn said in the first case (without witnesses) the ruling is as Abu Hanifa said, and in the second case (marrying during 'iddah) the ruling is as Zufar said. Zufar's proof: The addresses of the Shari'ah are general, e.g., Allah's saying: 'And do not resolve the marriage contract until the prescribed term reaches its end' (Quran 2:228), and the Prophet's saying: 'There is no marriage except with witnesses.' So the command is established generally. And since the addresses are general, they bind the disbelievers. However, they are not interfered with due to the covenant of dhimmah. But this non-interference is not because we consider their actions correct, but we turn away from them, just as they worship idols and we do not interfere by way of turning away. But when they take their case to a Muslim ruler or embrace Islam while the prohibition exists, then separation becomes necessary. Because Allah says: 'And judge between them by what Allah has revealed, and do not follow their desires' (Quran 5:49). In the verse, the pronoun 'between them' refers to the disbelievers. The translation: 'And you judge between the disbelievers in accordance with what Allah has revealed, and do not follow their desires.' From this verse it is known that the Muslim ruler will judge according to the Shari'ah.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of marriages contracted by disbelievers in a manner that is prohibited in Islam but permissible in their own religion, upon their conversion to Islam. The text begins by stating the case: a disbeliever marries without witnesses or during the 'iddah of a disbeliever, both of which are prohibited in Islam but allowed in their religion. If both then embrace Islam, is the marriage valid? Three positions are presented: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the marriage remains valid and the couple is left on it. Imam Zufar holds that the marriage is invalid (fasid) in both cases, but before they become Muslims or take the case to a Muslim judge, the Muslim authorities do not interfere due to the dhimmah covenant. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) distinguish: for marriage without witnesses, they agree with Abu Hanifa; for marriage during 'iddah, they agree with Zufar. Each gives evidence: Zufar argues that the general addresses of the Shari'ah (Quran and Hadith) apply to disbelievers as well, so the prohibition is binding. The Sahibayn argue that the prohibition of marriage during 'iddah is agreed upon by all, so disbelievers are committed to it, but the prohibition of marriage without witnesses is disputed among Muslim scholars, and disbelievers are not committed to all our differences. Abu Hanifa argues that prohibitions cannot be imposed on disbelievers as religious obligations because they are not addressed by the Shari'ah as such. Moreover, making 'iddah obligatory as a right of the husband would be futile since the disbeliever husband does not believe in it. The commentary then elaborates on the principles: (1) marriages valid between Muslims are also valid between disbelievers; (2) marriages void due to missing conditions have two categories depending on whether the disbelievers consider them prohibited; (3) marriages void due to the object being inherently prohibited (like incest) are invalid despite their belief. The passage concludes with Zufar's argument about the general nature of the Quranic command to judge by what Allah has revealed, implying that a Muslim judge must apply Islamic law when the case is brought before him. This passage is from the Hidayah commentary and reflects the relied-upon positions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مشرک (mushrik): One who associates partners with Allah; includes all disbelievers in this context.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying.
شهود (shuhood): Witnesses required for a valid marriage contract.
ذمہ (dhimmah): Covenant of protection granted to non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the marriage of a disbeliever who married without witnesses (permissible in his religion) and then both embrace Islam?
A) The marriage is invalid and must be renewed.
B) The marriage remains valid and the couple is left on it.
C) The marriage is valid but must be repeated with witnesses.
D) The marriage is suspended until a Muslim ruler judges the case.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's position that marriages of disbelievers are confirmed upon Islam unless the prohibition is agreed upon by all schools and the disbelievers themselves consider it prohibited.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
15 min
Validity of Pre-Islamic Marriages: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of pre-Islamic marriages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar on marriages of disbelievers without witnesses or during 'iddah, and apply the distinction between agreed and disputed rulings.

Core Idea
A marriage of disbelievers may be valid upon Islam depending on whether the prohibition is agreed upon or disputed — and whether they are addressed by Shari'ah.

This passage examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of marriages contracted by disbelievers before embracing Islam. The specific case involves two scenarios: marriage without witnesses and marriage during the 'iddah of another man. Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Zufar, and the two companions (Sahibayn) each present proofs based on Quran, Hadith, and usul principles. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school handles the legal capacity of disbelievers (khitab al-kuffar) and the effect of agreed versus disputed rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios and the three positions
State the two contested marriages: (1) without witnesses, (2) during 'iddah. Then list the positions: Abu Hanifa says both valid; Zufar says both invalid; Sahibayn say first valid, second invalid.
Memorize the positions before analyzing proofs.
2
Understand the three general principles
Review the three principles at the start of the chapter: (1) marriages valid between Muslims are valid between disbelievers; (2) marriages invalid due to missing conditions have two subcases based on whether disbelievers consider it prohibited; (3) marriages with permanent prohibitions (e.g., sister) are valid per their belief.
These principles set the foundation for the dispute.
3
Analyze the proofs of each imam
Zufar uses general addresses (Quran 2:235, hadith 'la nikah illa bi shuhud') to argue all Muslims are bound, but non-interference due to dhimma. Sahibayn distinguish between agreed (muttifaq 'alayh) and disputed (mukhtalaf fih) rulings. Abu Hanifa argues that prohibition of 'iddah marriage cannot be established as a right of the Lawgiver or the husband, so it is not binding on kuffar.
Trace the dalil for each position.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a couple embraces Islam, under Abu Hanifa they remain married in both cases. Under Sahibayn, they remain married in the witnesses case but separate in the 'iddah case. Under Zufar, they separate in both.
This shows the real impact of the ikhtilaf.
5
Apply the distinction between agreed and disputed rulings
Use the Sahibayn's criterion: if a ruling is agreed upon by all schools, it binds the protected disbelievers (ahl al-dhimma); if disputed, they follow their own madhhab. Apply this to other similar scenarios.
This is a key Hanafi principle in fiqh al-akalliyyat.

کتاب النکاح
اور جب نکاح صحیح ہو گیا تو مرافعہ اور اسلام کی حالت بقائے نکاح کی حالت ہے۔ اور شہادت حالت بقاء میں شرط نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی عدت حالت بقاء کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ جیسے منکوحہ جبکہ شبہ کے ساتھ وطی کی گئی۔
تشریح مشرک وہ ہے جو خداوند تعالیٰ کے ساتھ کسی کو شریک بنائے جیسے نصرانی بت پرست بشر طیکہ خدا کا اقرار کرتا ہوں۔ لیکن یہاں اہل شرک سے مطلقاً کا فرمراد ہے جو مشرک اور منکر خدا سب کو شامل ہے۔ نکاح اہل شرک کو نکاح رقیق کے بعد بیان کیا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ مشرک مرتبہ میں رقیق سے ادون اور اخس ہے۔ حق جل مجدہ کا ارشاد ہے ولعبد مؤمن خير من مشرک
اس باب کے مسائل تین اصول پر مبنی ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ جو نکاح دو مسلمانوں کے درمیان صحیح ہوتا ہے وہ دو کافروں میں بھی صحیح ہوگا۔ اسی معنی میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول وارد ہے ولدت من نکاح لامن سفاح یعنی میں نکاح سے پیدا ہوا ہوں نہ کہ زنا سے۔ دوسرا اصول یہ ہے کہ جو نکاح دو مسلمانوں میں شرط وغیرہ فوت ہونے سے فاسد یا باطل ہو جاتا ہے کافروں میں اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ کفار بھی اس کو ممنوع سمجھتے ہیں تو وہ ممنوع ہوگا ۔ اور اگر کفار اس کو جائز سمجھتے ہیں تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کافروں کے حق میں نکاح ہو گا حتی کہ اگر دونوں مسلمان ہو گئے تو اسی نکاح پر باقی رکھے جائیں گے۔ تیسرا اصول یہ کہ جو نکاح محل حرام ہونے کی وجہ سے حرام ہو مثلاً بہن وغیرہ کے ساتھ نکاح کیا تو وہ ان کے اعتقاد پر جائز واقع ہوگا۔ اور مشائخ عراق کے قول پر فاسد ہوگا۔
صورت مسئلہ
ایک کافر نے کسی کافر عورت سے بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح کیا یا کسی کا فر کی عدت میں تھی اس سے نکاح کیا اور یہ ان کے دین میں جاڑ بھی ہے۔ پھر دونوں مسلمان ہو گئے تو اس بارے میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ دونوں کو سابقہ مذہب پر باقی رکھا جائے گا اور امام زور نے فرمایا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں نکاح فاسد ہے۔ البتہ ان کے ساتھ تعرض نہیں کریں گے یہاں تک کہ وہ مسلمان ہو جائیں یا مسلمان عادل حاکم کے پاس مرافعہ کریں۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ پہلی صورت یعنی نکاح بغیر شہود میں وہ حکم ہے جو امام صاحب نے فرمایا اور دوسری صورت یعنی کافر کی معتدہ سے نکاح کرنے کی صورت میں وہ حکم ہے جو امام زفر نے فرمایا ۔
امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خطابات شرع عام ہیں، مثلاً باری تعالیٰ کا قول و لا تـعـزمـوا عـقــدة النكاح حتى يبلغ الكتاب اجلہ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول لا نكاح الا بشهود یعنی تم تعلق نکاح کا ارادہ بھی مت کرو یہاں تک کہ عدت مقررہ اپنی ختم کو پہنچ جائے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح نہیں ہوتا ہے ) لہذا حکم بھی علی العموم ثابت ہوگا اور چونکہ خطابات عام ہیں اسلئے وہ کافروں کو بھی لا زم ہوں گے۔ البتہ کفار کے ساتھ تعرض نہیں کریں گے۔ اسلئے کہ ان کے ساتھ تعرض نہ کرنے کا عقد ذمہ کر رکھا ہے۔ لیکن یہ تعرض نہ کرنا اسلئے نہیں کہ ہم ان کے ان افعال کو درست سمجھتے ہیں بلکہ ان سے اعراض کرتے ہوئے ان کے ساتھ تعرض نہیں کیا جائے گا جیسا کہ وہ بت پرستی کرتے ہیں اور ہم بطور اعراض کے ان سے تعرض نہیں کرتے۔ البتہ جب وہ اپنا معاملہ مسلمان حاکم کے پاس لے گئے یا اسلام قبول کر لیا درانحالیکہ حرمت نکاح بھی موجود ہے تو اب تفریق لازم ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے و ان احكم بينهم بما انزل الله ولا تتبع اهوائهم آیت میں بینھم کی ضمیر کفار کی طرف راجع ہے ترجمہ ہوگا اور تو فیصلہ کر کفار کے درمیان اس کے مطابق جو اللہ نے اتارا اور ان کی خواہشات کا اتباع مت کر اس آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مسلمان حاکم شریعت کے مطابق فیصلہ دے گا۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معتدة الغیر کے نکاح کی حرمت متفق علیہ ہے اور نکاح بغیر شہود کی حرمت مختلف فیہ ہے۔ کیونکہ امام مالک اور ابن ابی لیلی نکاح بغیر شہود کے جواز کے قائل ہیں۔ اور کفار اہل ذمہ نے ہمارے متفق علیہ احکام کا التزام تو کیا ہے لیکن مختلف فیہ احکام کا التزام نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس معتدۃ الغیر کے نکاح کی حرمت چونکہ متفق علیہ ہے۔ اسلئے کفار اہل ذمہ اس حکم میں مسلمانوں کے تابع ہیں اور چونکہ متعدۃ الغیر کے ساتھ اہل اسلام کا نکاح فاسد ہے۔ اسلئے کا فراہل ذمہ کا نکاح بھی فاسد ہو گا۔ اور مسلمان ہونے یا مرافعہ کے بعد واجب التفریق ہوگا ۔ اور نکاح بغیر شہود کی حرمت چونکہ مختلف فیہ ہے اسلئے کفار اہل ذمہ اس حکم میں مسلمانوں کے تابع نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ ان کے مذہب کے مطابق معتدة الغیر کے ساتھ نکاح درست ہو گا ۔ اور اسلام قبول کر لینے کے بعد اسی سابقہ نکاح پر باقی رکھا جائے گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عدت کی وجہ سے حرمت نکاح شارع کا حق بن کر ثابت ہوگی ۔ یا زوجہ کا حق بن کر ۔ اور یہ دونوں صورتیں ممکن نہیں ہیں شارع کا حق بنا کر ثابت کرنا تو اسلئے ممکن نہیں کہ کفار حقوق شرع کے مخاطب نہیں ہیں اور شوہر کے حق کی بنا پر عدت واجب کرنا اسلئے ممکن نہیں کہ شوہر وجوب عدت کا اعتقاد ہی نہیں رکھتا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر کوئی ذمیہ کتابیہ کسی مسلمان کے نکاح میں تھی پھر مسلمان نے اسکو طلاق دیدی تو اس کتابیہ پر شوہر کاحق بن کر عدت واجب ہوگی اسلئے کہ مسلمان وجوب عدت کا معتقد ہے لہذا عدت میں اس کتابیہ کا نکاح درست نہیں ہوگا۔ ہیں جب عدت کی وجہ سے حرمت نکاح کو ثابت کرنے کی دوصور تیں تھیں اور یہ دونوں ممکن نہیں تو ایک کافر کا نکاح دوسرے کافر کی معتدہ سے صحیح ہو گا۔ اور جب نکاح صحیح ہو گیا تو حالت مرافعہ اور اسلام قبول کرنے کی حالت ، حالت بقاء ہے ۔ اور حالت بقاء میں شہادت شرط نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر نکاح کے بعد گواہ مر گئے تو نکاح باطل نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اسی طرح عدت حالت بقاء کے منافی نہیں ہے مثلاً کسی شخص کی منکوحہ سے یہ سمجھ کر نکاح کر لیا کہ اسکا شوہر مر گیا ہے اور ولی بھی کر لی گئی ہے اسکے بعد معلوم ہوا کہ وہ زندہ ہے تو نکاح اول کے باقی رہنے کے باوجود عدت واجب ہو گی۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ عدت بقاء نکاح کے منافی نہیں ہے۔
Book of Marriage. And when marriage is valid, the state of litigation and Islam is a state of continuation of marriage. And testimony is not a condition in the state of continuation, and similarly the waiting period ('iddah) does not contradict the state of continuation. Like a married woman when intercourse occurs with doubt. Explanation: A polytheist is one who associates partners with Allah Almighty, like a Christian idolater who affirms God. But here 'people of shirk' generally means disbeliever, which includes polytheist and denier of God alike. The marriage of polytheists is mentioned after the marriage of slaves because the polytheist is lower and inferior in rank to the slave. Allah Most High says: 'And a believing slave is better than a polytheist.' The issues of this chapter are based on three principles. First: Any marriage that is valid between two Muslims will also be valid between two disbelievers. In this meaning, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I was born from marriage, not from fornication.' Second: A marriage that becomes invalid or void between two Muslims due to a condition being lost has two forms among disbelievers: one is that the disbelievers also consider it prohibited, so it will be prohibited; and if the disbelievers consider it permissible, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is a valid marriage for them, so that if they both become Muslim, they will be left upon that marriage. Third: A marriage that is prohibited due to the woman being a prohibited degree (e.g., sister) will be valid according to their belief, and according to the scholars of Iraq, it will be irregular. Case: A disbeliever married a disbeliever woman without witnesses, or married a woman who was in the waiting period of a disbeliever, and this is permissible in their religion. Then both become Muslim. Regarding this, Imam Abu Hanifa's doctrine is that both will be left upon their previous marriage; Imam Zufar said that in both cases the marriage is irregular, but they will not be interfered with until they become Muslim or take the matter to a Muslim just ruler. The two companions said that in the first case (marriage without witnesses) the ruling is what Imam Sahib said, and in the second case (marriage to a woman in 'iddah) the ruling is what Imam Zufar said. Imam Zufar's proof: The addresses of the Sacred Law are general, e.g., Allah's word 'And do not resolve upon a marriage contract until the prescribed term reaches its end' and the Prophet's saying 'No marriage except with witnesses.' Therefore the ruling is established generally, and since the addresses are general, they are binding on disbelievers. However, they will not be interfered with because the covenant of protection (dhimma) prevents interference. But this non-interference is not because we consider their actions correct, but we turn away from them, just as they worship idols and we do not interfere. However, when they bring their affair to a Muslim ruler or accept Islam while the prohibition of marriage is present, then separation becomes necessary. Because Allah says: 'And judge between them by what Allah has revealed and do not follow their desires.' The pronoun 'between them' refers to the disbelievers. This verse indicates that the Muslim ruler will judge according to the Sacred Law. The two companions' proof: The prohibition of marriage with a woman in another's waiting period is agreed upon, while the prohibition of marriage without witnesses is disputed. Because Imam Malik and Ibn Abi Layla permit marriage without witnesses. The protected disbelievers (ahl al-dhimma) have undertaken our agreed-upon rulings but not the disputed ones. So since the prohibition of marriage with a woman in another's waiting period is agreed upon, the protected disbelievers are subject to Muslims in this ruling, and since the marriage of Muslims with such a woman is irregular, the marriage of the protected disbelievers is also irregular. And after becoming Muslim or litigation, separation is obligatory. As for marriage without witnesses, since its prohibition is disputed, the protected disbelievers are not subject to Muslims in this ruling; rather, according to their own madhhab, the marriage will be valid. And after accepting Islam, they will be left upon that previous marriage. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: The prohibition of marriage due to 'iddah is established either as a right of the Lawgiver or as a right of the wife. Both are impossible: Establishing it as a right of the Lawgiver is impossible because disbelievers are not addressed by the rights of the Sacred Law; establishing it as a right of the husband is impossible because the husband does not believe in the obligation of 'iddah. Conversely, if a Jewish or Christian woman was married to a Muslim and he divorced her, then 'iddah will be obligatory upon her as a right of the husband because the Muslim believes in the obligation of 'iddah, so her marriage during 'iddah is not valid. Therefore, since there were two ways to establish the prohibition of marriage due to 'iddah, and both are impossible, the marriage of a disbeliever to another disbeliever's woman in 'iddah is valid. And when the marriage is valid, the state of litigation and conversion to Islam is a state of continuation. And in the state of continuation, testimony is not a condition. This is why if witnesses die after marriage, the marriage does not become invalid. Similarly, 'iddah does not contradict the state of continuation. For example, someone marries a married woman thinking her husband died, and consummates, then learns he is alive; so even though the first marriage remains, 'iddah is obligatory. Thus it is established that 'iddah does not contradict the continuation of marriage.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of marriages contracted by disbelievers when they later embrace Islam. The author begins by clarifying that 'mushrik' here includes all disbelievers. The discussion follows three principles laid out at the start of the chapter: (1) marriages valid between Muslims are also valid between disbelievers; (2) marriages that are invalid or void due to missing conditions (like witnesses) have two sub-cases depending on whether the disbelievers themselves consider the act prohibited or permissible; (3) marriages with permanent prohibitions (like sister) are valid in their belief but irregular according to the Mashayikh of Iraq. The specific case involves two scenarios: a marriage without witnesses and a marriage during the 'iddah of a disbeliever. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that both marriages are valid and continue upon conversion. Imam Zufar holds that both are irregular (fasid) and must be separated after conversion or litigation. The Sahibayn differentiate: they follow Abu Hanifa on the witnesses case (since it's disputed among Muslims, disbelievers are not bound), but follow Zufar on the 'iddah case (since its prohibition is agreed upon, disbelievers are bound). The passage then provides each imam's proof. Imam Zufar uses general addresses (Khitabat al-Shar' 'amma) from Quran and Hadith, but adds that disbelievers are not interfered with due to the dhimma covenant. The Sahibayn base their view on the distinction between agreed-upon and disputed rulings. Imam Abu Hanifa uses a sophisticated argument: prohibition due to 'iddah cannot be established as a right of the Lawgiver (because disbelievers are not addressed) nor as the husband's right (because he doesn't believe in 'iddah), so the marriage is valid. He also argues that 'iddah does not contradict the continuation of marriage with a parallel case of a woman unknowingly married to a living husband. The passage thus demonstrates a classic Hanafi usul process: principles of general applicability, addressing of disbelievers (khitab al-kuffar), and the effect of differing schools within Madhhab.

Key Terms
مرافعہ (murafa'ah): Litigation or taking a case to a Muslim judge.
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarriage.
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony or witnesses present at marriage contract.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is a marriage contracted during the 'iddah of a disbeliever considered irregular when they embrace Islam, while a marriage without witnesses is upheld?
A) Because the prohibition of marriage during 'iddah is agreed upon among all Muslim schools, while the prohibition without witnesses is disputed.
B) Because witnesses are only a condition for initiation, not continuation.
C) Because disbelievers are not bound by any Shari'ah rulings.
D) Because the Sahibayn consider all marriages of kuffar invalid.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a marriage contracted by disbelievers upon embracing Islam depends on whether the prohibition is agreed upon (muttifaq 'alayh) or disputed (mukhtalaf fih) among Muslim schools, and whether the condition is only required at inception or for continuation.

Ruling on Majusi Marrying Mother or Daughter
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahram marriage validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the validity of a marriage between a Majusi and his mahram, and state the practical outcome after conversion.

Core Idea
Even if a marriage is valid among disbelievers, permanent mahram prohibitions require separation upon conversion.

This passage examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the status of marriages contracted by Majus with their mahram (e.g., mother, daughter). While all Hanafi imams agree that separation is required after conversion, they differ on whether the marriage was valid from the start. This distinction reveals a deeper usul principle about how Islamic law interacts with pre-existing contracts of non-Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling
Both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree that after conversion to Islam, the couple must be separated (farq baynahuma). This is the practical outcome.
The consensus (ijma) on separation is noted in the passage.
2
Locate the point of disagreement
The dispute is about the status of the marriage before conversion: Was it valid or invalid from the outset?
Abu Hanifa holds it was valid; Sahibayn hold it was invalid.
3
Analyze the reasoning of each side
Sahibayn argue by analogy with 'iddah: since the prohibition of mahram is absolute and agreed upon, it binds the disbelievers too, making the marriage invalid. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: the prohibition is not applied to their contracts before Islam; rather, it only takes effect upon conversion.
The distinction between temporary ('iddah) and permanent (mahram) prohibitions is key.
4
Apply the usul principle
This dispute revolves around whether the Shari'ah rulings regarding prohibitions are retroactively applied to pre-Islamic contracts. Abu Hanifa argues they are not, but they prevent continuation after conversion.
This is an example of the maxim: 'Islam does not invalidate past actions but prevents future continuation.'
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that for Sahibayn the marriage was never valid, so the couple were in sin; for Abu Hanifa they were not sinning until after conversion, when they must separate.
Both end with separation, but the moral and legal history differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا تزوج المجوسى امه او ابنته ثم اسلما فرق بينهما لان نكاح المحارم له حكم البطلان فيما بينهم عندهما كما ذكرنا فى المعتدة ووجب التعرض بالاسلام فيفرق و عنده له حكم الصحة في الصحيح الا ان المحرمية تنافى بقاء النكاح فيفرق بخلاف العدة لانها لا تنافيه
ترجمہ ۔ پس جب مجوسی نے اپنی ماں یا اپنی بیٹی سے نکاح کیا پھر دونوں مسلمان ہو گئے تو دونوں میں تفریق کر دی جائے گی ( بالا جماع) کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک محرمات ابدیہ کا نکاح خود کفار کے درمیان باطل ہونے کا حکم رکھتا ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے معدہ میں ذکر کیا۔ اور اسلام لانے کی وجہ سے تعرض کرنا واجب ہو گیا ( تو حاکم دونوں میں ) تفریق کر دے گا۔ اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک نکاح محارم کیلئے صحت کا حکم ہے۔ صحیح قول میں مگر محرمیت بقاء نکاح کے منافی ہے تو تفریق کر دی جائے گی۔ بخلاف عدت کے کیونکہ وہ بقاء نکاح کے منافی نہیں ہے۔
So when a Majusi marries his mother or his daughter, then both embrace Islam, they are separated (by consensus). Because according to the two companions (Sahibayn), the marriage of permanently prohibited relatives has the ruling of invalidity among them (the disbelievers) as we mentioned in the case of 'iddah, and interference becomes obligatory upon Islam, so he separates them. And according to him (Imam Abu Hanifa), it has the ruling of validity in the correct view, except that prohibition by kinship contradicts the continuation of marriage, so he separates them. Unlike 'iddah, because it does not contradict continuation. Translation: So when a Majusi marries his mother or his daughter, then both become Muslim, they are separated (by consensus). Because in the view of the Sahibayn, the marriage of permanently prohibited relatives has the ruling of invalidity even among the disbelievers, as we mentioned in the case of 'iddah. And due to Islam, interference becomes obligatory, so the judge separates them. And in the view of Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa), the marriage of prohibited relatives has the ruling of validity in the correct view, except that kinship prohibition contradicts the continuation of marriage, so they are separated. Unlike 'iddah, because it does not contradict continuation.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of a marriage between a Majusi (fire worshiper) and his mother or daughter, and the effect of their conversion to Islam. The ruling is that they must be separated (farq baynahuma) by consensus, but the reasoning differs. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), such marriages are inherently invalid even among disbelievers because the prohibition is agreed upon (like the 'iddah case), so when they convert, the judge interferes and separates them. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the marriage is actually valid in principle among disbelievers (since they consider it permissible), but once they embrace Islam, the prohibition of kinship (muhrimiyyah) is a permanent impediment that contradicts the continuation of the marriage. Therefore, separation is necessary. He contrasts this with the 'iddah case where the prohibition is temporary and does not contradict continuation, so the marriage remains valid. The passage shows the third principle mentioned earlier: marriage with a woman who is permanently prohibited (like mother or sister) is considered valid by Imam Abu Hanifa in their belief, but after conversion, the permanent prohibition requires separation. The consensus on separation is due to the irremovable nature of the mahram relationship in Islam.

Key Terms
مجوسی (Majusi): A fire worshiper, Zoroastrian, considered a non-Muslim but with special rulings different from idolaters.
محارم (mahram): Permanently prohibited relatives for marriage (e.g., mother, daughter, sister).
محرمیت (muhrimiyyah): The state of being a prohibited relative; an impediment to marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical outcome when a Majusi man who married his mother converts to Islam along with his wife?
A) They remain married because the marriage was valid among the Majus.
B) They are separated by consensus, regardless of the pre-conversion validity dispute.
C) They are separated only according to the Sahibayn, but not according to Abu Hanifa.
D) They are separated only if they converted in front of a judge.

Key Takeaway
When a non-Muslim couple with a permanent mahram relationship converts to Islam, the marriage must be annulled because the permanent prohibition contradicts continuation, even if the marriage was valid under their previous law.

Marriage of a Dhimmi to a Woman in Iddah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dhimmi marriage during iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn regarding the validity of a dhimmi's marriage to a woman in iddah, and apply the principle that dhimmis are bound only by agreed-upon shar'i rulings.

Core Idea
Dhimmis are subject to agreed-upon rulings, not disputed ones—determining the prohibition's nature decides validity.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a dhimmi man can validly marry a woman who is in the iddah of another dhimmi. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ on the basis of how shar'i prohibitions apply to non-Muslims. The resolution hinges on whether the prohibition is a right of Allah or a right of the husband, and whether dhimmis are addressed by such rights. You will dissect their arguments and understand the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Clearly state the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the validity of a dhimmi's marriage to a woman in iddah. Note that Abu Hanifa considers it valid (sahih), while the Sahibayn consider it invalid (fasid).
The dispute is about the marriage of two dhimmis, not involving a Muslim.
2
Identify the opposing proof of Sahibayn
Explain the Sahibayn's argument: the prohibition of marrying a woman in iddah of another is unanimously agreed upon (muttadaq 'alayh) among Muslims. Since dhimmis have committed to following our agreed-upon rulings, they are bound by this prohibition. Therefore, the marriage is invalid.
Sahibayn contrast this with the disputed ruling on marriage without witnesses, which dhimmis are not bound by.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Imam Abu Hanifa deconstructs the prohibition into two possible bases: a right of the Lawgiver (haqq al-shar') or a right of the husband (haqq al-zawj). He argues that neither can apply to dhimmis: they are not addressed by shar'i rights, and the dhimmi husband does not believe in iddah. Hence, no prohibition exists, and the marriage is valid.
This is a rational (aqli) argument, not based on textual evidence directly.
4
Explore the exception
Note the exception: if the woman was previously married to a Muslim who divorced her, then iddah becomes obligatory due to the Muslim husband's belief, and marriage during that iddah is invalid even for a dhimmi. This shows that the right of the husband is recognized when the husband believes in iddah.
This exception confirms Abu Hanifa's principle that the husband's belief is relevant.
5
Determine the practical difference
If a dhimmi marries a woman in iddah and then both convert to Islam, according to Abu Hanifa the marriage remains valid, while according to Sahibayn it is invalid and must be separated. This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
Later Hanafi fatwa often follows Abu Hanifa on such matters.

صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معتدة الغیر کے نکاح کی حرمت متفق علیہ ہے اور نکاح بغیر شہود کی حرمت مختلف فیہ ہے۔ کیونکہ امام مالک اور ابن ابی لیلی نکاح بغیر شہود کے جواز کے قائل ہیں۔ اور کفار اہل ذمہ نے ہمارے متفق علیہ احکام کا التزام تو کیا ہے لیکن مختلف فیہ احکام کا التزام نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس معتدۃ الغیر کے نکاح کی حرمت چونکہ متفق علیہ ہے۔ اسلئے کفار اہل ذمہ اس حکم میں مسلمانوں کے تابع ہیں اور چونکہ متعدۃ الغیر کے ساتھ اہل اسلام کا نکاح فاسد ہے۔ اسلئے کا فراہل ذمہ کا نکاح بھی فاسد ہو گا۔ اور مسلمان ہونے یا مرافعہ کے بعد واجب التفریق ہوگا ۔ اور نکاح بغیر شہود کی حرمت چونکہ مختلف فیہ ہے اسلئے کفار اہل ذمہ اس حکم میں مسلمانوں کے تابع نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ ان کے مذہب کے مطابق معتدة الغیر کے ساتھ نکاح درست ہو گا ۔ اور اسلام قبول کر لینے کے بعد اسی سابقہ نکاح پر باقی رکھا جائے گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عدت کی وجہ سے حرمت نکاح شارع کا حق بن کر ثابت ہوگی ۔ یا زوجہ کا حق بن کر ۔ اور یہ دونوں صورتیں ممکن نہیں ہیں شارع کا حق بنا کر ثابت کرنا تو اسلئے ممکن نہیں کہ کفار حقوق شرع کے مخاطب نہیں ہیں اور شوہر کے حق کی بنا پر عدت واجب کرنا اسلئے ممکن نہیں کہ شوہر وجوب عدت کا اعتقاد ہی نہیں رکھتا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر کوئی ذمیہ کتابیہ کسی مسلمان کے نکاح میں تھی پھر مسلمان نے اسکو طلاق دیدی تو اس کتابیہ پر شوہر کاحق بن کر عدت واجب ہوگی اسلئے کہ مسلمان وجوب عدت کا معتقد ہے لہذا عدت میں اس کتابیہ کا نکاح درست نہیں ہوگا۔ ہیں جب عدت کی وجہ سے حرمت نکاح کو ثابت کرنے کی دوصور تیں تھیں اور یہ دونوں ممکن نہیں تو ایک کافر کا نکاح دوسرے کافر کی معتدہ سے صحیح ہو گا۔ اور جب نکاح صحیح ہو گیا تو حالت مرافعہ اور اسلام قبول کرنے کی حالت ، حالت بقاء ہے ۔ اور حالت بقاء میں شہادت شرط نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر نکاح کے بعد گواہ مر گئے تو نکاح باطل نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اسی طرح عدت حالت بقاء کے منافی نہیں ہے مثلاً کسی شخص کی منکوحہ سے یہ سمجھ کر نکاح کر لیا کہ اسکا شوہر مر گیا ہے اور ولی بھی کر لی گئی ہے اسکے بعد معلوم ہوا کہ وہ زندہ ہے تو نکاح اول کے باقی رہنے کے باوجود عدت واجب ہو گی۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ عدت بقاء نکاح کے منافی نہیں ہے۔
The evidence of the two companions (Sahibayn) is that the prohibition of marriage with a woman in iddah of another is unanimously agreed upon, while the prohibition of marriage without witnesses is disputed. Because Imam Malik and Ibn Abi Layla believe in the permissibility of marriage without witnesses. And the dhimmi disbelievers have committed to our agreed-upon rulings but not to disputed rulings. So since the prohibition of marriage with a woman in iddah of another is agreed upon, therefore dhimmi disbelievers are subject to Muslims in this ruling, and since the marriage of Muslims with a woman in iddah of another is invalid, therefore the marriage of dhimmi is also invalid. And upon becoming Muslim or after litigation, separation becomes obligatory. And since the prohibition of marriage without witnesses is disputed, therefore dhimmi disbelievers are not subject to Muslims in this ruling; rather, according to their own school, marriage with a woman in iddah of another is valid. And after accepting Islam, they will be kept on that previous marriage. The evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the prohibition of marriage due to iddah is established as a right of the Lawgiver or as a right of the husband. And both possibilities are not possible. Establishing it as a right of the Lawgiver is not possible because disbelievers are not addressed by shar'i rights. And making iddah obligatory based on the husband's right is not possible because the husband does not believe in the obligation of iddah. In contrast, if a dhimmi kitabiyya was in the marriage of a Muslim, then the Muslim divorced her, then iddah becomes obligatory upon that kitabiyya based on the husband's right because the Muslim believes in the obligation of iddah; therefore, marriage of this kitabiyya during iddah is not valid. So, when there were two possibilities to establish the prohibition of marriage due to iddah, and both are not possible, then a disbeliever's marriage to another disbeliever's woman in iddah is valid. And when the marriage is valid, then the state of litigation and the state of accepting Islam are states of survival. And in the state of survival, witnesses are not a condition. This is why if witnesses died after marriage, the marriage does not become invalid. And similarly, iddah is not contrary to the state of survival; for example, if a person married a married woman thinking that her husband had died and she had completed her iddah, then it became known that he is alive, then despite the first marriage remaining, iddah becomes obligatory. So it is established that iddah is not contrary to the survival of marriage.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the validity of a dhimmi's marriage to a woman who is in the iddah of another man. The Sahibayn argue that since the prohibition of marrying a woman in iddah of another is unanimously agreed upon (muttadaq 'alayh) among Muslims, dhimmi are bound by this ruling. Therefore, their marriage is invalid (fasid) and must be separated upon conversion or litigation. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees, reasoning that the prohibition of marriage during iddah is either a right of the Lawgiver (haqq al-shar') or a right of the husband (haqq al-zawj). It cannot be a right of the Lawgiver because kuffar are not addressed by shar'i obligations (they are not mukallaf with respect to Islamic legal rights). It cannot be a right of the husband because the dhimmi husband does not believe in the obligation of iddah. Therefore, the prohibition cannot be established, and the marriage is valid. However, if the wife was previously married to a Muslim who divorced her, then iddah becomes obligatory due to the Muslim husband's right, and the marriage would be invalid. The text also notes that the dispute about marriage without witnesses (shuhud) is different because that is a disputed prohibition, so dhimmi are not bound by it. The conclusion is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a dhimmi's marriage to a woman in iddah (of another dhimmi) is valid, but according to Sahibayn it is invalid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated in this passage, but in the Hanafi school, the position of Imam Abu Hanifa is often preferred in such matters of 'shar'i rights' regarding non-Muslims.

Key Terms
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman who is in the waiting period (iddah) after divorce or death of her husband.
ذمی (dhimmī): A non-Muslim living under the protection of an Islamic state, bound by the contract of dhimma.
حرمت نکاح (ḥurmat al-nikāḥ): The prohibition of marriage due to a specific cause, such as iddah or consanguinity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis of the Sahibayn's argument that a dhimmi's marriage to a woman in iddah is invalid?
A) The prohibition is unanimously agreed upon, so dhimmis are bound.
B) Dhimmis are not bound by any Islamic laws.
C) The dhimmi husband does not believe in iddah.
D) The woman's iddah is from a Muslim husband.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a dhimmi's marriage during iddah depends on whether the prohibition is a unanimously agreed shar'i right; Imam Abu Hanifa argues it is not applicable to dhimmis.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Magian Marriage to Mahram and Effect of Conversion
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of Magian-mahram marriage and effect of conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the validity of a Magian's marriage to a mahram relative, explain the proof of each side, and apply the ruling to a conversion scenario.

Core Idea
Conversion to Islam dissolves a Magian's marriage to a mahram, even if it was valid before.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a Magian (fire-worshipper) who marries his mother, daughter, or other permanently prohibited relative (mahram abadi). The central question: Is such a marriage valid among non-Muslims, and what happens when both spouses convert to Islam? Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree on the original validity, but all agree that upon conversion, the marriage must be dissolved. Understanding the proof structure and the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is key to mastering this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the disputed issue
Read the passage carefully. The case is a Magian who married his mother/daughter (mahram). Both then become Muslim. The dispute is whether such a marriage was valid before conversion (from a Hanafi perspective).
The dispute is only within the Hanafi school; other schools uniformly deem such marriages invalid.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the marriage was originally valid. His evidence: Kuffar are not addressed by shar'i rights (khitab al-shar') because they reject the Messenger. Therefore, the prohibition of marrying mahram, which is a shar'i right, does not apply to them. The contract of dhimma only obligates them to worldly transactions, not matters of worship.
This is based on the principle that kuffar are not mukallaf with regard to furu' (details) of shari'ah.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn hold that the marriage was invalid even before conversion. Their evidence: The prohibition of marrying mahram is established by ijma' (consensus) among Muslims, and dhimmis are bound by such universally agreed rulings. Therefore, the marriage is invalid from the start, and the Islamic judge would have the right to separate them if they had become Muslim earlier, but conversion triggered that intervention.
The Sahibayn analogize this to the unanimously prohibited marriage with a woman in iddah of another.
4
Understand why both sides agree on separation after conversion
Despite disagreement on original validity, both views require separation upon conversion. For Imam Abu Hanifa, after conversion the spouses become subject to Islamic law, and mahramiyyat (being within prohibited degrees) is contrary to both the initiation and survival of marriage in Islam. For the Sahibayn, the marriage was already invalid, and conversion simply makes it possible for the judge to intervene and formally separate them.
The common ground is that Islam does not recognize a marriage with a mahram relative.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference lies in the original validity. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the marriage was valid, so children are legitimate and spouses inherit from each other before conversion. According to the Sahibayn, the marriage was invalid, so children are illegitimate and no inheritance rights are established. The text notes that the mashayikh of Iraq preferred the view of invalidity (Sahibayn's view) for fatwa.
This affects situations where the couple converts but had children before conversion.

فاذا تزوج المجوسى امه او ابنته ثم اسلما فرق بينهما لان نكاح المحارم له حكم البطلان فيما بينهم عندهما كما ذكرنا فى المعتدة ووجب التعرض بالاسلام فيفرق و عنده له حكم الصحة في الصحيح الا ان المحرمية تنافى بقاء النكاح فيفرق بخلاف العدة لانها لا تنافيه
ترجمہ ۔ پس جب مجوسی نے اپنی ماں یا اپنی بیٹی سے نکاح کیا پھر دونوں مسلمان ہو گئے تو دونوں میں تفریق کر دی جائے گی ( بالا جماع) کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک محرمات ابدیہ کا نکاح خود کفار کے درمیان باطل ہونے کا حکم رکھتا ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے معدہ میں ذکر کیا۔ اور اسلام لانے کی وجہ سے تعرض کرنا واجب ہو گیا ( تو حاکم دونوں میں ) تفریق کر دے گا۔ اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک نکاح محارم کیلئے صحت کا حکم ہے۔ صحیح قول میں مگر محرمیت بقاء نکاح کے منافی ہے تو تفریق کر دی جائے گی۔ بخلاف عدت کے کیونکہ وہ بقاء نکاح کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صور یہ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی آتش پرست نے اپنی ماں یا بیٹی یا محارم بد یہ میں سے کسی کے ساتھ نکاح کیا پھر دونوں مسلمان

ہو گئے تو اس بارے میں امام صاحب کا قول صحیح یہ ہے کہ یہ نکاح صحیح تھا اور بقول مشائخ عراق کے باطل تھا۔ یہی صاحبین کا قول ہے لیکن اس پر سب متفق ہیں کہ مسلمان ہونے کے بعد دونوں میں تفریق کر دی جائے گی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ محرمات ابدیہ کا نکاح خود کافروں کے درمیان باطل ہونے کا حکم رکھتا ہے۔ جیسے ہم نے معتدۃ الغیر میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ یعنی پہلے مسئلہ میں کہا کہ غیر کی معتدہ کے نکاح کی حرمت متفق علیہ ہے۔ لہذا کفا ر اہل ذمہ بھی اسکا التزام کرنے والے ہوں گے۔ اسی طرح اہل اسلام کا اجماع ہے کہ محارم ابدیہ کا نکاح باطل ہے۔ لہذا اہل ذمہ اسی کے تابع ہوں گے۔ البتہ عقد ذمہ کی وجہ سے ان سے تعرض نہیں ہو سکتا تھا۔ لیکن جب وہ دونوں مسلمان ہو گئے تو اب حکم اسلام میں داخل ہوں گے۔ اور اسلام چونکہ محارم الا بدیہ کے نکاح کے منافی ہے۔ اسلئے اسلام لانے کی وجہ سے تعرض کرنا واجب ہو گیا ۔ پس حاکم دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آتش پرست کا محارم الا بد یہ کے ساتھ نکاح اصل میں تو صحیح تھا۔ اور وجہ صحت وہی ہے جو ماقبل میں گذر چکی که حرمت حق شرع کی وجہ سے ہوگی یا حق زوج کی وجہ سے۔ حق شرع کی وجہ سے تو اسلئے نہیں ہو سکتی کہ کفار حقوق شرع کے مخاطب ہی نہیں ہیں۔ تو گویا خطاب ان کے حق میں اترا ہی نہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ مبلغ کی تکذیب کرتے ہیں اور رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کی رسالت کا انکار کرتے ہیں۔ اور رہی یہ بات کہ ہم کو کفار پر ولایت الزام حاصل ہو یہ اسلئے نہیں ہو سکتا کہ ولایت الزام تلوار کے ذریعہ حاصل ہوتی ہے یا محاجہ کے ذریعہ اور یہ دونوں چیز میں عقد ذمہ کی وجہ سے قطع ہو گئیں۔ لہذا ہم کو ان پر ولایت الزام حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی ۔ بہر حال حق شرع کی وجہ سے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہو گی۔ اور حق زوج کی وجہ سے اسلئے نہیں ہو سکتی کہ زوج آتش پرست اس کی حرمت کا اعتقاد ہی نہیں رکھتا ہے۔ پس ثبوت حرمت کی دو صورتیں تھیں اور دونوں ممکن نہیں اسلئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ابتداء محارم ابد یہ کے ساتھ آتش پرست کا نکاح درست ہے۔ الا ان المحرمة سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ جب امام صاحب کے نزدیک محارم کا نکاح ابتداء صیح ہے تو اسلام لانے کے بعد بھی باقی رہنا چاہئے تفریق کیوں
واجب کی گئی ہے؟ جواب کا فر اسلام لانے کے بعد حقوق شرع کا مخاطب ہو گیا ہے اور شریعت اسلام میں محرمیت جس طرح ابتداء نکاح کے منافی ہے۔ اسی طرح بقاء نکاح کے بھی منافی ہے۔ مثلاً ایک بالغہ عورت نے صغیر کے ساتھ اس کی مدت رضاعت میں نکاح کیا۔ پھر اس عورت نے اسکو دودھ پلا دیا تو یہ اس کا رضاعی بیٹا ہو گیا تو اب اس کے ساتھ تعرض کرنا واجب ہو گا۔ اور حاکم دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا۔ بخلاف عدت کے کیونکہ عدت بقاع نکاح کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے معتدۃ الخیر کے نکاح کو اسلام لانے کے بعد بھی باقی رکھا گیا ہے۔ دونوں میں سے ایک کے اسلام سے تفریق کی جائے گی اور مرافعہ کی صورت میں تفریق نہیں کی جائے گی
ثم باسلام احدهما يفرق بينهما وبمرافعة احدهما لايفرق عنده خلافا لهما والفرق ان استحقاق احدهما لا يبطل بمرافعة صاحبه اذلا يتغيرب اعتقاده اما اعتقاد المصر بالكفر لا يعارض اسلام المسلم لان الاسلام يعلو او لا يعلى ولوترافعا يفرق بالاجماع لان مرافعتهما كتحكيمهما
When a Magian married his mother or his daughter, then both become Muslim, they will be separated. When a Magian married his mother or his daughter, then both became Muslim, they are separated because, according to them (Sahibayn), the marriage of permanently prohibited relatives has the ruling of invalidity among them, as we mentioned in the case of the woman in iddah, and intervention became obligatory due to Islam, so he separates. According to him (Imam Abu Hanifa), it has the ruling of validity in the correct view, but mahramiyyat is contrary to the survival of the marriage, so he separates, unlike iddah because it is not contrary to it. Translation: So when a Magian married his mother or his daughter, then both became Muslim, they will be separated (by consensus) because according to Sahibayn, the marriage of permanently prohibited relatives has the ruling of invalidity among the disbelievers themselves, as we mentioned in the case of the woman in iddah. And due to becoming Muslim, intervention becomes obligatory, so the ruler separates them. And according to Imam Sahib, the marriage of prohibited relatives has the ruling of validity in the correct view, but mahramiyyat is contrary to the survival of the marriage, so they are separated. Unlike iddah, because it is not contrary to the survival of marriage. Explanation: The scenario is that if a fire-worshipper married his mother or daughter or any permanently prohibited relative, then both became Muslim, then regarding this, Imam Sahib's correct view is that this marriage was valid, and according to the scholars of Iraq, it was invalid. That is the view of Sahibayn, but all agree that after becoming Muslim, they will be separated. The evidence of Sahibayn is that the marriage of permanently prohibited relatives has the ruling of invalidity among the disbelievers themselves. As we mentioned in the case of the woman in iddah. That is, in the previous issue, it was said that the prohibition of marrying a woman in iddah of another is unanimously agreed upon. Therefore, dhimmi disbelievers will also be bound by it. Similarly, there is consensus of Ahl al-Islam that marriage with permanently prohibited relatives is invalid. Therefore, dhimmis will be subject to it. However, due to the contract of dhimma, they could not be interfered with. But when they both became Muslim, they now enter into the rulings of Islam. And since Islam is contrary to the marriage of permanently prohibited relatives, therefore intervention becomes obligatory due to becoming Muslim. So the ruler separates them. The evidence of Imam Sahib is that the fire-worshipper's marriage with permanently prohibited relatives was originally valid. And the reason for validity is the same as passed earlier: that the prohibition would be due to a right of the Lawgiver or a right of the husband. Due to the right of the Lawgiver, it cannot be because disbelievers are not addressed by shar'i rights. So it is as if the address did not come down for them. Because they deny the messenger and reject the prophethood of the Messenger of Allah. And as for the idea that we have the authority of compulsion over disbelievers, this cannot be because the authority of compulsion is obtained through the sword or through argument, and both of these are cut off due to the contract of dhimma. Therefore, we cannot have the authority of compulsion over them. In any case, the prohibition is not established due to the right of the Lawgiver. And due to the right of the husband, it cannot be because the fire-worshipper husband does not believe in its prohibition. So there were two possibilities for establishing prohibition, and both are not possible, therefore we say that initially the marriage of a fire-worshipper with permanently prohibited relatives is valid. But the question arises: when according to Imam Sahib the marriage of prohibited relatives is initially valid, why is separation made obligatory after becoming Muslim? The answer: After becoming Muslim, he becomes addressed by shar'i rights, and in the Shari'ah of Islam, mahramiyyat is contrary to the initiation of marriage as well as to the survival of marriage. For example, a mature woman married a minor during his breastfeeding period, then she breastfed him, so he becomes her foster son; then intervention becomes obligatory, and the ruler separates them. Unlike iddah, because iddah is not contrary to the survival of marriage. Therefore, the marriage with a woman in iddah of another is kept intact after becoming Muslim. If one of them becomes Muslim, they are separated. And in the case of litigation by one of them, according to him (Imam Abu Hanifa) they are not separated, contrary to them (Sahibayn). The difference is that the entitlement of one of them is not voided by the litigation of the other, because his belief does not change. As for the belief of the one persisting in disbelief, it does not oppose the Islam of the Muslim because Islam is exalted and not exalted over. And if both litigate, they are separated by consensus because their litigation is like their arbitration.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a Magian's marriage to his mother, daughter, or other permanently prohibited relatives (mahram mahram). There are two positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such a marriage is originally valid among them, because they are not addressed by Islamic laws that prohibit such marriages. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it is invalid even among them, because the prohibition of marrying mahram is unanimously agreed upon by all Muslims, and thus dhimmis (and by extension Magians under dhimma) are subject to this ruling. However, all agree that upon conversion to Islam, the marriage must be dissolved (separation) because Islam prohibits such marriages. The reason for separation according to Imam Abu Hanifa is that mahramiyyat (being within the prohibited degrees) is contrary to the survival of the marriage in Islam; it is not like iddah which does not prevent survival. Thus, upon conversion, the marriage ends because the shar'i prohibition now applies. The text also discusses the case where only one spouse converts: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if only one converts, the separation occurs, but if they merely go to court (murafa'ah) without converting, it does not cause separation because the court cannot impose Islamic laws on them while they remain disbelievers. If both go to court, then they are separated by consensus. The example of a woman breastfeeding her husband (foster relationship) is given to illustrate that mahramiyyat affects both the initiation and survival of marriage in Islam.

Key Terms
مجوسی (majūsī): A Magian, fire-worshipper, considered a dhimmi in Islamic law.
محارم ابدیہ (maḥārim abadiyyah): Permanently prohibited relatives in marriage due to lineage, suckling, or marriage ties.
تعرض (taʿarruḍ): Intervention by the Islamic judge to annul a marriage that is invalid according to Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason Imam Abu Hanifa gives for separating the Magian couple upon their conversion?
A) The marriage was invalid from the beginning.
B) Mahramiyyat is contrary to the survival of marriage in Islam.
C) Conversion automatically annuls all previous marriages.
D) The judge has discretion to separate them.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, conversion to Islam dissolves a marriage between a Magian and a mahram relative, regardless of the original validity; the practical difference lies in the legitimacy of children and inheritance before conversion.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Separation by Murafa'a in Zoroastrian Mahram Marriage
Explains differing Hanafi views on separation upon complaint in mahram marriage of Zoroastrians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding separation upon murafa'a in a Zoroastrian mahram marriage and explain the difference in their legal reasoning.

Core Idea
One spouse's complaint (murafa'a) does not trigger separation according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn say it does.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of a judicial complaint (murafa'a) on a Zoroastrian mahram marriage. While there is consensus that conversion to Islam of one spouse necessitates separation, the ruling differs when only one spouse seeks an Islamic judgment without converting. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the marriage remains intact, whereas the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that separation is required. Understanding their proofs and the underlying distinction between conversion and complaint is key to appreciating the school's internal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core factual scenario
A Zoroastrian man and woman who are mahram (eternally prohibited relatives) are married. One spouse becomes Muslim, or one spouse makes a complaint (murafa'a) to the qadi seeking an Islamic ruling. You need to know the dispute centers on the murafa'a case.
The conversion case is unanimous; the dispute is only about murafa'a.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his reasoning
Abu Hanifa: separation does NOT occur upon single murafa'a. His proof: the original marriage was valid because kuffar are not addressed by sharia prohibitions, and one spouse's complaint does not change the other's belief or right. Islam's dominance applies only upon actual conversion, not upon mere submission to a judgment.
His analogy: the marriage remains valid; complaint does not override the other spouse's right.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their reasoning
Sahibayn: separation DOES occur upon single murafa'a. They analogize murafa'a to conversion: just as conversion triggers separation by consensus, so does complaint because it demonstrates submission to Islamic law. They view the original marriage as invalid under universal prohibition, with dhimma preventing interference until complaint removes that protection.
They argue that the judge must give effect to the complaint as if both had submitted.
4
Compare the key distinction: conversion vs. complaint
Abu Hanifa distinguishes on the basis of belief change: conversion changes the spouse's status (Islam dominates), but complaint does not alter the non-complaining spouse's belief. The Sahibayn see no essential difference: both actions place the couple under Islamic jurisdiction.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Abu Hanifa the judge does not separate on single murafa'a; under Sahibayn he does.
5
Identify the consensus scenario and its reasoning
If both spouses complain (murafa'a), there is consensus that separation is wajib. This is because both have submitted to Islamic law, making it as if they appointed the judge as an arbiter. The judge's general authority (wilaya 'amma) then mandates separation.
This consensus underscores that the dispute is only about unilateral action.

کے پاس مرافعہ کیا اور حکم اسلام طلب کیا تو بالاتفاق تفریق کر دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کا مرافعہ کرنا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ دونوں کا کسی تیسرے کو حکم بنانا اور یہ دونوں اگر کسی کو حکم بناتے اور اس سے حکم اسلام طلب کرتے تو حکم کیلئے جائز تھا کہ ان دونوں کے درمیان تفریق کر دے۔ پس قاضی عموم ولایت کی وجہ سے زیادہ مستحق ہے کہ ان دونوں میں تفریق کر دے۔ اسی کی طرف اللہ تعالیٰ نے اشارہ فرمایا ہے فسان جاؤک فاحكم بينهم بما انزل الله الآیة
Then, when one of them becomes Muslim, they are separated between them, and when one of them makes a complaint (murafa'a), they are not separated according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to them (the two companions). The difference is that the right of one of them is not invalidated by the complaint of his companion, because his belief does not change. As for the belief of the one persisting in disbelief, it does not oppose the Islam of the Muslim, because Islam is dominant and not dominated. If both make a complaint, they are separated by consensus, because their complaint is like their making (the judge) an arbiter.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effects of conversion to Islam and judicial complaint (murafa'a) on a marriage between Zoroastrians (Majus) that involves a mahram (prohibited relative). The discussion begins by establishing that when both spouses convert to Islam, there is consensus that the judge must separate them because the marriage, which was valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa but invalid according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), becomes subject to Islamic law, which prohibits marriage between mahram. The Sahibayn argue that the marriage was originally invalid because the prohibition of eternal relatives (maharmat abadiyya) is universal, binding even on non-Muslims under dhimma, but the dhimma contract prevented interference until conversion. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the marriage was valid because kuffar are not addressed by the rights of sharia (khitab al-shar'i) and do not believe in the prohibition; thus the original marriage was valid. The author then addresses a question: if the marriage was valid, why separate upon conversion? The answer is that after conversion, the spouses become subject to Islamic law, which prohibits such a marriage both initially and continuously. An analogy is given: a woman marries an infant, then breastfeeds him, making him her foster son; the judge must separate them. In contrast, a marriage with a woman in her 'idda is not invalidated by its continuity, so it remains after conversion. The core of the passage is the ruling when only one spouse converts or makes a complaint. According to the text: 'Then, when one of them becomes Muslim, they are separated; and when one of them makes a complaint (murafa'a), they are not separated according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to them (the two companions).' The commentary explains that Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that a single spouse's complaint does not invalidate the other's right because their belief (i.e., the complaining spouse's submission to Islamic law) does not change the other's belief. But when one converts, Islam's dominance overrides the other's disbelief, so separation occurs. If both complain, they are separated by consensus because it is as if they appointed the judge as an arbiter. The passage then provides the detailed proofs: the Sahibayn analogize one spouse's complaint to one spouse's conversion, both triggering separation, while Abu Hanifa insists on the original validity of the marriage and the lack of preference between conflicting beliefs in the absence of conversion. Finally, the judge's general authority (wilaya 'amma) is invoked via the Quranic verse 'So if they come to you, judge between them by what Allah has revealed' (5:49) to justify separation when both complain.

Key Terms
مرافعہ (murafa'a): Complaint or recourse to a judge seeking a legal ruling or judgment.
محارم ابدیہ (maharmat abadiyya): Eternal prohibited relatives by blood, marriage, or fosterage, whom one can never marry.
مجوسی (majusi): Zoroastrian, a follower of the Magian religion, considered a kitabi (People of the Book) in Hanafi law for certain rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling when one spouse in a Zoroastrian mahram marriage makes a murafa'a (complaint) without converting?
A) The judge must separate them immediately.
B) The judge does not separate them, as the original marriage remains valid and one complaint does not override the other spouse's right.
C) The judge must wait for the other spouse to also complain.
D) The judge refers the matter to a higher authority.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa differentiates murafa'a from conversion; the Sahibayn analogize them, leading to different rulings on separation in Zoroastrian mahram marriages upon a single complaint.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Ruling on Apostate Marriages
States prohibition of marriage involving apostates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited marriages involving apostates and explain the rational (dalil aqli) behind each prohibition.

Core Idea
An apostate's marriage is prohibited because it distracts from the essential contemplation required for repentance.

This passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya presents a clear ruling on marriages involving apostates. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the underlying rationale: an apostate is under threat of execution and given respite only for repentance; marriage would distract from that purpose. Similarly, an apostate woman is confined for contemplation and cannot be married.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited marriages
The text lists: apostate man marrying a Muslim woman, a disbelieving woman, or an apostate woman. Also, an apostate woman cannot be married by anyone.
Note that the prohibition is comprehensive: no spouse qualifies.
2
Trace the rational (dalil aqli)
The reason given is that the apostate is liable for execution; respite is only for the necessity of contemplation (ta'mul). Marriage distracts from this, so it is not legislated.
The ruling is derived from the purpose of the apostate's situation, not from a specific text.
3
Extend to the apostate woman
The apostate woman is also prohibited from marrying because she is confined for contemplation and marriage involves service to a husband, which would conflict.
The wording 'and the service of the husband' adds a gender-specific nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوزان يتزوج المرتد مسلمة ولا كافرة ومرتدة لانه مستحق للقتل والامهال ضرورة التامل والنكاح يشغله عنه فلا يشرع فى حقه و كذا المرتدة لايتزوجها مسلم ولا كافر لانها محبوسة للتامل وخدمة الزوج
And it is not permissible for an apostate to marry a Muslim woman, nor a disbelieving woman, nor an apostate woman, because he is liable for execution, and respite is only for the necessity of contemplation, and marriage distracts him from it, so it is not legislated for him. Similarly, an apostate woman cannot be married by a Muslim nor by a disbeliever, because she is confined for contemplation and the service of the husband.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This is a clear ruling statement regarding marriages involving apostates (murtadd). The text establishes three prohibitions: (1) an apostate man cannot marry a Muslim woman; (2) he cannot marry a disbelieving woman (kafira); (3) he cannot marry an apostate woman. The reason given is that an apostate is subject to capital punishment (for leaving Islam), and the only reason he is given respite (imhal) is to allow for repentance and contemplation. Marriage would distract him from this essential purpose, so it is not legislated for him. Similarly, an apostate woman cannot be married by anyone—neither a Muslim nor a disbeliever—because she is also in a state of being confined for contemplation (mahbusa li al-ta'mul), and marriage involves service to a husband, which would conflict with this. The ruling is based on rational deduction (dalil 'aqli) from the primary objective of an apostate's situation: the necessity of repentance over worldly affairs.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A person who has renounced Islam, either by word, action, or belief.
امهال (imhal): Respite or postponement of execution to allow for contemplation and repentance.
تامل (ta'mul): Contemplation on the truth of Islam and repentance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Yes, if he converts back to Islam first.

Key Takeaway
An apostate's marriage is prohibited in all forms because it interferes with the sole purpose of their respite: repentance.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Murafa'ah and Magian Marriage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on murafa'ah in Magian marriages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the effect of murafa'ah on a Magian marriage, and explain the underlying rationale behind each view.

Core Idea
A spouse's seeking a judge's ruling does not dissolve a Magian marriage, unless both seek it or one converts.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the dissolution of a Magian marriage when one spouse approaches the Islamic judge seeking a ruling (murafa'ah). While conversion to Islam by one spouse leads to separation unanimously, what if they merely seek the judge's decree? Imam Abu Hanifa and the Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ on this precise question, with each side relying on distinct legal principles. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the Hanafi methodology of distinguishing between original validity and post-conversion dynamics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Understand when the disagreement arises: a Magian couple married within prohibited degrees. One spouse approaches the judge seeking an Islamic ruling (murafa'ah), but does not convert to Islam.
Conversion triggers separation by consensus; the dispute is only about murafa'ah.
2
State each Imam's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the marriage remains intact; no separation is made. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that separation is required.
This is the core of the intra-school ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof (qiyas)
The Sahibayn analogize murafa'ah to conversion: just as conversion triggers separation, so should seeking the judge's ruling, because both show submission to Islamic law. They also argue the original marriage was invalid but tolerated under dhimmah.
Their analogy: one's conversion like both converting; one's murafa'ah like both making reference.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's response and distinction
Abu Hanifa argues the original marriage was valid. Murafa'ah does not change the other spouse's belief; there is no preponderance (tarjih) to dissolve. Conversion, in contrast, brings dominant Islam that overcomes disbelief.
Key distinction: conversion has overcoming force; murafa'ah lacks it.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A judge following Abu Hanifa will not separate the couple upon one spouse's request; a judge following the Sahibayn will. This affects judicial practice in Islamic courts.
The text does not indicate which view is mufta bihi.
