بہر حال عورت تو وہ طلاق کی اہل نہیں ہے۔ لہذا قاضی عورت کے اباء عن الاسلام کے وقت اس عورت کا قائم مقام نہیں ہوگا۔ پھر جب قاضی نے عورت کے انکار کی وجہ سے دونوں میں تفریق کر دی تو عورت کیلئے مہر ہو گا اگر اس کے ساتھ دخول کیا تھا۔ دخول کے ذریعہ مہر کے مؤکد ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر اس کے ساتھ دخول نہیں کیا تھا تو اس عورت کیلئے مہر نہیں ہو گا۔ اسلئے کہ فرقت عورت ہی کی جانب سے آئی اور مہر مؤکر نہیں ہوا۔ پس ردت اور مطاوعت ابن زوج کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عورت مسلمان ہوگئی اور اس کا شوہر کا فر ہے کتابی یا غیر کتابی۔ تو اب قاضی شوہر پر اسلام پیش کرے گا۔ اگر قاضی کے اسلام پیش کرنے پر شو ہر مسلمان ہو گیا تو وہ عورت اس کی بیوی ہے۔ اور نکاح بدستور رہے گا اور اگر شوہر نے اسلام لائے سے انکار کر دیا تو قاضی دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا۔ اور یہ تفریق طرفین کے نزدیک طلاق ہے، فسخ نکاح نہیں ۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ شوہر مسلمان ہو گیا اور اس کے تحت مجوسیہ ہے تو قاضی مجوسیہ عورت پر اسلام پیش کرے گا اور اگر وہ اسلام لائی تو یہ اس کی بیوی ہے۔ نکاح بدستور باقی ہے اور اگر اسلام لانے سے انکار کر دیا تو قاضی دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا۔ اور یہ فرقت طلاق نہیں ہوگی بلکہ فسخ نکاح ہو گا۔ امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں تفریق طلاق نہیں ہوگی۔ برابر ہے کہ شوہر اسلام لانے سے انکار کرے یا عورت انکار کرے بلکہ فسخ نکاح ہو گا۔

اس تفریق کو نسخ مانے کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ تفریق کے بعد بھی عدد طلاق میں کمی نہیں آئے گی۔ حتی کہ اگر آخر کے مسلمان ہونے کے بعد دوسری مرتبہ نکاح کر لیا تو شوہر تین طلاقوں کا مالک ہوگا۔ اور جن کے نزدیک فرقت کی وجہ سے ایک کم ہوگئی ان کے نزدیک دوسری مرتبہ نکاح کرنے کے بعد شو ہر دو طلاقوں کا مالک ہو گا فرقت کی وجہ سے ایک کم ہو گئی ۔ حاصل یہ ہے امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شوہر انکار کرے یا عورت دونوں صورتوں میں تفریق فتح ہے۔ اور طرفین کے نزدیک شوہر کے انکار کرنے سے جو تفریق ہوگی وہ طلاق ہے فسخ نہیں اور عورت کے انکار کرنے سے جو تفریق ہے وہ مسخ ہوگی طلاق نہیں ۔

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ آخر پر اسلام پیش کرنا ہمارا مذ ہب ہے۔ ورنہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ آخر پر اسلام پیش نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اسلام پیش کرنے میں ذمیوں کے ساتھ تعرض کرنا ہے۔ حالانکہ عقد ذمہ کے ذریعہ ہم نے اس بات کی ضمانت دی ہے کہ ہم ان کے ساتھ کوئی تعرض نہیں کریں گے ۔ مگر چونکہ ملک نکاح دخول سے پہلے غیر مؤکد ہے اس لئے اسلام لاتے ہی نکاح منقطع ہو جائے گا۔ اور دخول کے بعد ملک نکاح مؤکد ہو جاتی ہے اسلئے وقوع فرقت تین حیض کے گذرنے تک مؤخر ہو جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ طلاق میں۔ یعنی دخول سے پہلے نفس طلاق نکاح کو منقطع کر دیتی ہے۔ اور دخول کے بعد نکاح انقضاء عدت کے بعد منقطع ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت فیتا جل الی انقضاء ثلث حیض میں ثلث حیض غلط ہے کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک عدت میں طہر معتبر ہے نہ کہ حیض ۔ مگر صحیح عبارت کے طور پر یوں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اے حنفیو! تمہارے نزدیک مناسب ہے کہ وقوع فرقت تین حیض گذرنے تک مؤخر کر دیا جائے ۔ اس صورت میں عبارت بے غبار ہو جائے گی۔

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کے مسلمان ہونے یا مجوسیہ کے شوہر کے مسلمان ہونے سے مقاصد نکاح فوت ہو گئے اور فوات امر حادث ہے۔ اسلئے اس کے واسطے ایسے سبب کا ہونا ضروری ہے جس پر اس کی بنیاد قائم ہو سکے۔ اب دو ہی صورتیں ہیں۔ مقاصد نکاح کے فوات کا سبب اسلام کو قرار دیں یا اس شخص کے کفر کو جو ابھی تک کفر پر باقی ہے۔ صورت اول تو ممکن نہیں ۔ کیونکہ اسلام طاعت اور فرمانبرداری ہے۔ مقاصد نکاح جیسی نعمتوں کے فوت ہونے کا سبب نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور صورت ثانیہ بھی ممکن نہیں ۔ کیونکہ مـن بقــى علـى کفرہ کا کفر پہلے سے موجود ہے۔ اور اس کفر نے نہ تو ابتداء نکاح کو منع کیا اور نہ بقاء مقاصد نکاح ( نعمتوں ) کو فوت کیا۔ پس ان دونوں کے علاوہ کسی تیسری چیز کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ جس کو سبب قرار دیا جا سکے۔ اس وجہ سے قاضی من بقی علی کفرہ پر اسلام پیش کرتے۔ پس اگر ہو مسلمان ہو گیا تو الحمد للہ مقاصد نکاح ہی حاصل ہو جائیں گئے۔ فرقت کی ضرورت ہی نہیں۔ اور اگر اسلام لانے سے انکار کر دیا تو فرقت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ پس یہ اباء عن الاسلام مقاصد نکاح کے فوت ہونے کا سبب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ابا عن الاسلام سلب نعمت کا سبب بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے اور چونکہ فوات مقاصد نکاح کیلئے فرقت لازم ہے لہذا جو سبب ہو گا فوات کا وہی سبب ہو گا اس کے لازم یعنی فرقت کا۔ اسلئے احناف کہتے ہیں کہ من بقی علی کفرہ پر اسلام پیش کیا جائے گا۔ تاکہ اس کے اباء عن الاسلام کو تفریق کا سبب بنایا جا سکے۔

امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ ذمیوں کے ساتھ تعرض ممتنع ہے۔ تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جبری تعرض ممتنع ہے۔ لیکن اس کے ساتھ اختیاری طور پر نفس بات چیت کرنا منع نہیں ہے۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جو موطاء میں ابن شہاب الزہری سے روایت ہے۔ حديث ان ابنة الوليد بن المغيرة كانت تحت صفوان ابن امية فاسلمت يوم الفتح وهرب زوجها صفوان ابن امية من الاسلام فلم يفرق رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بينه و بين امرأته حتى اسلم صفوان واستقرت عنده امرأته بذالک النكاح - ترجمہ ولید بن مغیرہ کی بیٹی صفوان ابن امیہ کے تحت (نکاح) میں تھی ۔ فتح کے دن وہ مسلمان ہوگئی ۔ اور اس کا شوہر صفوان ابن امیہ اسلام سے بھاگ گیا۔ تو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اسکے اور اس کی بیوی کے درمیان تفریق نہیں کی۔ یہاں تک کہ صفوان مسلمان ہو گیا۔ اور اس کے پاس اس کی بیوی اسی نکاح سے باقی رہی۔ اور طحاوی اور ابن العربی نے ذکر کیا ان عمر فرق بين نصراني و بين نصرانية بابائه عن الاسلام یعنی حضرت عمر نے نصرانی اور نصرانیہ کے درمیان تفریق کی نصرانی کے اسلام سے انکار کر دینے کی وجہ سے و ذکر اصحابنا ان رجلاً من تغلب اسلمت امرأته وهى نصرانية فرفعت الى عمر بن الخطاب فقال له اسلم والا فرقت بينكما فابی ففرق بینها یعنی ہمارے اصحاب نے ذکر کیا کہ تغلب کا ایک آدمی اس کی بیوی مسلمان ہوگئی حالانکہ وہ نصرانی تھی ۔اس نے حضرت عمر کی عدالت میں معاملہ پیش کیا آپ نے فرمایا اس سے تو اسلام لا اور نہ تم دونوں میں تفریق کر دی جائے گی اس نے (اسلام لانے سے انکار کر دیا تو آپ نے ان دونوں میں تفریق کر دی۔ ان احادیث سے اسلام کا پیش کرنا ثابت ہے۔

(الخ) امام شافعی کے ساتھ بحث و مباحثہ سے فراغت پا کر وجہ قول ابی یوسف سے امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ بات چیت کرنا چاہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ انہوں نے فرمایا کہ تفریق دونوں صورتوں میں طلاق نہیں بلکہ نسخ ہے۔ ابو یوسف کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ فرقت ایسے سبب سے واقع ہوئی جس میں زوجین دونوں شریک ہیں۔ یعنی ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی طرف سے متحقق ہے۔ مطلب یہ کہ ایک مسلمان ہوا اور دوسرے نے اسلام لانے سے انکار کیا تب فرقت واقع ہوئی اور ہر وہ فرقت جو ایسے سبب سے ہو جس میں عورت و مرد دونوں شریک ہوں طلاق نہیں ہوگی۔ مثلاً احد الزوجین دوسرے کا مالک ہو گیا تو اس کی وجہ سے جو فرقت ہوگی وہ طلاق نہیں ہوگی بلکہ فسخ نکاح ہوگا۔ طرفین کی دلیل اور دونوں صورتوں میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ اباء عن الاسلام کی وجہ سے شوہر امساک بالمعروف سے رک گیا۔ حالانکہ وہ اسلام قبول کر کے امساک بالمعروف پر قادر تھا اور شریعت کا اصول ہے کہ اگر شوہر امساک بالمعروف سے رک جائے تو قاضی تسریح بالاحسان میں شوہر کے قائم مقام ہو گا۔ اور تسریح نام ہے طلاق کا لہذا قاضی کی یہ تفریق طلاق کہلائے گی۔ جیسا کہ مقطوع الذکر اور معنین
In any case, a woman is not eligible to divorce. Therefore, the qadi will not act as the woman's representative at the time of her refusal of Islam. Then, when the qadi separates them due to the woman's refusal, the woman will receive mahr if consummation had occurred with her, because mahr is confirmed by consummation. If consummation had not occurred with her, then she will not receive mahr, because the separation came from her side and mahr was not confirmed. Thus, apostasy and [the case of] a woman who is compelled to [divorce] her husband become similar.

Explanation of the scenario: A woman becomes Muslim and her husband is a disbeliever, whether a scriptural or non-scriptural disbeliever. Then the qadi will present Islam to the husband. If the husband becomes Muslim upon the qadi's presentation of Islam, then the woman is his wife and the marriage remains as before. If the husband refuses to accept Islam, the qadi will separate them. This separation, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), is divorce, not annulment of marriage. The second scenario: The husband becomes Muslim and under him is a Zoroastrian wife. Then the qadi will present Islam to the Zoroastrian woman. If she accepts Islam, she is his wife; the marriage remains as before. If she refuses to accept Islam, the qadi will separate them. This separation will not be divorce but annulment of marriage. Imam Abu Yusuf said that in both cases the separation is not divorce; whether the husband refuses or the woman refuses, it is annulment of marriage.

The benefit of considering this separation as annulment is that the number of divorces is not reduced after the separation. Even if, after both become Muslim later, they marry again, the husband will have control of three divorces. According to those who hold that the separation reduces the count by one, after a second marriage the husband will have control of two divorces because one was reduced due to the separation. In summary, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, whether the husband refuses or the woman refuses, in both cases the separation is annulment. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the separation that occurs due to the husband's refusal is divorce, not annulment, and the separation that occurs due to the woman's refusal is annulment, not divorce.

Author of Hidayah states: Presenting Islam to the non-Muslim spouse is our madhhab. Otherwise, Imam Shafi'i says that Islam will not be presented to the non-Muslim spouse. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that presenting Islam involves interference with dhimmis, whereas through the contract of dhimma we have guaranteed that we will not interfere with them. However, because the ownership of marriage before consummation is not confirmed, as soon as he accepts Islam, the marriage is dissolved. After consummation, the ownership of marriage becomes confirmed, so the occurrence of separation is delayed until three menstruations pass, as in divorce. That is, before consummation, the divorce itself dissolves the marriage, and after consummation, the marriage is dissolved after the completion of the waiting period. The author of Hidayah's phrase 'yatijah al-insiraf ila ingida thalath hiya' [meaning: it is deferred until the end of three menstruations] is incorrect because according to Imam Shafi'i, in waiting periods, purity (tuhr) is considered, not menstruation. But it can be said correctly: Imam Shafi'i says, 'O Hanafis! According to you, it is appropriate that the occurrence of separation be deferred until three menstruations pass.' In that case, the expression becomes clear.

Our proof is that due to the woman becoming Muslim or the Zoroastrian woman's husband becoming Muslim, the objectives of marriage are lost, and this loss is an incidental matter. Therefore, it is necessary that there be a cause upon which it can be based. There are only two possibilities: either we consider Islam as the cause of the loss of the objectives of marriage, or we consider the disbelief of the person who remains upon disbelief. The first possibility is not possible because Islam is obedience and submission; it cannot be the cause of the loss of blessings like the objectives of marriage. The second possibility is also not possible because the disbelief of the one who remains upon disbelief existed before, and that disbelief neither prevented the initial marriage nor caused the loss of the continuation of the objectives of marriage. Therefore, a third thing is necessary that can be made the cause. For this reason, the qadi presents Islam to the one who remains upon disbelief. So if he becomes Muslim, praise be to Allah, the objectives of marriage are achieved and there is no need for separation. If he refuses to accept Islam, then separation is established. Thus, this refusal of Islam becomes the cause of the loss of the objectives of marriage because refusal of Islam is capable of being a cause of the removal of blessing. And since separation is necessary for the loss of the objectives of marriage, whatever is the cause of the loss is also the cause of its necessary consequence, i.e., separation. Therefore, the Hanafis say that Islam will be presented to the one who remains upon disbelief so that his refusal of Islam can be made the cause of separation.

As for Imam Shafi'i's statement that interference with dhimmis is prohibited, we say that compulsory interference is prohibited, but voluntarily speaking with them is not prohibited. Our madhhab is also supported by the hadith narrated in Muwatta from Ibn Shihab al-Zahri: 'The daughter of al-Walid ibn al-Mughirah was under Safwan ibn Umayyah. She became Muslim on the day of the conquest, and her husband Safwan ibn Umayyah fled from Islam. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did not separate between him and his wife until Safwan became Muslim, and his wife remained with him with that marriage.' Al-Tahawi and Ibn al-Arabi mentioned that Umar separated between a Christian and a Christian woman due to the man's refusal of Islam. And our companions mentioned that a man from Taghlib, his wife became Muslim while she was a Christian. She raised the matter to Umar ibn al-Khattab. He said to him, 'Accept Islam, or I will separate between you two.' He refused, so he separated between them. These hadiths establish the presentation of Islam.

(End) Having finished the discussion with Imam Shafi'i, the author intends to discuss the reasoning for Abu Yusuf's statement with Imam Abu Yusuf. Because he said that the separation in both cases is not divorce but annulment. The reason for Abu Yusuf's statement is that the separation occurred due to a cause in which both spouses participate, i.e., it is actualized from both sides. Meaning that one became Muslim and the other refused to accept Islam; then separation occurred. And every separation that occurs due to a cause in which both man and woman participate is not divorce. For example, if one of the spouses becomes the owner of the other, the separation that occurs due to that is not divorce but annulment of marriage. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and the reason for the difference in the two cases is that due to refusal of Islam, the husband refrains from retaining [the wife] with kindness, whereas he was capable of retaining with kindness by accepting Islam. And the principle of shariah is that if the husband refrains from retaining with kindness, the qadi becomes his representative for releasing with kindness. And releasing is called divorce; therefore, this separation by the qadi is called divorce, as in the case of a eunuch and an impotent man...
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from Ashraf al-Hidayah on the rulings related to the separation of spouses when one accepts Islam and the other refuses. It covers several interconnected issues: the effect on mahr, the nature of the separation (talaq vs faskh), the intra-Hanafi difference, and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Shafi'i.

The author begins by noting a nuance: if a wife apostatizes or refuses Islam, the qadi does not act as her representative for divorce, because a woman cannot divorce. If separation occurs due to her refusal, she gets mahr only if consummation occurred; otherwise no mahr, as the separation originated from her side.

He then explains two scenarios: (1) Wife becomes Muslim, husband is non-Muslim: qadi presents Islam to husband; if he accepts, marriage continues; if he refuses, qadi separates them. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), this separation is talaq (divorce). (2) Husband becomes Muslim, wife is Zoroastrian: qadi presents Islam to her; if she accepts, marriage continues; if she refuses, qadi separates them. Here the separation is faskh (annulment), not talaq. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that in both cases it is faskh.

The practical benefit of considering it faskh is that the number of divorces is not reduced; if they remarry later, the husband retains full three divorces. If considered talaq, one talaq is used.

The passage then presents the inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafis hold that Islam must be presented to the non-Muslim spouse; Imam Shafi'i opposes this, arguing it violates the dhimma contract. The Hanafi response is that compulsory interference is prohibited, but voluntary invitation is not. They provide proof from a hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) did not separate Safwan and his wife until Safwan accepted Islam, and from actions of Umar (RA) separating couples when the husband refused Islam.

Finally, the author discusses the reasoning for Abu Yusuf's view: the separation occurs due to a cause involving both spouses, like one becoming owner of the other, which is faskh. The majority (tarafayn) respond that the husband's refusal to retain with kindness allows the qadi to act as his representative for divorce, hence it is talaq. This is analogous to cases of physical incapacity.

Key Terms
اباء عن الإسلام (ibā’ ‘an al-islām): Refusal to accept Islam after being invited; the act of rejecting the offer of Islam.
تفريق (tafrīq): Separation between spouses ordered by the qadi due to the spouse's refusal of Islam.
فسخ نکاح (faskh al-nikāḥ): Annulment of marriage; a dissolution that does not count towards the three divorces and does not reduce the number of available divorces.

According to the Hanafi school, what is the hukm (legal classification) of presenting Islam to the non-Muslim spouse?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obliges the qadi to present Islam to the non-Muslim spouse before separation, establishing the refusal as the legal cause for tafriq, and this is supported by hadith and the practice of the Sahaba.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Nature of Separation: Talaq vs Faskh (Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on talaq vs faskh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between talaq and faskh in the case of spousal refusal of Islam, and explain the practical consequence on the count of divorces.

Core Idea
When the wife refuses Islam, separation is faskh; when the husband refuses, it is talaq — protecting the husband's full divorce capacity.

This lesson focuses on two key scenarios: when the husband refuses Islam after the wife converts, and when the wife refuses Islam after the husband converts. The Hanafi school distinguishes between them, and there is an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Abu Yusuf holds both are faskh, while the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) differentiate. We will explore the reasoning and the practical benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Scenario A: Wife becomes Muslim, husband refuses. Scenario B: Husband becomes Muslim, wife (Zoroastrian) refuses. The qadi presents Islam in both cases.
The passage explicitly describes these two scenarios with the ruling on mahr.
2
Note the default ruling (tarafayn)
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: In Scenario A (husband refuses), the separation is talaq (divorce). In Scenario B (wife refuses), the separation is faskh (annulment). This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
The passage says: 'شوہر کے انکار کرنے سے جو تفریق ہوگی وہ طلاق ہے' and 'عورت کے انکار کرنے سے جو تفریق ہے وہ مسخ ہوگی'.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's view and his reasoning
Imam Abu Yusuf holds both scenarios result in faskh. His reasoning: the separation occurs due to a cause involving both spouses (one converting, the other refusing), similar to when one spouse becomes the owner of the other, which is faskh.
The passage explains: 'فرقت ایسے سبب سے واقع ہوئی جس میں زوجین دونوں شریک ہیں'.
4
Understand the practical benefit of faskh
If the separation is faskh, it does not count as a divorce, so the husband retains all three divorces for future marriages. If it is talaq, one divorce is used up.
The passage explicitly states this benefit: 'عدد طلاق میں کمی نہیں آئے گی'.

بہر حال عورت تو وہ طلاق کی اہل نہیں ہے۔ لہذا قاضی عورت کے اباء عن الاسلام کے وقت اس عورت کا قائم مقام نہیں ہوگا۔ پھر جب قاضی نے عورت کے انکار کی وجہ سے دونوں میں تفریق کر دی تو عورت کیلئے مہر ہو گا اگر اس کے ساتھ دخول کیا تھا۔ دخول کے ذریعہ مہر کے مؤکد ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر اس کے ساتھ دخول نہیں کیا تھا تو اس عورت کیلئے مہر نہیں ہو گا۔ اسلئے کہ فرقت عورت ہی کی جانب سے آئی اور مہر مؤکر نہیں ہوا۔ پس ردت اور مطاوعت ابن زوج کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عورت مسلمان ہوگئی اور اس کا شوہر کا فر ہے کتابی یا غیر کتابی۔ تو اب قاضی شوہر پر اسلام پیش کرے گا۔ اگر قاضی کے اسلام پیش کرنے پر شو ہر مسلمان ہو گیا تو وہ عورت اس کی بیوی ہے۔ اور نکاح بدستور رہے گا اور اگر شوہر نے اسلام لائے سے انکار کر دیا تو قاضی دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا۔ اور یہ تفریق طرفین کے نزدیک طلاق ہے، فسخ نکاح نہیں ۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ شوہر مسلمان ہو گیا اور اس کے تحت مجوسیہ ہے تو قاضی مجوسیہ عورت پر اسلام پیش کرے گا اور اگر وہ اسلام لائی تو یہ اس کی بیوی ہے۔ نکاح بدستور باقی ہے اور اگر اسلام لانے سے انکار کر دیا تو قاضی دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا۔ اور یہ فرقت طلاق نہیں ہوگی بلکہ فسخ نکاح ہو گا۔ امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں تفریق طلاق نہیں ہوگی۔ برابر ہے کہ شوہر اسلام لانے سے انکار کرے یا عورت انکار کرے بلکہ فسخ نکاح ہو گا۔

اس تفریق کو نسخ مانے کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ تفریق کے بعد بھی عدد طلاق میں کمی نہیں آئے گی۔ حتی کہ اگر آخر کے مسلمان ہونے کے بعد دوسری مرتبہ نکاح کر لیا تو شوہر تین طلاقوں کا مالک ہوگا۔ اور جن کے نزدیک فرقت کی وجہ سے ایک کم ہوگئی ان کے نزدیک دوسری مرتبہ نکاح کرنے کے بعد شو ہر دو طلاقوں کا مالک ہو گا فرقت کی وجہ سے ایک کم ہو گئی ۔ حاصل یہ ہے امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شوہر انکار کرے یا عورت دونوں صورتوں میں تفریق فتح ہے۔ اور طرفین کے نزدیک شوہر کے انکار کرنے سے جو تفریق ہوگی وہ طلاق ہے فسخ نہیں اور عورت کے انکار کرنے سے جو تفریق ہے وہ مسخ ہوگی طلاق نہیں ۔

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ آخر پر اسلام پیش کرنا ہمارا مذ ہب ہے۔ ورنہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ آخر پر اسلام پیش نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اسلام پیش کرنے میں ذمیوں کے ساتھ تعرض کرنا ہے۔ حالانکہ عقد ذمہ کے ذریعہ ہم نے اس بات کی ضمانت دی ہے کہ ہم ان کے ساتھ کوئی تعرض نہیں کریں گے ۔ مگر چونکہ ملک نکاح دخول سے پہلے غیر مؤکد ہے اس لئے اسلام لاتے ہی نکاح منقطع ہو جائے گا۔ اور دخول کے بعد ملک نکاح مؤکد ہو جاتی ہے اسلئے وقوع فرقت تین حیض کے گذرنے تک مؤخر ہو جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ طلاق میں۔ یعنی دخول سے پہلے نفس طلاق نکاح کو منقطع کر دیتی ہے۔ اور دخول کے بعد نکاح انقضاء عدت کے بعد منقطع ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت فیتا جل الی انقضاء ثلث حیض میں ثلث حیض غلط ہے کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک عدت میں طہر معتبر ہے نہ کہ حیض ۔ مگر صحیح عبارت کے طور پر یوں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اے حنفیو! تمہارے نزدیک مناسب ہے کہ وقوع فرقت تین حیض گذرنے تک مؤخر کر دیا جائے ۔ اس صورت میں عبارت بے غبار ہو جائے گی۔

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کے مسلمان ہونے یا مجوسیہ کے شوہر کے مسلمان ہونے سے مقاصد نکاح فوت ہو گئے اور فوات امر حادث ہے۔ اسلئے اس کے واسطے ایسے سبب کا ہونا ضروری ہے جس پر اس کی بنیاد قائم ہو سکے۔ اب دو ہی صورتیں ہیں۔ مقاصد نکاح کے فوات کا سبب اسلام کو قرار دیں یا اس شخص کے کفر کو جو ابھی تک کفر پر باقی ہے۔ صورت اول تو ممکن نہیں ۔ کیونکہ اسلام طاعت اور فرمانبرداری ہے۔ مقاصد نکاح جیسی نعمتوں کے فوت ہونے کا سبب نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور صورت ثانیہ بھی ممکن نہیں ۔ کیونکہ مـن بقــى علـى کفرہ کا کفر پہلے سے موجود ہے۔ اور اس کفر نے نہ تو ابتداء نکاح کو منع کیا اور نہ بقاء مقاصد نکاح ( نعمتوں ) کو فوت کیا۔ پس ان دونوں کے علاوہ کسی تیسری چیز کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ جس کو سبب قرار دیا جا سکے۔ اس وجہ سے قاضی من بقی علی کفرہ پر اسلام پیش کرتے۔ پس اگر ہو مسلمان ہو گیا تو الحمد للہ مقاصد نکاح ہی حاصل ہو جائیں گئے۔ فرقت کی ضرورت ہی نہیں۔ اور اگر اسلام لانے سے انکار کر دیا تو فرقت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ پس یہ اباء عن الاسلام مقاصد نکاح کے فوت ہونے کا سبب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ابا عن الاسلام سلب نعمت کا سبب بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے اور چونکہ فوات مقاصد نکاح کیلئے فرقت لازم ہے لہذا جو سبب ہو گا فوات کا وہی سبب ہو گا اس کے لازم یعنی فرقت کا۔ اسلئے احناف کہتے ہیں کہ من بقی علی کفرہ پر اسلام پیش کیا جائے گا۔ تاکہ اس کے اباء عن الاسلام کو تفریق کا سبب بنایا جا سکے۔

امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ ذمیوں کے ساتھ تعرض ممتنع ہے۔ تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جبری تعرض ممتنع ہے۔ لیکن اس کے ساتھ اختیاری طور پر نفس بات چیت کرنا منع نہیں ہے۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے جو موطاء میں ابن شہاب الزہری سے روایت ہے۔ حديث ان ابنة الوليد بن المغيرة كانت تحت صفوان ابن امية فاسلمت يوم الفتح وهرب زوجها صفوان ابن امية من الاسلام فلم يفرق رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بينه و بين امرأته حتى اسلم صفوان واستقرت عنده امرأته بذالک النكاح - ترجمہ ولید بن مغیرہ کی بیٹی صفوان ابن امیہ کے تحت (نکاح) میں تھی ۔ فتح کے دن وہ مسلمان ہوگئی ۔ اور اس کا شوہر صفوان ابن امیہ اسلام سے بھاگ گیا۔ تو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اسکے اور اس کی بیوی کے درمیان تفریق نہیں کی۔ یہاں تک کہ صفوان مسلمان ہو گیا۔ اور اس کے پاس اس کی بیوی اسی نکاح سے باقی رہی۔ اور طحاوی اور ابن العربی نے ذکر کیا ان عمر فرق بين نصراني و بين نصرانية بابائه عن الاسلام یعنی حضرت عمر نے نصرانی اور نصرانیہ کے درمیان تفریق کی نصرانی کے اسلام سے انکار کر دینے کی وجہ سے و ذکر اصحابنا ان رجلاً من تغلب اسلمت امرأته وهى نصرانية فرفعت الى عمر بن الخطاب فقال له اسلم والا فرقت بينكما فابی ففرق بینها یعنی ہمارے اصحاب نے ذکر کیا کہ تغلب کا ایک آدمی اس کی بیوی مسلمان ہوگئی حالانکہ وہ نصرانی تھی ۔اس نے حضرت عمر کی عدالت میں معاملہ پیش کیا آپ نے فرمایا اس سے تو اسلام لا اور نہ تم دونوں میں تفریق کر دی جائے گی اس نے (اسلام لانے سے انکار کر دیا تو آپ نے ان دونوں میں تفریق کر دی۔ ان احادیث سے اسلام کا پیش کرنا ثابت ہے۔

(الخ) امام شافعی کے ساتھ بحث و مباحثہ سے فراغت پا کر وجہ قول ابی یوسف سے امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ بات چیت کرنا چاہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ انہوں نے فرمایا کہ تفریق دونوں صورتوں میں طلاق نہیں بلکہ نسخ ہے۔ ابو یوسف کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ فرقت ایسے سبب سے واقع ہوئی جس میں زوجین دونوں شریک ہیں۔ یعنی ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی طرف سے متحقق ہے۔ مطلب یہ کہ ایک مسلمان ہوا اور دوسرے نے اسلام لانے سے انکار کیا تب فرقت واقع ہوئی اور ہر وہ فرقت جو ایسے سبب سے ہو جس میں عورت و مرد دونوں شریک ہوں طلاق نہیں ہوگی۔ مثلاً احد الزوجین دوسرے کا مالک ہو گیا تو اس کی وجہ سے جو فرقت ہوگی وہ طلاق نہیں ہوگی بلکہ فسخ نکاح ہوگا۔ طرفین کی دلیل اور دونوں صورتوں میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ اباء عن الاسلام کی وجہ سے شوہر امساک بالمعروف سے رک گیا۔ حالانکہ وہ اسلام قبول کر کے امساک بالمعروف پر قادر تھا اور شریعت کا اصول ہے کہ اگر شوہر امساک بالمعروف سے رک جائے تو قاضی تسریح بالاحسان میں شوہر کے قائم مقام ہو گا۔ اور تسریح نام ہے طلاق کا لہذا قاضی کی یہ تفریق طلاق کہلائے گی۔ جیسا کہ مقطوع الذکر اور معنین
In any case, a woman is not eligible to divorce. Therefore, the qadi will not act as the woman's representative at the time of her refusal of Islam. Then, when the qadi separates them due to the woman's refusal, the woman will receive mahr if consummation had occurred with her, because mahr is confirmed by consummation. If consummation had not occurred with her, then she will not receive mahr, because the separation came from her side and mahr was not confirmed. Thus, apostasy and [the case of] a woman who is compelled to [divorce] her husband become similar.

Explanation of the scenario: A woman becomes Muslim and her husband is a disbeliever, whether a scriptural or non-scriptural disbeliever. Then the qadi will present Islam to the husband. If the husband becomes Muslim upon the qadi's presentation of Islam, then the woman is his wife and the marriage remains as before. If the husband refuses to accept Islam, the qadi will separate them. This separation, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), is divorce, not annulment of marriage. The second scenario: The husband becomes Muslim and under him is a Zoroastrian wife. Then the qadi will present Islam to the Zoroastrian woman. If she accepts Islam, she is his wife; the marriage remains as before. If she refuses to accept Islam, the qadi will separate them. This separation will not be divorce but annulment of marriage. Imam Abu Yusuf said that in both cases the separation is not divorce; whether the husband refuses or the woman refuses, it is annulment of marriage.

The benefit of considering this separation as annulment is that the number of divorces is not reduced after the separation. Even if, after both become Muslim later, they marry again, the husband will have control of three divorces. According to those who hold that the separation reduces the count by one, after a second marriage the husband will have control of two divorces because one was reduced due to the separation. In summary, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, whether the husband refuses or the woman refuses, in both cases the separation is annulment. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the separation that occurs due to the husband's refusal is divorce, not annulment, and the separation that occurs due to the woman's refusal is annulment, not divorce.

Author of Hidayah states: Presenting Islam to the non-Muslim spouse is our madhhab. Otherwise, Imam Shafi'i says that Islam will not be presented to the non-Muslim spouse. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that presenting Islam involves interference with dhimmis, whereas through the contract of dhimma we have guaranteed that we will not interfere with them. However, because the ownership of marriage before consummation is not confirmed, as soon as he accepts Islam, the marriage is dissolved. After consummation, the ownership of marriage becomes confirmed, so the occurrence of separation is delayed until three menstruations pass, as in divorce. That is, before consummation, the divorce itself dissolves the marriage, and after consummation, the marriage is dissolved after the completion of the waiting period. The author of Hidayah's phrase 'yatijah al-insiraf ila ingida thalath hiya' [meaning: it is deferred until the end of three menstruations] is incorrect because according to Imam Shafi'i, in waiting periods, purity (tuhr) is considered, not menstruation. But it can be said correctly: Imam Shafi'i says, 'O Hanafis! According to you, it is appropriate that the occurrence of separation be deferred until three menstruations pass.' In that case, the expression becomes clear.

Our proof is that due to the woman becoming Muslim or the Zoroastrian woman's husband becoming Muslim, the objectives of marriage are lost, and this loss is an incidental matter. Therefore, it is necessary that there be a cause upon which it can be based. There are only two possibilities: either we consider Islam as the cause of the loss of the objectives of marriage, or we consider the disbelief of the person who remains upon disbelief. The first possibility is not possible because Islam is obedience and submission; it cannot be the cause of the loss of blessings like the objectives of marriage. The second possibility is also not possible because the disbelief of the one who remains upon disbelief existed before, and that disbelief neither prevented the initial marriage nor caused the loss of the continuation of the objectives of marriage. Therefore, a third thing is necessary that can be made the cause. For this reason, the qadi presents Islam to the one who remains upon disbelief. So if he becomes Muslim, praise be to Allah, the objectives of marriage are achieved and there is no need for separation. If he refuses to accept Islam, then separation is established. Thus, this refusal of Islam becomes the cause of the loss of the objectives of marriage because refusal of Islam is capable of being a cause of the removal of blessing. And since separation is necessary for the loss of the objectives of marriage, whatever is the cause of the loss is also the cause of its necessary consequence, i.e., separation. Therefore, the Hanafis say that Islam will be presented to the one who remains upon disbelief so that his refusal of Islam can be made the cause of separation.

As for Imam Shafi'i's statement that interference with dhimmis is prohibited, we say that compulsory interference is prohibited, but voluntarily speaking with them is not prohibited. Our madhhab is also supported by the hadith narrated in Muwatta from Ibn Shihab al-Zahri: 'The daughter of al-Walid ibn al-Mughirah was under Safwan ibn Umayyah. She became Muslim on the day of the conquest, and her husband Safwan ibn Umayyah fled from Islam. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did not separate between him and his wife until Safwan became Muslim, and his wife remained with him with that marriage.' Al-Tahawi and Ibn al-Arabi mentioned that Umar separated between a Christian and a Christian woman due to the man's refusal of Islam. And our companions mentioned that a man from Taghlib, his wife became Muslim while she was a Christian. She raised the matter to Umar ibn al-Khattab. He said to him, 'Accept Islam, or I will separate between you two.' He refused, so he separated between them. These hadiths establish the presentation of Islam.

(End) Having finished the discussion with Imam Shafi'i, the author intends to discuss the reasoning for Abu Yusuf's statement with Imam Abu Yusuf. Because he said that the separation in both cases is not divorce but annulment. The reason for Abu Yusuf's statement is that the separation occurred due to a cause in which both spouses participate, i.e., it is actualized from both sides. Meaning that one became Muslim and the other refused to accept Islam; then separation occurred. And every separation that occurs due to a cause in which both man and woman participate is not divorce. For example, if one of the spouses becomes the owner of the other, the separation that occurs due to that is not divorce but annulment of marriage. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and the reason for the difference in the two cases is that due to refusal of Islam, the husband refrains from retaining [the wife] with kindness, whereas he was capable of retaining with kindness by accepting Islam. And the principle of shariah is that if the husband refrains from retaining with kindness, the qadi becomes his representative for releasing with kindness. And releasing is called divorce; therefore, this separation by the qadi is called divorce, as in the case of a eunuch and an impotent man...
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from Ashraf al-Hidayah on the rulings related to the separation of spouses when one accepts Islam and the other refuses. It covers several interconnected issues: the effect on mahr, the nature of the separation (talaq vs faskh), the intra-Hanafi difference, and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Shafi'i.

The author begins by noting a nuance: if a wife apostatizes or refuses Islam, the qadi does not act as her representative for divorce, because a woman cannot divorce. If separation occurs due to her refusal, she gets mahr only if consummation occurred; otherwise no mahr, as the separation originated from her side.

He then explains two scenarios: (1) Wife becomes Muslim, husband is non-Muslim: qadi presents Islam to husband; if he accepts, marriage continues; if he refuses, qadi separates them. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), this separation is talaq (divorce). (2) Husband becomes Muslim, wife is Zoroastrian: qadi presents Islam to her; if she accepts, marriage continues; if she refuses, qadi separates them. Here the separation is faskh (annulment), not talaq. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that in both cases it is faskh.

The practical benefit of considering it faskh is that the number of divorces is not reduced; if they remarry later, the husband retains full three divorces. If considered talaq, one talaq is used.

The passage then presents the inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafis hold that Islam must be presented to the non-Muslim spouse; Imam Shafi'i opposes this, arguing it violates the dhimma contract. The Hanafi response is that compulsory interference is prohibited, but voluntary invitation is not. They provide proof from a hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) did not separate Safwan and his wife until Safwan accepted Islam, and from actions of Umar (RA) separating couples when the husband refused Islam.

Finally, the author discusses the reasoning for Abu Yusuf's view: the separation occurs due to a cause involving both spouses, like one becoming owner of the other, which is faskh. The majority (tarafayn) respond that the husband's refusal to retain with kindness allows the qadi to act as his representative for divorce, hence it is talaq. This is analogous to cases of physical incapacity.

Key Terms
اباء عن الإسلام (ibā’ ‘an al-islām): Refusal to accept Islam after being invited; the act of rejecting the offer of Islam.
تفريق (tafrīq): Separation between spouses ordered by the qadi due to the spouse's refusal of Islam.
فسخ نکاح (faskh al-nikāḥ): Annulment of marriage; a dissolution that does not count towards the three divorces and does not reduce the number of available divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the nature of separation when a husband refuses to accept Islam after his wife has become Muslim?
A) Faskh (annulment)
B) Talaq (divorce)
C) It depends on whether consummation occurred
D) The marriage remains intact

Key Takeaway
The nature of separation due to refusal of Islam depends on which spouse refuses: if the husband refuses, it is talaq; if the wife refuses, it is faskh — a distinction with significant practical implications for the husband's future divorce rights.

Presenting Islam to the Zimmī Spouse Who Refuses Conversion
Explaining Hanafi ruling on presenting Islam to non-Muslim spouse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires presenting Islam to a zimmī spouse before separation, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Refusal of Islam after invitation, not the original conversion, is the legal cause for separation between spouses in Hanafi fiqh.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a critical point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: what to do when one spouse converts to Islam and the other remains a dhimmi. The Hanafi school insists that before any separation, the qadi must present Islam to the non-Muslim spouse. Why? Because the existing kufr did not prevent the marriage, so a new cause – the refusal to embrace Islam – is needed to dissolve it. Let's walk through the argument.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The qadi must present Islam to the non-Muslim spouse; separation occurs only upon refusal (ibā’ an al-islām).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that dhimmis should not be interfered with, so no presentation is required; separation is immediate upon conversion.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'is argue based on the inviolability of dhimmis under the dhimma pact, which prohibits interference.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis distinguish forced interference (prohibited) from optional invitation (permitted). Only forced interference is prohibited.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis require an active step by the qadi before separation; Shafi'is permit immediate separation upon conversion.

The Book of Marriage: Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume four. Obedience. The objectives of marriage cannot be a cause for the loss of such blessings. And the second scenario is also not possible, because the disbelief of 'he who remains upon his disbelief' is already present. That disbelief neither prevented the initial marriage nor caused the loss of the objectives of marriage (blessings). So besides these two, a third thing must exist that can be assigned as the cause. For this reason, the qadi presents Islam to the one who remains upon his disbelief. Then if he becomes Muslim, praise be to Allah, the objectives of marriage are achieved, and there is no need for separation. And if he refuses to accept Islam, then separation becomes established. So this refusal of Islam becomes the cause for the loss of the objectives of marriage, because refusal of Islam has the capacity to cause deprivation of blessing. And since separation is necessary for the loss of the objectives of marriage, whatever is the cause of the loss is also the cause of its necessary consequence, i.e., separation. Therefore, the Hanafis say that Islam will be presented to the one who remains upon his disbelief, so that his refusal of Islam can be made the cause of separation. As for Imam Shafi'i's statement that interference with dhimmis is prohibited, we say: forced interference is prohibited, but optional conversation with him is not prohibited. Our school is supported by this hadith narrated from Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri in the Muwatta: 'Indeed, the daughter of al-Walid ibn al-Mughirah was married to Safwan ibn Umayyah. She accepted Islam on the day of the Conquest, and her husband Safwan ibn Umayyah fled from Islam. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not separate him and his wife until Safwan became Muslim, and his wife remained with him by that marriage.' And Tahawi and Ibn al-Arabi mentioned that Umar separated between a Christian man and a Christian woman due to his refusal of Islam. And our companions mentioned that a man from Taghlib, his wife became Muslim while he was Christian. She raised the matter to Umar ibn al-Khattab. He said to him: 'Accept Islam, or I will separate between you two.' He refused, so he separated between them. From these hadiths, the presentation of Islam is established.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author explains the Hanafi ruling that when a non-Muslim spouse (dhimmi) remains upon his disbelief after the other spouse has converted, the qadi must invite him to Islam. This is because the existing disbelief of the non-Muslim spouse did not prevent the marriage initially, nor does it automatically destroy the objectives of marriage. A new cause is needed for separation, and that is the refusal to embrace Islam when invited. The author then addresses Imam Shafi'i's objection that interference with dhimmis is prohibited. The Hanafi response distinguishes between forced interference (which is prohibited) and optional invitation (which is permitted). The ruling is supported by a hadith from the Muwatta showing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not immediately separate Safwan and his wife; rather, he waited for Safwan's conversion. Also, actions of Caliph Umar (RA) are cited where he separated a couple after the husband refused Islam. Thus, the presentation of Islam is established as a prerequisite for separation.

Key Terms
اباء عن الاسلام (ibā’ an al-islām): The refusal to accept Islam after being invited, which is treated as the cause for separation between spouses when one has converted.
تعرض (ta‘arruḍ): Interference or molestation; in this context, forced interference with a dhimmi is prohibited.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Talaq or Faskh Upon Apostasy of One Spouse
Intra-Hanafi dispute on talaq vs faskh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) regarding the nature of separation when one spouse converts and the other refuses, and state the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
When one spouse converts and the other refuses, the separation is talaq—not annulment—because the qadi acts as the husband's proxy for divorce.

This lesson examines an internal Hanafi dispute over the legal classification of court-ordered separation when one spouse accepts Islam and the other refuses. Imam Abu Yusuf argued that such separation is an annulment (faskh), while the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) held it is a divorce (talaq). The difference has practical consequences for iddah, mahr, and remarriage. We will explore the reasoning behind each position and learn which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ikhtilaf
First, clearly state the two positions: Abu Yusuf says the separation is faskh (annulment); the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say it is talaq (divorce).
The dispute is about the nature of the separation, not its validity.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's dalil
Abu Yusuf analogizes to the case where one spouse becomes the owner of the other: the separation is faskh because the cause (ownership) involves both parties. He extends this to the apostasy case where both spouses contribute (one converts, one refuses).
The illa: a cause shared by both spouses results in faskh, not talaq.
3
Analyze the majority's dalil
The majority argue that the husband's refusal to convert means he has ceased to observe good conduct (imsaak bil ma'roof). The qadi therefore stands in his place to effect an honorable release (tasreeh), which is talaq. They analogize to cases of a husband with a severed penis or impotence.
The qadi's action is talaq because tasreeh is the husband's prerogative, and the qadi acts as his proxy.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that the separation is talaq. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah, and preferred by later Hanafi authorities like Al-Marghinani.
Abu Yusuf's view is a legitimate ikhtilaf but not followed for fatwa.
5
Apply the mahr implications
If the marriage was consummated, full mahr is due because consummation confirms the mahr. If not consummated, no mahr is due because the separation is attributed to the woman's refusal (she caused the dissolution).
This rule holds regardless of the talaq/faskh dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(It is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir) After finishing the discussion with Imam Shafi'i, they want to discuss the view of Abu Yusuf. Because he said that the separation in both cases is not talaq but rather annulment (naskh). The reason for Abu Yusuf's statement is that the separation occurred due to a cause in which both spouses share; that is, it is actualized from each of them. Meaning, one became Muslim and the other refused to accept Islam, then separation occurred. And every separation that occurs due to a cause in which both the man and woman share will not be talaq. For example, if one of the spouses becomes the owner of the other, the separation that occurs due to that is not talaq but rather annulment of marriage (faskh). The proof for the other view and the reason for the difference in both cases is that due to the refusal of Islam, the husband stopped observing the prescribed good conduct (imsaak bil ma'roof), although he was capable of observing it by accepting Islam. And the principle of Shariah is that if the husband stops observing good conduct, the qadi will stand in the husband's place for honorable release (tasreeh bil ihsaan). And tasreeh means talaq. Therefore, this separation by the qadi will be called talaq. Just as in the case of a man with severed penis (maqtoo' al-dhakar) and an impotent man, the qadi will separate upon the woman's request, and this separation is talaq. Similarly, here the separation from the husband's side is talaq. In any case, the woman is not eligible for talaq. Therefore, when she refuses Islam, the qadi cannot stand in her place for honorable release, because honorable release (talaq) from the woman's side is not conceivable. Then, when the qadi separated due to the woman's refusal to accept Islam, it is now to be seen whether the husband had consummated the marriage with her or not. If he did not consummate, then there is no mahr for the woman, because the separation occurred due to the woman's side and the mahr was not confirmed due to lack of consummation. So this resembles apostasy and the case of a woman who allows her husband's son to have power over herself (i.e., zina). A'udhu billah! So if it is after consummation, then for the woman, the full mahr is due because the mahr was confirmed by consummation. And if before consummation, then there is no mahr for her. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author introduces the view of Imam Abu Yusuf concerning the nature of the separation (firqah) when one spouse converts and the other refuses. Abu Yusuf holds that the separation is an annulment (naskh) of the marriage, not a divorce (talaq). His reasoning is that the cause for separation involves both spouses - the conversion of one and the refusal of the other. When a cause is shared by both parties, the resulting separation is deemed faskh, not talaq, analogous to the case where one spouse becomes the owner of the other, resulting in annulment. However, the author then presents the opposing view (which is the relied-upon Hanafi position) that the separation is indeed talaq. The proof is that the husband's refusal to accept Islam means he has failed to maintain good conduct (imsaak bil ma'roof). Since he could have observed this by converting, the qadi steps in to grant a release (tasreeh), which is a form of talaq. The author compares it to the case of a husband who is physically incapable of intercourse, where the qadi's separation is considered talaq. Finally, the passage discusses the implications for mahr: if the husband had not consummated the marriage, no mahr is due because the separation is attributed to the woman's refusal; if consummation occurred, full mahr is due because it becomes confirmed.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Annulment of marriage; in this context, Abu Yusuf uses it to mean dissolution of marriage without the incidence of talaq.
تسریح بالاحسان (tasreeh bil ihsaan): Honorable release, meaning divorce in a proper manner. The qadi may perform this on behalf of the husband.
امساک بالمعروف (imsaak bil ma'roof): Maintaining the marriage with kindness; a husband's duty to treat his wife well. Failure to do so allows the qadi to step in.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi view regarding the nature of separation when one spouse converts and the other refuses?
A) It is annulment (faskh)
B) It is divorce (talaq)
C) It is neither, but a new type of separation
D) It depends on which spouse converted

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, separation due to apostasy of one spouse is talaq, not annulment; the qadi executes it as the husband's proxy, and mahr depends on consummation.

Separation in Dar al-Harb After Conversion
Ruling on separation after conversion in Dar al-Harb with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for separation in Dar al-Harb when one spouse converts and explain the legal rationale (istihsan) substituting a condition for the impossible cause.

Core Idea
In Dar al-Harb, conversion alone does not end a marriage; separation requires waiting three menstruations as a condition.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario: when one spouse converts to Islam in enemy territory where no Islamic authority exists. The ruling requires a waiting period of three menstrual cycles (or three months) before separation is effective. This delay arises from a sophisticated legal analogy (istihsan) that substitutes a measurable condition for an impossible cause, ensuring corruption is removed without overstepping the limits of Islamic governance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Observe the two cases: a woman converting while husband is kafir, and a harbi man converting while wife is Majusiyyah. Recognize that in both, the non-Muslim spouse remains unconverted.
These are the only possibilities in the text.
2
State the ruling precisely
The passage says separation does not occur immediately; it occurs after the wife has experienced three menstruations (or if she does not menstruate, after three months). After that, she becomes separated (bainuna).
Note that separation is automatic after the condition is met, not due to a pronouncement.
3
Trace the rationale
The text gives two reasons: (1) Islam is not a cause for separation; the cause is the non-Muslim spouse's refusal to accept Islam. (2) In Dar al-Harb, there is no qadi to present Islam to the kafir (presentation is impossible). So separation is needed to remove corruption (zina), but since the cause is absent, they substitute a condition: the passage of three menstruations.
This substitution is called 'iqamat al-shart maqam al-sabab'.
4
Examine the analogy (istihsan)
The text analogizes to 'digging a well' (hafr al-bi'r). In that case, a condition (e.g., time) stands in place of the actual cause (the well being full). Here, the passage of three menstruations stands in place of the presentation of Islam and the consequent refusal.
This is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) based on removing hardship.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The text mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i distinguishes between pre- and post-consummation marriages in Dar al-Islam. In Dar al-Harb, the Hanafi view holds no such distinction—the ruling is uniform. The passage hints that Shafi'i may apply a similar distinction in Dar al-Harb, but the Hanafi position is clear.
We will explore this in the al-mukhtalaf fih block.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the scenario when one spouse converts to Islam in Dar al-Harb (the abode of war) where no Islamic authority exists. The ruling is that separation does not occur immediately upon conversion; rather, it occurs after three menstrual cycles (or three months for non-menstruating women). This is because Islam itself is not a cause for separation; the actual cause is refusal to accept Islam, but in Dar al-Harb, there is no qadi to present Islam to the non-Muslim spouse. To prevent ongoing marital corruption, the Hanafis have made the passage of three menstruations a condition that substitutes for the cause. This is analogous to the case of digging a well where a condition is made to stand in place of the actual cause. The passage also notes that Imam Shafi'i distinguishes between consummated and non-consummated marriages in Dar al-Islam, but in Dar al-Harb, there is no such distinction in the Hanafi view. The explanation clarifies a grammatical inversion in the Arabic text. The passage cuts off, but the key ruling is clear.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory not under Muslim rule, where Islamic law is not enforced and Muslim authority is absent.
حفر البير (ḥafr al-bi’r): Digging a well; used as analogy where a condition (like passing of time) substitutes for a cause in legal rulings.
عرض اسلام علی الکافر (‘arḍ al-islām ‘alā al-kāfir): Presenting Islam to the disbeliever; the correct phrase understood from the text after considering inversion (qalb).

Condition for Separation in Dar al-Harb: The Three Haid Requirement
Explains condition of three haid for separation via qiyas and refutes Shafi'i distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that three menstrual periods are a condition for separation in Dar al-Harb for both consummated and unconsummated spouses, and state the qiyas reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
In Dar al-Harb, the condition of three haid substitutes for the cause of separation to prevent the evil of Muslim under kafir authority.

This passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya addresses a key scenario: when one spouse becomes Muslim in Dar al-Harb. For separation to occur, the Hanafi school requires a waiting period of three haid (or three months) regardless of consummation. The author uses a powerful analogy with digging a well to justify this ruling, and then contrasts it with the Shafi'i view, explaining that these three periods are for separation, not 'iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
The need for separation when one spouse converts in Dar al-Harb because Islam has no authority there. The separation is wajib to prevent a Muslim from being under a kafir's authority.
2
Analyze the cause and condition
The actual cause of separation is the spouse's refusal to accept Islam (aba' an al-Islam). However, this cause is a legal excuse, so the jurists make the condition (three haid) stand in place of the cause.
3
Understand the qiyas analogy
The author compares this to a well-digger: the condition (digging) is substituted for the cause (falling) to establish liability. Similarly, three haid substitute for the refusal to convert.
Same illa: condition stands in place of cause.
4
State the Hanafi position
Both madkhul biha and ghayr madkhul biha require three haid; no distinction.
Zahir al-Riwayah position.
5
Contrast with Shafi'i and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i differentiates based on consummation, analogizing to Dar al-Islam. The Hanafi response: these three haid are for separation, not 'iddah, so the analogy fails.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Shafi'is allow immediate separation for ghayr madkhul; Hanafis require three haid.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

و اذا وقعت الفرقة والمرأة حربية فلاعدة عليها و ان كانت هى المسلمة فكذلك عند ابي حنيفة خلافالهما وسيأتيك ان شاء الله واذا اسلم زوج الكتابية فهما على نكاحهما لانه يصح النكاح بينهما ابتداء فلان يبقى اولى
ترجمہ اور جب فرقت واقع ہوئی اور حال یہ ہے کہ عورت حربیہ ہے تو ( بالا جماع ) عورت پر عدت نہیں ۔ اور اگر وہ ( حربیہ ) مسلمان ہوئی تو ایسا ہی ہے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اختلاف ہے صاحبین کا اور عنقریب آئے گا انشاء اللہ ۔ اور جب کتابیہ کا شوہر مسلمان ہو گیا تو وہ دونوں اپنے نکاح پر ( باقی ) رہیں گے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں ابتداء نکاح صحیح ہے۔ پس بدرجہ اولی باقی رہے گا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب تین حیض گذرنے کے بعد فرقت واقع ہوئی اور عورت حربیہ ہے اسلام نہیں لائی صرف اس کا بعد شو هر مسلمان ہوا ہے تو بالاجماع حربیہ عورت پر عدت واجب نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ حکم شرع اس کے حق میں ثابت ہی نہیں ہے اور اگر حربیہ مسلمان ہوگئی اور اس کا شو ہر حربی کافر ہی رہا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر بھی عدت واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس پر عدت واجب ہوگی ۔ شمس الائمہ نے ایسا ہی ذکر کیا اور یہ اختلاف انشاء اللہ عنقریب آجائے گا۔ اور اگر کتابیہ کا شوہر مسلمان ہو گیا تو وہ دونوں اپنے سابقہ نکاح پر باقی رہیں گے۔ کیونکہ مسلمان مرد اور کتابیہ عورت کے درمیان ابتداء نکاح صحیح ہے۔ لہذا ابقاء بدرجہ اولیٰ صحیح رہے گا۔ اسلئے کہ بقاء ابتداء سے آسان ہے۔
Islam does not have guardianship. Therefore, in Dar al-Harb, presenting Islam to a disbeliever is also impossible. And for the removal of corruption, separation must occur. So when the cause of separation—i.e., refusal of Islam—was deemed an excuse, we made the condition of separation (passage of three menstrual periods if among those who menstruate, or three months if not) stand in place of the cause of separation, like in the case of digging a well. The case is that a man dug a well in a public road or in the property of another. Then a person or animal fell into it and died, so the digger is liable. Because the cause of falling is the killer of the one who falls, but it cannot become the cause of falling, since it is natural and involves no transgression. The cause of falling is walking, but making walking the cause is impossible because walking on the road is permissible. Thus, the condition of falling (digging the well) is made to stand in place of the cause, and the digger is held liable. Similarly, here the condition of separation stands in place of the cause of separation.
According to us, there is no difference between a woman who has been consummated and one who has not. For both, the condition for separation is the passage of three menstrual periods. However, Imam al-Shafi'i gives the same detail as his view in Dar al-Islam, i.e., in Dar al-Harb, if one of the spouses converts before consummation, separation occurs immediately; if after consummation, separation occurs after three menstrual periods. But we say to Imam al-Shafi'i with respect: These three menstrual periods are not for 'iddah; rather, they are for separation. So in this, the consummated and unconsummated are equal, and Allah knows best. (Mu'ini Sharh Hidayah) When separation has occurred and the woman is harbiyyah, there is no 'iddah upon her. If she is a Muslim woman, the same ruling applies. Statements of jurists: Wa idha waqa'at al-furqah wa al-mar'atu harbiyyahun fala 'iddata 'alayha. Wa in kanat hiya al-muslimatu fa kadhalika 'inda Abi Hanifah khilafan lahumah. Wa sa ya'tika in sha' Allah. Wa idha aslama zawju al-kitabiyyahi fahuma 'ala nikahihima li'annahu yasihhu al-nikahu baynahuma ibtida'an falan yabqa awla. Translation: And when separation occurs and the woman is harbiyyah, upon her is no 'iddah by consensus. And if she (the harbiyyah) becomes Muslim, then similarly according to Abu Hanifah—there is disagreement of the two Sahibayn—and it will come to you soon, in sha' Allah. And when the husband of a Kitabiyyah becomes Muslim, they both remain upon their marriage, because marriage between them is valid initially, so it is more fitting that it remain. Explanation: The scenario is that when separation occurs after three menstrual periods and the woman is harbiyyah, she has not accepted Islam, only her husband became Muslim. Then by consensus, there is no 'iddah upon the harbiyyah woman, because the rule of Shari'ah is not established for her. And if the harbiyyah woman becomes Muslim and her husband remains a harbi disbeliever, then according to Imam Abu Hanifah, there is no 'iddah upon her either. And according to the two Sahibayn, 'iddah would be obligatory upon her. Shams al-A'imma mentioned this. And if the husband of a Kitabiyyah becomes Muslim, they both remain on their previous marriage, because marriage between a Muslim man and a Kitabiyyah woman is valid initially, so its continuation is even more valid, because continuation is easier than initiation.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn from Al-Hidayah. It begins by establishing the legal issue: when a non-Muslim spouse becomes Muslim in Dar al-Harb, separation must occur to prevent the evil of a Muslim being under the authority of a non-Muslim. Since the actual cause of separation (the spouse's refusal to accept Islam) is a legal excuse, the Hanafi jurists have made the condition of separation—the passage of three menstrual periods (or three months for non-menstruating women)—stand in place of that cause. This is analogous to the case of digging a well on public property: the immediate cause of death is the fall, but since walking (the true cause) is permissible, liability is placed on the digger as the condition. Thus, the condition (digging) substitutes for the cause. The author then clarifies the Hanafi position: there is no distinction between a consummated and unconsummated spouse; both require three menstrual periods for separation. Imam al-Shafi'i differentiates based on consummation, but the Hanafis respond that these three periods are not for 'iddah but solely for separation, making the ruling uniform. After separation, if the woman is harbiyyah (a non-Muslim from Dar al-Harb), there is no 'iddah upon her by consensus. If she becomes Muslim while remaining in Dar al-Harb (her husband still harbi), Abu Hanifa holds no 'iddah, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that 'iddah is obligatory. The Sahibayn's view is a minority opinion; the mufta bihi (relied upon view) is Abu Hanifa's. Finally, if a husband of a Kitabiyyah (Jewish or Christian woman) becomes Muslim, the marriage remains valid because such a marriage is permissible initially, and continuation is even easier than initiation.

Key Terms
فرقت (furqah): Legal separation between spouses due to difference of religion in Dar al-Harb.
حیض (hayd): Menstrual period used as a time marker for the condition of separation.
عدت ('iddah): Waiting period after separation or divorce; not applicable here as the condition is for separation, not 'iddah.
مدخول بہا (madkhul biha): A woman with whom marriage was consummated.
غیر مدخول بہا (ghayr madkhul biha): A woman with whom marriage was not consummated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for separation when one spouse converts to Islam in Dar al-Harb?
A) Immediate separation regardless of consummation
B) Passage of three menstrual periods (or three months) for both consummated and unconsummated spouses
C) Passage of three menstrual periods only if consummated
D) Passage of one menstrual period

Key Takeaway
The condition of three haid for separation in Dar al-Harb is a Hanafi requirement for both consummated and unconsummated spouses, justified by qiyas where the condition substitutes for the cause.

Ruling on 'Iddah for a Harbiyyah Woman After Separation
States the ruling on 'iddah for harbiyyah after separation and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'iddah for a harbiyyah woman after separation and identify the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
No 'iddah for harbiyyah after separation; if she converts, Abu Hanifa says no 'iddah, Sahibayn say wajib.

After the condition of three haid is fulfilled and separation occurs, the question of 'iddah arises. This passage addresses two scenarios: when the woman is a harbiyyah (non-Muslim from Dar al-Harb) and when she converts to Islam. By consensus, the harbiyyah does not observe 'iddah because Islamic rulings do not apply to her. However, if she becomes Muslim, a dispute arises between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. This lesson unpacks that ikhtilaf and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Confirm separation has occurred
The separation is effective after three haid; now the focus is on 'iddah.
2
Identify the woman's status
Is she a harbiyyah (non-Muslim) or has she converted? If harbiyyah, consensus is clear.
3
Apply the consensus ruling
If harbiyyah without conversion, no 'iddah because Islamic law is not established for her.
Consensus of all Hanafi authorities.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
If she converts, Abu Hanifa: no 'iddah; Sahibayn: 'iddah wajib. The reasoning: Sahibayn consider that Islamic rulings apply to her upon conversion, but Abu Hanifa holds that the separation occurred while she was a harbiyyah, so 'iddah is not established.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's, as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma. Therefore, a converting harbiyyah woman does not need to observe 'iddah.

اسلام کو ولایت بھی حاصل نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے دار الحرب میں کافر پر اسلام پیش کرنا بھی محال ہے۔ اور فساد دور کرنے کیلئے فرقت کا ہونا بھی ضروری ہے۔ (فساد مسلمان کا کافر کے تحت ہونا ) پس جب سبب فرقت یعنی اباء عن الاسلام کا مقدر مانا عذر ہو گیا تو ہم نے فرقت کی شرط ( تین حیض کا گذرنا اگر ذوات الحیض میں سے ہے یا تین ماہ کا گذر نا اگر ذوات الحیض میں سے نہیں ہے ) کو سبب فرقت کے قائم مقام بنا دیا جیسا کہ کنواں کھودنے میں ۔ صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے عام راستہ یا ملک غیر میں کنواں کھود دیا ۔ پھر اس میں آدمی یا جانور گر کر مر گیا تو کھودنے والا ضامن ہے اسلئے کہ کنویں میں گرنے کی علت گرنے والے کا قتل اور بوجھ ہے لیکن نقل گرنے کا سبب نہیں بن سکتا۔ کیونکہ یہ امر طبعی ہے اس میں کوئی تعدی نہیں۔ اور گرنے کا سبب مشی (چلنا) ہے۔ مگر مشی کو بھی سبب بنانا محال ہے۔ کیونکہ راستہ میں چلنا مباح ہے۔ لہذا گرنے کی شرط ( کنواں کھودنا ) کو سبب کے قائم مقام بنا کر صاحب شرط یعنی کنواں کھودنے والے کو ضامن قرار دے دیا۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی فرقت کی شرط سبب فرقت کے قائم مقام ہے۔
ہمارے نزدیک مدخول بہا اور غیر مدخول بہا میں کوئی فرق نہیں دونوں کی فرقت کیلئے تین حیض گذار نا شرط ہے۔ البتہ امام شافعی ویسی ہی تفصیل کرتے ہیں جیسے ان کا قول دار السلام میں گذرا یعنی دار الحرب میں اگر احد الزوجین کا اسلام دخول سے پہلے ہے تو فرقت فی الحال واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر دخول کے بعد ہے تو تین حیض گذرنے کے بعد فرقت واقع ہوگی ۔ لیکن ہم امام شافعی سے دست بستہ عرض کرتے ہیں کہ حضرت یہ تین حیض عدت کیلئے نہیں ہیں۔ بلکہ فرقت کیلئے ہیں۔ لہذا اس میں مدخول بہا اور غیر مدخول بہا دونوں برابر ہیں واللہ اعلم ۔ (معینی شرح ہدایہ) فرقت واقع ہو گئی اور عورت حربیہ ہے اس پر عدت نہیں، مسلمان عورت کا بھی یہی حکم ہے ، اقوال فقہاء
و اذا وقعت الفرقة والمرأة حربية فلاعدة عليها و ان كانت هى المسلمة فكذلك عند ابي حنيفة خلافالهما وسيأتيك ان شاء الله واذا اسلم زوج الكتابية فهما على نكاحهما لانه يصح النكاح بينهما ابتداء فلان يبقى اولى
ترجمہ اور جب فرقت واقع ہوئی اور حال یہ ہے کہ عورت حربیہ ہے تو ( بالا جماع ) عورت پر عدت نہیں ۔ اور اگر وہ ( حربیہ ) مسلمان ہوئی تو ایسا ہی ہے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اختلاف ہے صاحبین کا اور عنقریب آئے گا انشاء اللہ ۔ اور جب کتابیہ کا شوہر مسلمان ہو گیا تو وہ دونوں اپنے نکاح پر ( باقی ) رہیں گے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں ابتداء نکاح صحیح ہے۔ پس بدرجہ اولی باقی رہے گا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب تین حیض گذرنے کے بعد فرقت واقع ہوئی اور عورت حربیہ ہے اسلام نہیں لائی صرف اس کا بعد شو هر مسلمان ہوا ہے تو بالاجماع حربیہ عورت پر عدت واجب نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ حکم شرع اس کے حق میں ثابت ہی نہیں ہے اور اگر حربیہ مسلمان ہوگئی اور اس کا شو ہر حربی کافر ہی رہا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر بھی عدت واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس پر عدت واجب ہوگی ۔ شمس الائمہ نے ایسا ہی ذکر کیا اور یہ اختلاف انشاء اللہ عنقریب آجائے گا۔ اور اگر کتابیہ کا شوہر مسلمان ہو گیا تو وہ دونوں اپنے سابقہ نکاح پر باقی رہیں گے۔ کیونکہ مسلمان مرد اور کتابیہ عورت کے درمیان ابتداء نکاح صحیح ہے۔ لہذا ابقاء بدرجہ اولیٰ صحیح رہے گا۔ اسلئے کہ بقاء ابتداء سے آسان ہے۔
Islam does not have guardianship. Therefore, in Dar al-Harb, presenting Islam to a disbeliever is also impossible. And for the removal of corruption, separation must occur. So when the cause of separation—i.e., refusal of Islam—was deemed an excuse, we made the condition of separation (passage of three menstrual periods if among those who menstruate, or three months if not) stand in place of the cause of separation, like in the case of digging a well. The case is that a man dug a well in a public road or in the property of another. Then a person or animal fell into it and died, so the digger is liable. Because the cause of falling is the killer of the one who falls, but it cannot become the cause of falling, since it is natural and involves no transgression. The cause of falling is walking, but making walking the cause is impossible because walking on the road is permissible. Thus, the condition of falling (digging the well) is made to stand in place of the cause, and the digger is held liable. Similarly, here the condition of separation stands in place of the cause of separation.
According to us, there is no difference between a woman who has been consummated and one who has not. For both, the condition for separation is the passage of three menstrual periods. However, Imam al-Shafi'i gives the same detail as his view in Dar al-Islam, i.e., in Dar al-Harb, if one of the spouses converts before consummation, separation occurs immediately; if after consummation, separation occurs after three menstrual periods. But we say to Imam al-Shafi'i with respect: These three menstrual periods are not for 'iddah; rather, they are for separation. So in this, the consummated and unconsummated are equal, and Allah knows best. (Mu'ini Sharh Hidayah) When separation has occurred and the woman is harbiyyah, there is no 'iddah upon her. If she is a Muslim woman, the same ruling applies. Statements of jurists: Wa idha waqa'at al-furqah wa al-mar'atu harbiyyahun fala 'iddata 'alayha. Wa in kanat hiya al-muslimatu fa kadhalika 'inda Abi Hanifah khilafan lahumah. Wa sa ya'tika in sha' Allah. Wa idha aslama zawju al-kitabiyyahi fahuma 'ala nikahihima li'annahu yasihhu al-nikahu baynahuma ibtida'an falan yabqa awla. Translation: And when separation occurs and the woman is harbiyyah, upon her is no 'iddah by consensus. And if she (the harbiyyah) becomes Muslim, then similarly according to Abu Hanifah—there is disagreement of the two Sahibayn—and it will come to you soon, in sha' Allah. And when the husband of a Kitabiyyah becomes Muslim, they both remain upon their marriage, because marriage between them is valid initially, so it is more fitting that it remain. Explanation: The scenario is that when separation occurs after three menstrual periods and the woman is harbiyyah, she has not accepted Islam, only her husband became Muslim. Then by consensus, there is no 'iddah upon the harbiyyah woman, because the rule of Shari'ah is not established for her. And if the harbiyyah woman becomes Muslim and her husband remains a harbi disbeliever, then according to Imam Abu Hanifah, there is no 'iddah upon her either. And according to the two Sahibayn, 'iddah would be obligatory upon her. Shams al-A'imma mentioned this. And if the husband of a Kitabiyyah becomes Muslim, they both remain on their previous marriage, because marriage between a Muslim man and a Kitabiyyah woman is valid initially, so its continuation is even more valid, because continuation is easier than initiation.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn from Al-Hidayah. It begins by establishing the legal issue: when a non-Muslim spouse becomes Muslim in Dar al-Harb, separation must occur to prevent the evil of a Muslim being under the authority of a non-Muslim. Since the actual cause of separation (the spouse's refusal to accept Islam) is a legal excuse, the Hanafi jurists have made the condition of separation—the passage of three menstrual periods (or three months for non-menstruating women)—stand in place of that cause. This is analogous to the case of digging a well on public property: the immediate cause of death is the fall, but since walking (the true cause) is permissible, liability is placed on the digger as the condition. Thus, the condition (digging) substitutes for the cause. The author then clarifies the Hanafi position: there is no distinction between a consummated and unconsummated spouse; both require three menstrual periods for separation. Imam al-Shafi'i differentiates based on consummation, but the Hanafis respond that these three periods are not for 'iddah but solely for separation, making the ruling uniform. After separation, if the woman is harbiyyah (a non-Muslim from Dar al-Harb), there is no 'iddah upon her by consensus. If she becomes Muslim while remaining in Dar al-Harb (her husband still harbi), Abu Hanifa holds no 'iddah, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that 'iddah is obligatory. The Sahibayn's view is a minority opinion; the mufta bihi (relied upon view) is Abu Hanifa's. Finally, if a husband of a Kitabiyyah (Jewish or Christian woman) becomes Muslim, the marriage remains valid because such a marriage is permissible initially, and continuation is even easier than initiation.

Key Terms
حربیہ (harbiyyah): A woman from Dar al-Harb who is not a Muslim and not a dhimmi.
عدت ('iddah): Waiting period after separation or divorce; not required for harbiyyah woman after furqah.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the ruling on 'iddah for a harbiyyah woman who converts to Islam after separation?
A) 'Iddah is wajib because conversion makes her a Muslim
B) No 'iddah, because the separation occurred while she was a harbiyyah
C) 'Iddah is wajib only if she converted before the separation
D) No 'iddah, because she never consummated the marriage

Key Takeaway
A harbiyyah woman has no 'iddah after separation by consensus; if she converts, Abu Hanifa maintains no 'iddah, which is the mufta bihi.

Nikah — Marriage
