Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Apostasy on Marriage: Talaq or Faskh?
Dispute on whether riddah causes talaq or faskh, comparing with refusal to accept Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi positions on riddah separation and explain why Abu Hanifa considers it faskh rather than talaq.

Core Idea
Apostasy nullifies marriage because it removes inviolability; refusal to accept Islam does not.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a crucial intra-Hanafi debate on whether apostasy of a spouse dissolves the marriage as talaq or as faskh. The issue turns on whether apostasy is inherently contrary to marriage, unlike the refusal to accept Islam. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Hanafi theory of marriage inviolability and the limits of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi positions
State the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding whether riddah causes talaq or faskh.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold faskh; Muhammad has two narrations.
2
Examine Imam Muhammad's analogy
Muhammad analogizes riddah to iba' (refusal to accept Islam), where the judge effects talaq. Explain the commonality he sees.
He argues both involve husband refraining from keeping with kindness.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's distinction
Abu Hanifa distinguishes riddah from iba' because riddah makes life and property permissible, directly contradicting marriage. Iba' does not.
This distinction renders the analogy invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).
4
Understand the judicial decree issue
Separation due to iba' requires a judge's decree; riddah does not, because it is inherently nullifying, like mahramiyyah.
This practical difference affects iddah and inheritance.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is faskh for both spouses, without need for a judge's order, as supported by Al-Hidayah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اسلام لانے سے انکار کرناوہ اپنی اصلی حالت کفر پر رہنا چاہتا ہے اسلئے ذمی بنارہا۔لہذا اس کا خون مباح نہیں ہوا۔ اس وجہ سے اباء عن الاسلام منافی نکاح نہیں ہے۔ اور ردت منافی نکاح ہے۔ پس ردت کو اباء عن الاسلام پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اباء عن الاسلام کی وجہ سے شوہر امساک بالمعروف سے رک گیا پس تسریح بالاحسان واجب ہوگا۔ اور تسریح بالاحسان نام ہے طلاق کا اس وجہ سے اباء عن الاسلام کی وجہ سے تفریق کو طلاق قرار دیا گیا۔ اور چونکہ ردت منافی نکاح ہے اور اباء عن الاسلام منافی نکاح نہیں ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے اباء عن الاسلام کی وجہ سے فرقت قضاء قاضی پر موقوف رہے گی ۔ کیونکہ اباء عن الاسلام منافی نہیں ہے اور امداد کی وجہ سے فرقت قضاء قاضی پر موقوف نہیں رہے گی۔ کیونکہ منافی کا حکم قضاء پر موقوف نہیں رہتا جیسے محرمیت کی وجہ سے فرقت قضاء پر موقوف نہیں ہوتی۔
In the Book of Marriage it was said: Ibn Abi Layla said that from one of the spouses becoming apostate, separation does not occur, neither before consummation nor after. Rather the apostate will be asked to repent; if he repents, then praise be to God, she is his wife, the previous marriage remains; and if he dies in apostasy or is killed, his wife inherits from him. In any case, the separation that occurs due to apostasy: according to the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), this separation is not divorce but dissolution (faskh); and according to Imam Muhammad (in a narration), if the apostasy is from the husband, then this separation is divorce, otherwise not. Imam Muhammad analogizes the husband's apostasy to the husband's refusal to accept Islam (iba' an al-Islam). That is, if the wife becomes Muslim and the husband refuses to accept Islam, that is a divorce from the husband's side. Similarly, the husband's apostasy is a divorce from the husband's side. The commonality between the analogized case and the analogue is what we have explained: just as when the husband refuses to accept Islam, he refrains from keeping [the wife] with kindness (imsak bi'l-ma'ruf) while he was able to do so, so the judge stands in his place and effects separation with kindness (tasrih bi'l-ihsan), and this separation is divorce. Similarly, due to apostasy, the husband refrains from keeping with kindness, so the judge stands in his place. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that which has passed in the case of refusal: the separation occurred due to a cause in which both spouses share, and divorce is only from the husband's side—the wife has no part in it. Thus the separation due to apostasy is not divorce but annulment. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguished between refusal and apostasy. Thus the separation due to the husband's refusal to accept Islam is considered divorce, while the separation due to apostasy is not considered divorce. The reason for the difference is that apostasy is contrary to marriage because apostasy is contrary to the inviolability of life and property. Thus the life and property of an apostate are permissible; if someone kills him, no retaliation or blood money is obligatory; and the apostate's ownership and marriage become void. As for divorce, it is not contrary to marriage, because divorce lifts the marriage after its existence. That is why if the husband wants to remarry after divorce, he can. So the conclusion is that divorce is not contrary to marriage, while becoming an apostate is contrary to marriage, so making apostasy a divorce is impossible. In contrast, refusing to accept Islam means he wants to remain in his original state of disbelief, so he becomes a dhimmi, thus his blood is not permissible. Therefore refusal is not contrary to marriage, while apostasy is contrary to marriage. So analogizing apostasy to refusal is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). The author of al-Hidayah said: Due to refusal, the husband refrains from keeping with kindness, so beautiful release becomes obligatory. Beautiful release is the name for divorce; because of this, the separation due to refusal is considered divorce. And since apostasy is contrary to marriage and refusal is not contrary, therefore the separation due to refusal will be dependent on the judge's ruling, because refusal is not contrary, while the separation due to apostasy is not dependent on the judge's ruling, because the ruling of a contradictory matter does not depend on judgement, just as separation due to a prohibited relationship (mahramiyyah) does not depend on judgement.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the nature of separation (firqah) caused by apostasy (riddah) of one spouse. The author begins by presenting the view of Ibn Abi Layla (a non-Hanafi scholar) who holds that apostasy does not cause separation at all; rather the apostate is called to repentance, and if he dies or is killed in apostasy, the marriage persists for inheritance purposes. The Hanafi school does not accept this. Within the Hanafi school, there are three positions: (1) The Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, in one narration) hold that the separation is faskh (annulment), not talaq. (2) Imam Muhammad (in another narration) holds that if the husband apostatizes, the separation is talaq, because he analogizes it to the case where the husband refuses to accept Islam (iba' an al-Islam). In that case, the judge dissolves the marriage by talaq, so similar here. (3) Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between the two: refusal means the husband refuses to become Muslim but his blood is protected, so it is not contrary to the marriage bond; he can still perform the duties of marriage, so judicial separation is required and it is considered talaq. Apostasy, however, makes him mubah al-dam (life permissible), nullifies his ownership, and is directly antithetical to the marriage bond; hence separation occurs without judicial decree and is faskh, not talaq. The author of al-Hidayah endorses Abu Hanifa's distinction, emphasizing that qiyas (analogy) between riddah and iba' is qiyas ma'a al-fariq (invalid analogy due to a significant difference). The final point distinguishes that separation due to iba' requires a judge's decree because iba' is not inherently nullifying, whereas riddah nullifies directly like mahramiyyah (close kinship) which also dissolves marriage without a judge's order.

Key Terms
ردت (riddah): Apostasy from Islam by word or deed.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract due to a defect or subsequent event, not a revocable divorce.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An invalid analogy because the effective cause in the original case differs from the new case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, is the separation caused by a husband's apostasy considered talaq or faskh?
A) Talaq
B) Faskh
C) Neither, marriage remains
D) Depends on whether the wife also apostatizes

Key Takeaway
The separation caused by apostasy is faskh, not talaq, because apostasy is inherently contrary to the marriage bond, unlike refusal to accept Islam.

Nikah — Marriage

Mahr, Nafaqah, and Joint Apostasy
Rulings on mahr/nafaqah and joint apostasy with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on mahr and nafaqah when either spouse apostatizes, and apply the istihsan-based ruling for joint apostasy using the incident of Banu Hanifah.

Core Idea
Joint apostasy with simultaneous return preserves the marriage by istihsan, based on Companions' ijma'.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi financial consequences when one spouse apostatizes, and then delves into a unique case: if both apostatize together and both return together, the marriage stands. This ruling is not based on strict analogy (qiyas) but on juristic preference (istihsan) grounded in the historical precedent of Banu Hanifah. Understanding this case reveals how Hanafi scholars prioritize consensus (ijma') over analogical reasoning when a stronger source intervenes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios and rulings for single apostasy
Read the first part of the passage: specify the financial consequences for husband apostasy (with/without consummation) and wife apostasy (with/without consummation). Note the key difference: the apostatizing wife is considered nashizah and loses maintenance.
Focus on the condition of consummation and which party caused the separation.
2
Locate the controversial joint apostasy ruling
Find where the passage says both apostatize and return together. Identify the Hanafi position (marriage valid by istihsan) and the opposing view of Imam Zufar (marriage invalid by qiyas).
This is the core ruling_with_proof section.
3
Trace the Hanafi proof: the hadith of Banu Hanifah
Examine the cited hadith: Banu Hanifah apostatized, then returned to Islam, and the Companions did not order renewal of marriages. This incident is used as proof of ijma'.
Understand how the Companions' silence is interpreted as consensus that the marriages remained valid.
4
Analyze the opposing qiyas argument
Imam Zufar (and other schools) argue: if one apostate dissolves the marriage, then two apostates also dissolve it because each individual's apostasy is present. This is qiyas on the single-apostasy rule.
The dispute is between istihsan (based on specific incident) and qiyas (general analogy).
5
Evaluate the tarjih: why istihsan prevails
The Hanafi response: the precise timing of the Banu Hanifah apostasy is unknown, so we assume simultaneity. The Companions' ijma' overrides qiyas. Thus, if both apostatize and both return, no renewal needed. If only one returns, the marriage dissolves due to the other's persistence.
This step shows the hierarchical reasoning: ijma' > qiyas, leading to istihsan.

Then if the husband apostatizes and has consummated the marriage, then the wife is entitled to the full mahr and also the maintenance during the 'iddah. And if he has not consummated, then the wife gets half the mahr. And if the wife apostatizes and he has consummated, then the wife is entitled to the full mahr, but the maintenance during 'iddah is not obligatory because the separation came from the wife's side, so she is considered nashizah (disobedient), and a nashizah does not receive maintenance. And if he has not consummated, then she gets neither mahr nor maintenance. When both spouses apostatize together and then both become Muslim together, the marriage remains intact – this is by istihsan. Imam Zufar said it becomes invalid because the apostasy of one is contrary to marriage, and in their joint apostasy the apostasy of one is found. Our proof is the hadith that Banu Hanifah apostatized and then became Muslim, and the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them all) did not order them to renew the marriages, and their apostasy occurred together due to the history being unknown. And if one of them becomes Muslim after apostasy, the marriage between them becomes corrupt due to the other's persistence upon apostasy, because it is contrary just like the initial apostasy. Translation: And when both together apostatize and then together both become Muslim, then both are upon their marriage, by istihsan. Imam Zufar said it becomes invalid because the apostasy of one of them is contrary to marriage, and in their joint apostasy the apostasy of one is present. Our proof is the hadith that Banu Hanifah apostatized and then became Muslim, and the Companions did not order them to renew the marriages. And their apostasy occurred together due to the history being unknown. And if after apostasy one of them becomes Muslim, the marriage between them becomes corrupt due to the other's persistence upon apostasy, because that persistence is contrary just like the initial apostasy. Explanation: When both spouses apostatize together and then both become Muslim together, they will remain on their marriage. There is no need to renew the marriage. This is by istihsan. Imam Zufar said that in this case the marriage becomes invalid; this is by qiyas. Those who agree with him are Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad. Imam Zufar's proof is that when the apostasy of one is contrary to marriage, then the apostasy of both is, to a greater degree, contrary to marriage, because in the apostasy of two, the apostasy of one is also found. Our proof (and this is the basis of istihsan) is the hadith: that Banu Hanifah, which is a small tribe among the people of Musaylimah the Liar, these people apostatized due to refusing Zakat. Then the Caliph of the Muslims, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, sent an army of Companions to them, and they all became Muslim. But the Companions did not order them to renew the marriages. All the Companions agreed upon this. Hence there was ijma' of the Companions, and because of ijma', qiyas is abandoned. But if someone objects that their apostasy was not simultaneous, so how can this incident be used as evidence? The answer is that when the precedence and lateness are unknown in history, it will be assumed that they all apostatized simultaneously. And if after apostasy one of them becomes Muslim, the marriage between them becomes corrupt, i.e., separation occurs due to the other's persistence upon apostasy, because persistence upon apostasy is just like initial apostasy in being contrary to marriage.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi rulings on financial consequences of apostasy by one spouse, and then discusses the special case where both apostatize together. The first part: If the husband apostatizes and consummation occurred, the wife gets full mahr and 'iddah maintenance. If no consummation, half mahr. If the wife apostatizes and consummation occurred, she gets full mahr but no 'iddah maintenance because she is the causing party (nashizah). If no consummation, she gets neither mahr nor maintenance. This follows from the principle that the separation is from her side. Then the author shifts to the case of both apostatizing together. Istihsan (juristic preference) rules that the marriage remains valid because of the incident of Banu Hanifah: when they apostatized and later returned to Islam, the Companions did not order renewal of marriages. This establishes an ijma' that simultaneous apostasy does not dissolve the marriage if both return together. Imam Zufar (and the other three Sunni imams) hold that the marriage is invalidated because even if both apostatize, the effect is that each spouse's apostasy is present, and one person's apostasy alone would dissolve the marriage. But the Hanafi response relies on the hadith and the fact that the exact timing is unknown; we assume simultaneity. If one returns to Islam before the other, then the marriage is dissolved because the other's persistence on apostasy acts like the initial apostasy itself. The commentary explains that the proof is the ijma' of the Companions, which overrides qiyas.

Key Terms
ناشزہ (nashizah): A wife who is disobedient or causes separation; here the wife who apostatizes is considered nashizah, so she loses her right to maintenance during 'iddah.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas in favour of a stronger evidence (here, hadith and ijma).
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the Companions on not requiring renewal of marriages for Banu Hanifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If both spouses apostatize together and then both return to Islam together, what is the Hanafi ruling on their marriage?
A) The marriage is automatically dissolved and they must remarry
B) The marriage remains valid without renewal
C) The marriage is suspended until they repent
D) The marriage is dissolved only if they were not living together

Key Takeaway
When both spouses apostatize together and return together, the Hanafi school holds the marriage remains valid by istihsan, following the Companions' consensus.

Nikah — Marriage

Effect of Apostasy on Mahr
Clarifies mahr entitlement when one spouse returns to Islam after apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when a spouse apostatizes and returns, distinguishing four scenarios based on consummation.

Core Idea
Apostasy dissolves marriage but not debts: consummated mahr is a binding debt.

In this lesson, we examine a fa'idah from the Hanafi tradition that clarifies how apostasy (riddah) affects the mahr obligation. The key factor is whether the marriage was consummated (dukhul) before the apostasy. The ruling shows that financial obligations, once established as debts, survive the dissolution of marriage by apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
The text presents four cases: husband returns before/after consummation, wife returns before/after consummation. For each, note the mahr entitlement.
The ruling hinges on consummation status and which spouse apostatized.
2
Locate the underlying principle
The author states: 'Because due to consummation the mahr becomes a debt upon the husband. And debts are not voided due to apostasy.' This is the rational proof (dalil aqli).
Mahr transforms from a mere promise to a binding debt upon consummation.
3
Apply the principle to each scenario
After consummation: full mahr (debt remains). Before consummation: apostasy dissolves the marriage without consummation, so no mahr if husband apostatized, half mahr if wife apostatized (by analogy to divorce before consummation).
Before consummation, the marriage is dissolved by apostasy; mahr is either nil or half per general rules.
4
Confirm the authority weight
This is a fatwa from later authorities (fatawa mutakhkhirin), cited from Fath al-Qadir. It is the mufta bihi position.
The principle that debts survive apostasy is well-established in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدہ پھر جو اسلام کی طرف لوٹا ہے اگر شوہر ہے اور عورت کے ساتھ دخول نہیں ہوا تو عورت کیلئے کچھ مہر وغیرہ نہیں ہوگا ۔ اور اگر دخول ہو چکا تو عورت کیلئے کل مہر ہوگا۔ اور اگر عورت اسلام کی طرف واپس ہوئی اور اس کے ساتھ دخول نہیں ہوا تو اس کیلئے نصف مہر ہوگا۔ اور اگر دخول ہو چکا تو اس کے لئے کل مہر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دخول کی وجہ سے مہر شوہر کے ذمہ میں دین ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور دیون ردت کی وجہ سے ساقط نہیں ہونے۔ (فتح القدير )
A benefit: Then if he (the husband) returns to Islam and there was no consummation with the wife, then the wife will have no mahr etc. And if consummation occurred, then the wife will have the full mahr. And if the wife returns to Islam and there was no consummation with her, then for her half the mahr. And if consummation occurred, then for her the full mahr. Because due to consummation the mahr becomes a debt upon the husband. And debts are not voided due to apostasy. (Fath al-Qadir)
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This is a ruling from a benefit (fa'idah) section. It explains the effect of apostasy (riddah) on the mahr (dower) when one of the spouses returns to Islam. The ruling distinguishes between four scenarios: (1) If the husband returns to Islam before consummation, the wife receives no mahr because the marriage was dissolved before consummation. (2) If the husband returns after consummation, he must pay the full mahr because it has become a debt. (3) If the wife returns before consummation, she receives half the mahr as per the general rule of divorce before consummation (since apostasy dissolves marriage). (4) If she returns after consummation, she receives full mahr. The reasoning is that after consummation, mahr is a debt (dayn) on the husband, and debts are not cancelled by apostasy. This is consistent with the Hanafi position that apostasy dissolves the marriage but does not affect already established financial obligations.

Key Terms
مہر (mahr): Dower payable by husband to wife
دخول (dukhul): Consummation of marriage
ردت (riddah): Apostasy from Islam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband apostatizes then returns to Islam after consummation, how much mahr does the wife receive?
A) None
B) Half mahr
C) Full mahr
D) Mahr al-mithl

Key Takeaway
After consummation, mahr becomes a debt that apostasy does not annul; before consummation, mahr is halved or nil depending on which spouse apostatized.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Obligation of Equal Division Among Co-Wives (Bab al-Qasm)
Establishes obligation of equal division among free wives and its application to old/new wives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on equal division among co-wives, identify its proofs, and apply the distinction between wajib overnight stay and non-wajib intercourse.

Core Idea
Equal division of nights among free wives is wajib; the heart's love is not subject to obligation.

This passage from al-Hidayah opens the Chapter of Division (Bab al-Qasm). The author establishes that when a man has multiple free wives, he must divide his nights equally among them. This obligation is proven from the Quran and hadith, and applies regardless of whether the wives are virgins or matrons, old or new. The passage also clarifies that the duty is limited to external acts—specifically the overnight stay—while intimacy depends on desire and is not part of the obligatory division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act (equal division among co-wives) and its hukm level (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the two hadiths cited as proof: the warning of paralysis for inclination, and the Prophet's prayer acknowledging his own limitation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadiths indicate obligation (wujub) – the warning implies a sin, hence the opposite (justice) is wajib.
4
Note the scope of equality
The text specifies that equality is in overnight stay (baytutah), not intercourse. Why? Because intercourse depends on desire which is not fully controllable.
5
Apply the ruling to cases
The ruling applies equally to old and new wives, virgins and matrons. There is no distinction because the hadith is absolute and division is a right of marriage.

اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ تعدد ازواج کی صورت میں عدل و مساوات ضروری ہے۔ اصحاب سنن اربعہ نے حضرت عائشہ سے روایت کی ہے قالت كان رسول الله يقسم فيعدل ويقول اللهم هذا قسمی فیما املك فلا تلمني فيما تملک و لا املک یعنی القلب اى زيادة المحبة حضرت عائشہ نے فرمایا کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم بیبیوں کی باری کی حفاظت فرماتے تھے اور عدل فرماتے تھے ۔ اور فرماتے کہ اے اللہ یہ میری قسم ہے اس چیز میں جس کا میں مالک ہوں۔ سو مجھ کو ملامت نہ فرما اس چیز میں جس کے آپ مالک ہیں اور میں مالک نہیں ہوں۔ یعنی دل یعنی زیادتی محبت۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ زیادہ محبت کے علاوہ تمام چیزیں آدمی کی ملک اور قدرت میں ہے۔ حدیث ابی ہریرہ ہے انہ قال من كانت له امرأتان فمال الى احدا هما جاء يوم القيمة و شقه مائل ای مفلوج حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا جس کی دو بیبیاں ہوں پھر وہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کی طرف مائل ہوا تو قیامت کے دن اس حال میں آئے گا کہ اس کا ایک پہلو مفلوج ہوگا۔ (فتح القدير الكفايه )

قدیمہ اور جدیدہ باری میں برابر ہیں
و القديمة والجديدة سواء لإطلاق ما روينا و لان القسم من حقوق النكاح و لا تفاوت بينهن في ذلك والاختيار فى مقدار الدورالى الزوج لان المستحق هو التسوية دون طريقها والتسوية في البيتوتة لافي المجامعة لانها تبتنى على النشاط
ترجمہ اور پرانی عورت اور نئی عورت برابر ہیں اس حدیث کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ اور اسلئے کہ بٹوارہ نکاح کے حقوق میں سے ہے۔ اور اس حق میں عورتوں کے درمیان کوئی تفاوت نہیں ہے۔ اور چکر لگانے کی مقدار میں اختیار شوہر کو ہے۔ کیونکہ واجب برابری ہے نہ کہ برابری کا طریقہ۔ اور برابری رات گزارنے میں ہے نہ کہ جماع کرنے میں۔ اسلئے کہ مجامعت نشاط پر موقوف ہے۔
تشریح جس طرح باکرہ اور شیبہ کے درمیان بنوارہ میں عدل واجب ہے اسی طرح ہمارے نزدیک نئی اور پرانی کے درمیان بھی
Chapter of Division. When the author of al-Hidayah mentioned the permissibility of multiple wives, it is necessary to mention the justice that is legislated regarding them. Hence the Chapter of Division is included. al-Qasm (with fatha on qaf) is the source, meaning equality among wives. Justice between women is also called qasm, and qism (with kasra on qaf) means portion, and qasam (with fatha on qaf and sin) means oath. qismat is the name for distribution and division. Absolute true justice is impossible, as Allah said: 'And you will never be able to be just between women, even if you desire, so do not incline completely and leave her like one hanging.' The obligation of justice in polygyny is proven from Quran and hadith. The Quranic verse: 'then if you fear that you will not be just, then one or what your right hand possesses.' The meaning is that if there is a strong possibility of not being just, then marrying multiple women is forbidden in the sense that the person will be sinful, not that the marriage is invalid. The marriage will certainly be valid. From this verse it is understood that in the case of polygyny, justice and equality are necessary. The authors of the Sunan al-Arba'ah narrated from Aisha that the Messenger of Allah used to divide and be just and said: 'O Allah, this is my division in what I own, so do not blame me in what You own and I do not own,' meaning the heart, i.e., excess of love. This hadith indicates that aside from excess love, all things are within a person's control. The hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'Whoever has two wives and inclines towards one of them in division will come on the Day of Resurrection with one side paralyzed.' (Fath al-Qadir al-Kifayah) And if a man has two free wives, then it is obligatory upon him to be just between them in division, whether both are virgins or matrons, or one is a virgin and the other a matron, due to the saying of the Prophet: 'Whoever has two wives and inclines towards one of them in division will come on the Day of Resurrection with his side paralyzed.' And from Aisha, that the Prophet used to be just in division among his wives and said: 'O Allah, this is my division in what I own, so do not take me to task in what I do not own,' i.e., excess of love. There is no distinction in what we have narrated. Explanation: If a man has two or more free wives, whether both are virgins or both matrons or one virgin and one matron, then justice in division is wajib. The author of al-Hidayah presented two hadiths as proof. The words 'excess of love' are not the words of the hadith but an interpretation by the narrators. And since there is no distinction in the hadith between virgin and matron, no difference is made in their ruling. The old and new wife are equal in division due to the absolute nature of what we narrated, and because division is from the rights of marriage, and there is no difference among them in that right. The choice in the amount of rotation is with the husband because what is obligatory is equality, not the method of equality. Equality is in spending the night, not in intercourse, because intercourse depends on desire.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This is the beginning of the Chapter of Division (Bab al-Qasm) from the Hidayah. The author first explains the necessity of mentioning justice (adl) in the context of polygyny. He defines the term 'qasm' and notes that absolute equality in the heart is impossible as per the Quran. The obligation of justice in external matters (like division of nights) is proven from Quran and Sunnah. He then cites two hadiths: one from Aisha showing the Prophet's practice and dua, and one from Abu Hurairah warning against inclination. The matn then states the ruling: for a man with two free wives, equal division is wajib regardless of their status as virgins or matrons. The commentary clarifies that the hadith does not distinguish, so all are equal. Next, the mas'alah of old and new wives: they are equal in division because it is a right of marriage. The husband has discretion in the method of rotation (e.g., how many nights each) but must be equal overall. The equality applies to overnight stays (baytutah), not to sexual intercourse, as the latter depends on desire. This is a clear Hanafi ruling emphasizing the wajib nature of external justice while acknowledging the uncontrollable nature of love.

Key Terms
قسم (qasm): Division of time among co-wives equally
عدل (adl): Justice in measurable actions, not in heart feelings
بیتوتہ (baytutah): Overnight stay, the subject of division

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, is a husband required to be equal in sexual intercourse among co-wives?
A) Yes, it is wajib
B) Yes, it is sunnah
C) No, equality is only in overnight stay
D) No, equality is only in spending

Key Takeaway
Equal division of nights among free co-wives is wajib; the heart's love and sexual intimacy are not subject to the same legal obligation.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
8 min
Obligation of Equal Division Between Free Wives
States ruling on equal division between two free wives with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on equal division of nights between free wives and cite the two hadith proofs that establish this as wajib.

Core Idea
A husband must divide nights equally between free wives; inclining to one unjustly earns divine threat.

Marrying more than one wife is permissible in Islam, but it comes with a strict duty of justice. The Hanafi school holds that equal division of time (qism) between free wives is wajib. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs from the Sunnah, including a severe warning for injustice and the Prophet's own practice of equitable division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the division of nights (qism) among a husband's free wives. The ruling is wajib: it is an obligation, not merely recommended.
The obligation applies only to free wives, not slave wives (not covered here).
2
Locate the two hadith proofs
Two hadith are cited: (1) a threat hadith: 'Whoever has two wives and inclines to one will come on the Day of Resurrection with one side leaning'; (2) a practice hadith: the Prophet used to divide equally and prayed excusing matters beyond his control (love).
These are from Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Sahih Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The threat hadith indicates that unequal division is a major sin, so equality is obligatory. The practice hadith shows the Prophet's commitment to equality, and his du'a distinguishes between what he controls (division) and what he does not (love).
This proves that division must be equal, but natural inclination of the heart is not blameworthy.
4
Note the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies equally whether both wives are virgins, both previously married, or one of each. The hadith makes no distinction, so the Hanafi position treats them the same.
Some might mistakenly give a new virgin wife more nights; this is incorrect.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
ایک آدمی کی دو آزاد عور تیں ہوتی اس پر دونوں کے درمیان باری میں برابری کر نالازم ہے خواہ
دونوں باکرہ ہوں یا شیبہ یا ایک با کر ہی دوسری شیبہ ہو
واذا كان لرجل امرأتان حرتان فعليه ان يعدل بينهما في القسم بكرين كانتا او ثيبين او احدهما بكر او الاخرى ثيبا لقوله عليه السلام من كانت له امرأتان ومال الى احدهما في القسم جاء يوم القيمة وشقه مائل وعن عائشة رضى الله عنها ان النبي عليه السلام كان يعدل في القسم بين نسائه وكان يقول اللهم هذا قسمى فيما املك فلاتواخذني فيما لا املک یعنی زيادة المحبة ولافصل فيما رويـنـا
ترجمہ اور ایک مرد کی منکوحہ دو عورتیں آزاد ہوں تو اس پر واجب ہے کہ دونوں کے درمیان بانٹنے میں برابری کرے۔ دونوں باکرہ ہوں یا شیبہ یا ان دونوں میں سے ایک باکرہ ہو اور دوسری شیبہ ۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کی وجہ سے۔ جس شخص کی دو بیویاں ہوں اور وہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کی طرف جھک گیا بانٹنے میں تو قیامت کے دن اس حال میں آئے گا کہ اس کا آدھا دھڑ مفلوج ہوگا ۔ اور عائشہ سے مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اپنی عورتوں کے درمیان بانٹنے میں عدل فرماتے تھے۔ اور فرماتے تھے کہ الہی یہ میرا ہوارہ ایسے امور میں ہے جس کا میں مالک ہوں ۔ پس مجھ سے مواخذہ نہ فرمائیے ایسے امور میں جن کا میں مالک نہیں ہوں۔ یعنی محبت کی زیادت اور جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے اس میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ اگر ایک مرد کی دو یا زیادہ آزاد عورتیں ہیں خواہ دونوں باکرہ ہوں یا دونوں شیبہ یا ایک باکرہ اور دوسری شیبہ تو ان میں انصاف کے ساتھ بانٹنا واجب ہے۔ دلیل میں صاحب ہدایہ نے دو حدیثیں پیش کی ہیں۔ دونوں حدیثوں کا مضمون عنوان کے تحت گذر چکا ملاحظہ کر لیا جائے ۔ زیادۃ المحبۃ کے الفاظ حدیث کے الفاظ نہیں ہیں بلکہ رواۃ کی طرف سے تفسیر ہے۔ اور چونکہ حدیث میں باکرہ اور شیبہ میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے اسلئے ان کے حکم میں کوئی فرق نہیں کیا گیا۔
The Book of Nikah. 192. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Four. A man has two free wives; it is necessary for him to be equitable between them in division, whether both are virgins or previously married, or one is a virgin and the other previously married. And if a man has two free wives, it is upon him to balance between them in division, whether they are virgins or previously married, or one is a virgin and the other previously married, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever has two wives and inclines towards one of them in division will come on the Day of Resurrection with one side leaning.' And from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to be equitable in division between his wives and used to say: 'O Allah, this is my division in what I possess, so do not hold me accountable for what I do not possess,' meaning excess of love. And there is no detail in what we narrated. Translation: And a man's two wives are free, so it is obligatory upon him to be equitable between them in division. Both are virgins or previously married, or one is a virgin and the other previously married, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever has two wives and inclines towards one of them in division will come on the Day of Resurrection with half his body paralyzed.' And it is narrated from Aisha that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to be equitable in division between his wives and used to say: 'O Allah, this is my division in what I possess, so do not hold me accountable for what I do not possess,' meaning excess of love. And there is no detail in what we narrated. Explanation: The ruling: if a man has two or more free wives, whether both are virgins or both previously married, or one virgin and one previously married, equitable division between them is obligatory. In the proof, the author of Hidayah presented two hadiths. The content of both hadiths has passed under the heading; it may be reviewed. The words 'excess of love' are not the words of the hadith but an interpretation from the narrators. And since there is no detail in the hadith between virgin and previously married, no distinction is made in their ruling.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the obligation of equal division (qism) between two free wives. The author begins by stating the ruling: a husband with two free wives must treat them equally in the division of nights, whether they are virgins or previously married. The proof is from two hadith: the first warns of the severe consequence of inclining towards one wife, and the second shows the Prophet's practice of equitable division and his du'a excusing what is beyond his control (love). The commentary explains that the words 'excess of love' are an interpretation, not the hadith text. Since the hadith makes no distinction between a virgin and a previously married wife, the ruling applies equally to both. The level of obligation is wajib, as indicated by the warning.

Key Terms
باری (bari): The division of nights among wives by the husband.
باکرہ (bakr): A virgin woman.
ثیبہ (thayyib): A previously married woman.
عدل (adl): Equity; here, equal treatment in division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling regarding division of nights between two free wives?
A) It is recommended (sunnah) but not obligatory.
B) It is obligatory (wajib) to divide equally regardless of virginity.
C) It is obligatory only if both are virgins.
D) It is obligatory only if one is a virgin and the other is not.

Key Takeaway
Equal division of nights between free wives is wajib; the husband who inclines unjustly incurs a severe divine threat, while love outside his control is excused.

Nikah — Marriage

Equality of Old and New Wives in Division
Establishes equality of old and new wives with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on division of nights for a new wife and explain the opposing evidence from the hadith of Anas, distinguishing between obligatory equality and recommended practices.

Core Idea
A new wife is equal to old wives in division; no extra nights are required in the Hanafi school.

In this passage, the author establishes that old and new wives are treated equally in the division of nights (qism). This is a point of disagreement between the Hanafi school and the majority of other schools. The Hanafi proof relies on the generality of hadiths about equal treatment, while opponents cite the specific practice of the Prophet with a new wife. Let's examine the arguments and the reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: all wives, old and new, are equal in division; no special consecutive nights for a new wife.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
State the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali position: a new wife gets extra nights (7 if virgin, 3 if previously married). Identify their proof: the hadith of Anas.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain how the Hanafi school rebuts the opposing proof: their own general hadiths are absolute (mutlaq), and the hadith of Anas is interpreted as specific to the Prophet or recommended (mustahabb), not wajib.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Contrast the practical consequence: under Hanafi law, no extra nights; under other schools, extra nights are obligatory.
5
Examine ancillary rulings
Note that equality is only in nights spent, not in intercourse, and the husband has discretion in setting cycle length, provided he does not exceed one week or the period of ila (4 months) without consent.

Old and new wives are equal in division. The old and new are equal due to the generality of what we narrated, and because division is among the rights of marriage, and there is no distinction among them in that. The choice in the amount of rotation is the husband's, because what is owed is equality, not the method of equality. And equality is in spending the night, not in intercourse, because intercourse depends on desire. Translation: And the old woman and the new woman are equal, due to the generality of the hadith we narrated, and because division is from the rights of marriage, and there is no distinction among women in that right. And the choice in the amount of the cycle is the husband's, because what is obligatory is equality, not the way of equality. And equality is in spending the night, not in intercourse, because intercourse depends on desire. Explanation: Just as justice in division between a virgin and a previously married woman is obligatory, similarly in our view it is necessary to maintain equality between the new and the old. Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad said: if the new wife is a virgin, he should stay with her for seven days after marriage; if she is previously married, he should stay for three days. Their proof is the hadith of Anas: from Anas from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he appointed seven for the virgin and three for the previously married. And he said: it is from the sunnah that if one marries a virgin over a previously married woman, he stays with her for seven days then divides; and if one marries a previously married woman, he stays with her for three days then divides. (Sahihayn). Our proof is the hadiths which the author of Hidayah mentioned in the previous issue: these two hadiths are general. Therefore, there will be no difference between the new and the old. And the rational proof is that fixing division is from the rights of marriage. Just as maintenance (nafaqah) is from the rights of marriage, and in that right there is no difference between virgin and previously married, new and old, similarly here. Also, there is no difference between a Muslim and a Kitabiyya, between a virgin and a girl approaching puberty, between a madwoman and a sane woman, between a sick woman and a healthy woman, because the cause of this right (halal due to marriage) is equal among them. And the husband has choice in fixing the amount of the cycle: whether he wants to fix one day, two days, three days, or four days. And since the purpose of this division is to create familiarity and remove estrangement, it is necessary to consider a short period. In my opinion, a cycle of more than one week is burdensome. Therefore, it is appropriate to avoid fixing more than a week. However, if the women agree to more, there is no harm. But it is appropriate that this amount does not reach the period of ila (four months). The reason for giving the husband choice is that equality is obligatory upon the husband, but the method of equality is not obligatory. And equality is only in spending the night, not in intercourse. That is, he should spend equal nights with all wives. Intercourse on those nights is not a condition, because intercourse depends on desire and vigor, and that is not in his control. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the treatment of a new wife in the division of nights. The Hanafi position is that old and new wives are equal. The proof is twofold: (1) the hadiths previously cited (on equality) are general and do not distinguish between old and new; (2) rational argument: division is a right of marriage, like maintenance, and all wives are equal in that right regardless of their status. The opposing schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that a new wife, if virgin, gets seven consecutive nights, if previously married, three nights, citing the hadith of Anas. The Hanafi response is that their own hadiths are general and the hadith of Anas is interpreted as specific to the Prophet or as recommended (sunnah) rather than obligatory. The passage also emphasizes that equality is in nights spent, not in intercourse, and that the husband has discretion in setting the cycle length, provided he does not exceed what is reasonable (e.g., one week) or the period of ila (four months).

Key Terms
جدیدہ (jadidah): A new wife (recently married).
قدیمہ (qadimah): An old wife (pre-existing).
قسم (qism): Division of nights among wives.
دور (dawr): Cycle; the period for which a husband stays with each wife in rotation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that all wives, old and new, are equal in division; a new wife does not receive extra nights, as equality is wajib and the method is discretionary.

Dispute on Nights for Bride: Hanafi Equality vs. Other Schools
Debates the number of days a husband stays with a new wife before rotating.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the division of nights for a new wife and explain the Hanafi response to the opposing proof based on the hadith of Anas.

Core Idea
All wives are equal in the right to nights; virginity does not entitle extra time.

One of the key debates in marriage law is whether a husband must spend extra nights exclusively with a new wife before resuming rotation among co-wives. The Hanafi school holds that all wives are equal from the start, while the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools differentiate based on virginity. In this lesson, we examine the evidence and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding the division of nights for a new wife.
No distinction between bikr and thayyib.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
State the view of the majority (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) and the hadith they rely on.
Hadith of Anas: seven for virgin, three for non-virgin.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain why the Hanafis do not consider the hadith of Anas as obligating a distinction, and how they use analogy with nafaqah.
The hadith is seen as permissive, not obligatory; qiyas with nafaqah shows equality.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Describe the practical difference in application between the Hanafi and opposing views.
In practice, a Hanafi husband begins rotation immediately; others require an extended stay.

واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Chapter of Marriage: Maintaining equality is necessary. Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad said: If the new wife is a virgin (bikr), the husband stays with her seven days after the marriage contract, and if she is a non-virgin (thayyib), he stays three days. Their proof is the hadith of Anas: 'The Prophet assigned seven for the virgin and three for the non-virgin.' Also from Anas: 'It is from the Sunnah that when one marries a virgin over a non-virgin, he stays seven days then divides, and when he marries a non-virgin, he stays three days then divides.' (Sahihayn). Our proof is the hadiths mentioned by the author of Hidayah in the previous issue, which are absolute, so there is no difference between new and old. The rational proof: Dividing nights is among the rights of marriage, like maintenance (nafaqah), and in that right there is no difference between virgin and non-virgin, new and old, Muslim and kitabiyya, etc. The husband has discretion in setting the duration of the turn, but it should not be too long. Equality is only in spending nights, not necessarily in intercourse. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of days a husband must stay exclusively with a new wife before resuming rotation among co-wives. The Hanafi position, as stated in the Hidayah, holds that there is no distinction between a virgin and a non-virgin; the husband simply begins the rotation immediately after the marriage, and all wives are equal in the right to division of nights. The opposing view (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) is based on the hadith of Anas which specifies seven days for a virgin and three for a non-virgin. The Hanafi response argues that those hadiths are absolute and do not create a distinction, and that by analogy with nafaqah, which is equal for all wives, division of nights is also equal. The passage also discusses the husband's discretion in setting the length of the turn, recommending it not exceed a week or reach the period of ila' (four months). The emphasis is on equal treatment in terms of nights spent, not intercourse.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): A woman who has never been married or had sexual intercourse.
ثيب (thayyib): A woman who has been previously married (non-virgin).
قسم (qism): The division of nights among co-wives.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance provided by husband to wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Seven nights if she is a virgin, three if non-virgin.
B) The husband must spend one year with the new wife before dividing.
C) There is no distinction; the husband starts the rotation immediately after marriage.
D) The husband may choose but must compensate other wives with money.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school insists on strict equality in the division of nights, rejecting any distinction based on virginity.

Division Between Free and Slave Wife
Ruling with proof on proportional division of nights.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the division of nights between a free wife and a slave wife, explain the two proofs (athar and talil), and apply the same ruling to mukatabah, mudabbara, and umm walad.

Core Idea
A free wife gets two-thirds of the nights; a slave wife gets one-third—because her legal capacity is less.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi position on a specific case of marital division: when a man has one free wife and one slave wife. The ruling is established both by an athar (tradition from the Companions) and by a rational proof based on the difference in 'halal' (lawful intimacy). The same logic extends to other categories of women with partial servitude. Understanding this ruling illustrates how the Hanafi school considers legal capacity (ahliyyah) in the distribution of marital rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The division of nights between a free wife and a slave wife. The ruling: free wife gets two-thirds, slave wife gets one-third.
The ruling is explicit in the matn.
2
Locate the first proof (athar)
The text says 'بذلك ورد الاثر' (the tradition came regarding this). The commentary attributes this to Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and Ali. This is the textual evidence.
The athar is a Companion practice (qawl sahabi).
3
Analyze the second proof (talil)
The rational proof: 'لان حل الامة انقص من حل الحرة' (because the halal of the slave is less than that of the free). Therefore, deficiency in rights is shown proportionally.
This is an illah-based deduction.
4
Extend to analogous cases
The text applies the same ruling to mukatabah, mudabbara, and umm walad because they still possess riqq (servitude).
The illah is the presence of slavery, not the specific type.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih; other schools may not differentiate based on slavery in division of nights.
The Hanafi position is based on specific evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و ان كانت احدهما حرة و الاخرى امة فللحرة الثلثان من القسم وللامة الثلث بذلك ورد الاثرولان حل الامة انقص من حل الحرة فلابد من اظهار النقصان فى الحقوق والمكاتبة والمدبرة وام الولد بمنزلة الامة لان الرق فيهن قائم ترجمہ اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک آزاد اور دوسری باندی ہو تو آزاد کیلئے باری میں سے دو تہائی اور باندی کیلئے ایک تہائی ہے۔ اس پر اثر وارد ہوا ہے اور اس لئے کہ باندی کی حلت آزاد کی حلت سے کم ہے۔ لہذا حقوق میں نقصان کا اظہار ضروری ہوا اور مکاتبہ اور مدبرہ اورام ولد باندی کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ رقیت ان میں موجود ہے۔ تشریح اگر کسی کے نکاح میں ایک آزاد عورت ہے اور ایک باندی تو بٹوارہ میں سے دو تہائی آزاد کا ہوگا۔ اور ایک تہائی باندی کا۔ دلیل میں اثر پیش کیا گیا ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے الکفایہ میں لکھا کہ یہی فیصلہ صدیق اکبر اور حضرت علیؓ نے کیا ہے۔ دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ چونکہ باندی کی حلت آزاد عورت کی حلت سے کم ہے لہذا حقوق میں نقصان ظاہر کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اور اگر باندی کسی آدمی کی مکاتبہ یا مدبرہ یا ام ولد ہے تو وہ بھی باندی کے مرتبہ میں ہے کیونکہ ان میں رقیت موجود ہے۔
And if one of them (wives) is free and the other a slave, then for the free woman is two-thirds of the division, and for the slave woman is one-third. The tradition (athar) has come regarding this. And because the halal (lawful intimacy) of a slave woman is less than the halal of a free woman, so it is necessary to show deficiency in rights. The mukatabah, mudabbara, and umm walad are like a slave woman, because servitude (riqq) exists in them. Translation: And if one is free and the other is a slave, then the free gets two-thirds of the turns and the slave one-third. This is based on an athar (tradition), and because the halal of the slave is less than that of the free, so deficiency must be shown in rights. The mukatabah, mudabbara, and umm walad are like a slave because servitude exists in them. Commentary: The ruling is based on the judgment of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and Ali. The rational proof is that the legal capacity of a slave is less than that of a free woman, so deficiency in rights is necessary.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the division of nights when a man has one free wife and one slave wife. The free wife receives two-thirds of the nights, and the slave wife receives one-third. This proportional division is based on an athar (tradition from the Companions) and on the rational principle that the 'halal' (permissible intimacy) of a slave woman is less than that of a free woman due to the restrictions of slavery. Therefore, the deficiency in rights is shown proportionally. The same ruling applies to a mukatabah (slave under contract of manumission), mudabbara (slave whose freedom is deferred after the master's death), and umm walad (slave mother of the master's child) because they still possess some degree of slavery (riqq). The commentary by Ibn al-Humam in al-Kifayah attributes this judgment to Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and Ali.

Key Terms
حرة (hurra): A free woman (not a slave).
أمة (ama): A female slave.
حل (halal): Lawful sexual intimacy; here refers to the permissible nature of the marriage relationship.
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A slave who has contracted with her master to earn and purchase her freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Each gets an equal share regardless of status.
B) The free wife gets two-thirds, the slave wife gets one-third.
C) The slave wife gets two-thirds, the free wife gets one-third.
D) The husband must free the slave wife before dividing.

Key Takeaway
The division of nights between a free wife and a slave wife is proportional: two-thirds for the free and one-third for the slave, based on an athar and the principle of diminished legal capacity.

Hanafi vs. Shafi'i: Casting Lots Among Wives Before Travel
Explains that wives have no right to division during travel and lots are recommended.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on casting lots among wives before travel and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
During travel, wives have no right to division; casting lots is recommended to please hearts, not obligatory.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses two interconnected issues: the division of nights during travel and the recommended practice of casting lots. The Hanafi school holds that wives have no right to division when the husband is traveling, so he may choose any wife without compensation. Casting lots is mustahabb (recommended) to avoid partiality, not wajib. The Shafi'i school disagrees, viewing lots as an obligation based on the Prophet's practice. We will explore the proofs and the practical consequence of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: wives have no right to division during travel; husband may travel with whomever he wishes; casting lots is recommended but not obligatory.
The rule applies to all types of travel, long or short.
2
Identify the Opposing School and Their View
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that casting lots is wajib (obligatory) before travel, based on the Prophet's consistent practice.
3
Follow the Opponent's Proof
The Shafi'i proof is the hadith that the Prophet always cast lots among his wives when he intended to travel. They see this as evidence of obligation.
Hadith is authentic (muttafaq alayh).
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response: the Prophet's action was to please the wives' hearts, not to establish a wajib. Also, the Prophet himself was not required to divide nights equally (Quran 33:51). Therefore, the act falls under istihbab.
The Quranic verse allows the Prophet to postpone the turn of any wife, showing that division is not mandatory.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi says if a husband travels without lots, no compensation is owed. Shafi'i says he must compensate by staying with the left-behind wives for an equal period.
A visible difference in real-life application.

He (al-Quduri) said: And they (wives) have no right to division during travel. So the husband may travel with whomever he wishes from among them, and it is better that he cast lots among them, then travel with the one whose lot comes out. And al-Shafi'i said: The lot is an established right (wajib), because it is narrated that the Prophet, when he intended to travel, would cast lots among his wives. But we say that the lot is to please their hearts, so it falls under recommendation (istihbab). This is because the woman has no right when the husband travels; do you not see that he may not take any of them? Similarly, he may travel with one of them, and that period is not counted against him (in the division). And if one of the wives agrees to leave her turn for her co-wife, it is permissible, because Sawdah bint Zam'ah asked the Messenger of Allah to take her back and make her day for Aisha. And she has the right to revoke that, because she relinquished a right that had not yet become due, so it does not lapse. Translation: al-Quduri said: In travel, wives have no right to division. The husband may travel with whomever he wants, but it is better to cast lots. If he does not, it is not counted. The Shafi'i view is that lots are obligatory. The Hanafi response: The Prophet's action was for comfort, not obligation. Commentary: The Hanafi position is that lots are mustahabb, not wajib. If a wife gives up her turn voluntarily, it is valid but she may revoke it before the turn actually occurs.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct but related issues: the division of nights during travel and a wife's voluntary waiver of her turn. The Hanafi position, following al-Quduri, is that during travel, wives have no right to division of nights. The husband may travel with whichever wife he chooses, and it is recommended but not obligatory to cast lots. Imam al-Shafi'i considers casting lots obligatory based on the Prophet's practice of drawing lots among his wives before travel. The Hanafi response argues that the Prophet's action was to comfort the wives' hearts, making it mustahabb (recommended) rather than wajib. Furthermore, since the husband may even travel alone, he may choose without lots. The passage also addresses the scenario where a wife voluntarily forfeits her turn to a co-wife, citing the example of Sawdah bint Zam'ah who gave her day to Aisha. Such a waiver is valid, but the wife may revoke it before the turn becomes due because she is relinquishing a right not yet obligatory. The commentary emphasises that the Hanafi school sees lots as a recommended means to avoid partiality, not a required condition for travel.

Key Terms
قسم (qism): Division of nights among co-wives.
قرعة (qur'a): Casting lots to determine which wife accompanies the husband on travel.
استحباب (istihbab): Recommendation; an act that is encouraged but not obligatory.
سودة بنت زمعة (Sawdah bint Zam'ah): A wife of the Prophet who voluntarily gave her day to Aisha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on casting lots among wives before a husband travels?
A) It is obligatory (wajib) and failure to do so requires compensation.
B) It is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory.
C) It is forbidden because it creates discord.
D) It is required only if the wives demand it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that casting lots before travel is mustahabb, not wajib, because wives have no right to division during travel.

Division of Time (Qism) During Travel: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presents Hanafi position on qism during travel and refutes Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that qism is suspended during travel and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding drawing lots.

Core Idea
A wife's right to equal division of nights is suspended during travel; drawing lots is recommended, not obligatory.

In marriage, the husband must divide his nights equally among co-wives when at home. But does this duty extend to travel? This passage from al-Hidayah contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i views on whether a husband must draw lots before traveling with one wife, and whether missed turns must be compensated.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on qism during travel
Identify the core ruling: wives have no right to qism when the husband travels. The husband may freely choose which wife to take, and drawing lots is only recommended, not obligatory.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that drawing lots is obligatory (wajib) based on the hadith that the Prophet would cast lots among his wives before travel.
The hadith is cited as the primary evidence for obligation.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using the Quranic verse
The Hanafi school responds by citing Quran 33:51, which shows the Prophet was not bound by qism. Therefore, the Prophet's own action of casting lots cannot be obligatory—it was for the purpose of pleasing hearts (istihbab).
This illustrates the Hanafi usul principle of using the Quran to qualify the legal implication of a Prophetic action.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: Under Hanafi, if the husband travels without lots, he owes no compensation to the left-behind wife. Under Shafi'i, he must make up the missed nights.
This consequence directly affects the husband's obligation and the wife's claim.
5
Understand the tarjih (why the Hanafi position is relied upon)
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because it is supported by a clear Qur'anic text (33:51) that removes the basis for qism obligation, and the primary evidence for the Shafi'i view is interpreted as recommendation rather than obligation.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah affirms the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حالت سفر میں قسم نہیں
قال ولاحق لهن فى القسم حالة السفر فيسا فر الزوج بمن شاء منهن والأولى ان يقرع بينهن فيسا فربمن خرجت قرعتها وقال الشافعى القرعة مستحقة لماروى ان النبي عليه السلام كان اذا اراد سفرا اقرع بين نسائه الا انا نقول ان القرعة لتطييب قلوبهن فيكون من باب الاستحباب وهذا لانه لاحق للمرأة عند مسافرة الزوج الايرى ان له ان لايستصحب واحدة منهن فكذاله ان يسافر بواحدة منهن ولا يحتسب عليه بتلك المدة
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ سفر کی حالت میں منکوحات کا قسم میں کوئی حق نہیں ہے۔ پس شوہر ان میں سے جس کے ساتھ چاہے سفر کرے اور بہتر یہ ہے کہ ان میں قرعہ ڈالے۔ پھر جس کا قرعہ نکلے اس کا ساتھ سفر کرے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قرد حق واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے نبی جب سفر کا ارادہ کرتے تو اپنی عورتوں میں قرعہ ڈلاتے ۔ مگر ہم کہتے ہیں کہ قرعہ عورتوں کی دلجوئی کیلئے تھا۔ لہذا وہ استحباب کے قبیل سے ہو گا۔ یہ اسلئے کہ شوہر کے سفر کرتے وقت عورت کا کوئی حق نہیں ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتا کہ شوہر کیلئے جائز ہے کہ ان میں سے کسی کو ساتھ نہ لے۔ پس ایسے ہی اس کیلئے جائز ہے ان میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ سفر کرے اور یہ مدت اسپر محسوب نہیں ہوگی ۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص کی متعدد بیویاں ہیں تو سفر کی حالت میں ان کیلئے بنوارہ میں کوئی حق نہی ہے ان میں سے جس کے ساتھ چاہے سفر کرے۔ بہتر یہ ہے کہ ان میں قرعہ اندازی کرے جس کے نام کا قرعہ نکلے اسی کے ساتھ سفر کرے۔ یہ احناف کا مذہب ہے۔ امام شافعی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ قرعہ ڈالنا واجب ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر بغیر قرعہ کے کسی ایک کے ساتھ سفر کیا تو یہ مدت سفر محسوب ہوگی عینی اتنی ہی مدت اس عورت کے ساتھ قیام کرے جس کے ساتھ سفر نہیں کیا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم جب سفر کا ارادہ فرماتے تھے۔ تو اپنی عورتوں میں قرعہ اندازی فرماتے تھے۔ پس جس کا نام نکل آتا اسی کے ساتھ آپ سفر کرتے ۔ امام شافعی اس فعل نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم سے وجوب قرعہ پر استدلال کرتے ہیں ۔ لیکن ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا اپنی عورتوں میں قرعہ اندازی کرنا صرف ان کے دل خوش کرنے کیلئے تھا۔ لہذایہ قرعہ اندازی استبا ہا ہوگا نہ که و جو بادوسری بات یہ کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر قسم ( باری مقرر کرنا ) واجب ہی نہیں تھا۔ چنانچہ اللہ رب العزت کا ارشاد ہے تــرجـــى من تشاء منهن و تؤی الیک من تشاء یعنی ان میں سے آپ جس کو چاہیں اپنے سے دور رکھیں اور جس کو چاہیں اپنے نزدیک رکھیں ۔ (بیان القرآن ) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم قسم (باری) کے پابند نہیں ہیں۔ چنانچہ حافظ عبد العظیم منذری نے ذکر کیا کہ آپ نے سوده، جویریہ، ام حبیبہ، صفیہ اور میمونہ کو دور رکھا اور عائشہ اور باقی ازواج مطہرات کو اپنے نزدیک رکھا۔ پس جب آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر قتم ہی واجب نہیں ہے، تو قرعہ اندازی کیوں کر واجب ہوگی۔ اور قرعہ کا باب استحباب سے ہونا اسلئے بھی ہے کہ شوہر کے سفر کرنے کے وقت عورت کا کوئی حق ہی نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر شوہر ان میں سے کسی کو اپنے ساتھ سفر میں لے جائے تو اس کو اس کا اختیار ہے۔ اسی طرح یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ ان میں سے کسی کو اپنے ساتھ سفر میں نہ لے جائے تو اس کو اس کا اختیار ہے۔ اسی طرح یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ ان میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ سفر کرے اور یہ مدت محسوب نہیں ہوگی۔
Division during travel: He said: There is no right for them (wives) in division during travel. So the husband may travel with whomever he wishes among them. The better option is to cast lots among them, and then travel with the one whose lot emerges. Al-Shafi'i said: The lot is obligatory, due to the narration that the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he intended to travel, cast lots among his wives. But we say that the lot is to please their hearts, so it falls under recommendation. This is because the wife has no right when the husband travels. Do you not see that he is permitted not to take any of them? Similarly, he may travel with one of them, and that period is not counted against him. Translation: Quduri said: In the state of travel, wives have no right in division. So the husband may travel with whomever he wishes. It is better to cast lots. The one whose lot emerges, he travels with her. Imam Shafi'i said: The lot is obligatory. Because it is narrated that the Prophet, when he intended to travel, would cast lots among his wives. But we say that the lot was to please the wives' hearts. Therefore it falls under recommendation. This is because the wife has no right when the husband travels. Do you not see that the husband is permitted not to take any of them? Similarly, he is permitted to travel with one of them, and this period is not counted against him. Commentary: The issue is that if a person has multiple wives, in travel they have no right in division. He may travel with whomever he wishes. It is better to cast lots. Whose name appears, he travels with her. This is the Hanafi madhhab. Imam Shafi'i's madhhab is that casting lots is obligatory. So if he traveled without a lot, the travel period is counted, and he must stay with the wife he did not travel with for the same period. Imam Shafi'i's evidence is the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet, when he intended to travel, would cast lots among his wives. Whose name came out, he traveled with her. Imam Shafi'i deduces obligation from this action of the Prophet. But our response is that the Prophet's casting lots among his wives was only to please their hearts. Therefore it is recommended, not obligatory. The second point: The Prophet was not obligated to division. Allah says: "You may put aside whom you will of them and take to you whom you will." This verse indicates that the Prophet was not bound by division. Hafiz Abdul Azim al-Mundhiri mentioned that he kept away Sawda, Juwayriyya, Umm Habiba, Safiyya, and Maymuna, and kept Aisha and the rest close. When division is not obligatory on the Prophet, how can casting lots be obligatory? The matter of casting lots falls under recommendation also because the wife has no right when the husband travels. If the husband takes one with him, he has that option. Similarly, he has the option not to take any. Similarly, he may travel with one, and this period is not counted.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the rights of wives to equal division of time (qism) when the husband travels. The Hanafi position, stated first, is that wives have no right to qism during travel; the husband may choose freely. Drawing lots (qur'a) is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory. Al-Shafi'i holds that drawing lots is obligatory (wajib), based on the Prophetic practice of casting lots before travel. The Hanafi response argues that the Prophetic action was for pleasing hearts (istihbab), not obligation. Moreover, the verse (33:51) shows that the Prophet was not bound by qism at all, a fortiori drawing lots cannot be obligatory. The Hanafi view is further supported by the principle that a husband may even leave all wives behind, so taking one does not create a debt of time. This passage also illustrates the Hanafi method of using a Qur'anic verse (dalil aqli via istidlal) to limit the legal force of a prophetic practice, classifying it as recommendation rather than obligation.

Key Terms
قسم (qism): The husband's duty to divide nights equally among wives in residence.
قرعة (qur'a): Drawing lots to choose among wives for travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a husband travels without drawing lots among his wives, what is the ruling?
A) It is sinful, and he must make up the missed nights to the wife left behind.
B) It is permissible, and the travel period is not counted against him.
C) It is invalid, and the marriage is affected.
D) It is mandatory to draw lots only if the wives demand it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a wife's right to equal division of nights is suspended during travel; therefore, drawing lots is recommended but not obligatory, and no compensation is required.

Wife Voluntarily Giving Her Turn to a Co-Wife and Revocation
Ruling on a wife gifting her turn to a co-wife and later revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife giving her turn to a co-wife and explain the basis for revocation.

Core Idea
A wife may revoke her gift of a turn because the right was not yet due.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common situation in polygyny: if a wife voluntarily gives her allocated night to a co-wife, is that permissible? And if she later changes her mind, can she revoke? The text provides a clear ruling supported by the practice of Sawda bint Zam'a, one of the Prophet's wives. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi principle that a future right cannot be permanently dropped.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is a wife agreeing to leave her turn for a co-wife. The ruling is that it is ja'iz (permissible).
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
The proof is the story of Sawda bint Zam'a who offered her turn to Aisha. The Prophet accepted, indicating permissibility.
The dalil is a hadith (though not quoted verbatim).
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does the story prove permissibility? The Prophet's acceptance shows consent; if it were impermissible, he would have forbidden it.
This is implicit approval (taqriri sunnah).
4
Examine the Ruling on Revocation
The wife may revoke her gift before the turn becomes due. The reason: she waived a right that was not yet due, so it is not permanently dropped.
The key legal principle: a future right cannot be saqit (nullified) by a mere promise.
5
Understand the Legal Implication
Revocation is not taking back a dropped right; it is merely refraining from giving. The turn is a right that vests only when the night arrives.
This clarifies that no actual property was transferred.

Source Text

وان رضيت احدى الزوجات يترك قسمها لصا حبتها جازلان سودة بنت زمعة رضى الله عنها سالت رسول الله عليه السلام ان يراجعها وتجعل يوم نوبتها لعائشة عنها ولها ان ترجع في ذلك لانها اسقطت حقالم يجب بعد فلا يسقط
ترجمہ اور اگر منکوحات میں سے کوئی اپنی باری اپنی سوکن کیلئے چھوڑنے پر راضی ہوگئی تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ سودہ بنت زمعہ نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے درخواست کی تھی کہ سودہ سے مراجعت فرما دیں اور سودہ اپنی باری کا دن عائشہ کیلئے مقرر کر دے گی۔ اور اس عورت کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ اپنی باری میں رجوع کرلے۔ کیونکہ اس عورت نے ایسا حق ساقط کیا جو ابھی تک واجب نہیں ہوا تھا۔ لہذا ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔
تشریح اور جس عورت نے اپنی باری کا دن دوسری اپنی سوتن کو دے دیا اس کیلئے جائز ہے کہ وہ اپنے اس حق کو واپس لے لے۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایسا حق ساقط کیا جو ابھی تک واجب نہیں ہوا۔ لہذا وہ ساقط ہی نہیں ہوگا۔ پس یہ رجوع اپنی باری دینے سے رکنا ہوگا نہ کہ کسی ساقط شدہ چیز کو واپس لینا۔
And if one of the wives agrees to leave her turn for her co-wife, it is permissible. Because Sawda bint Zam'a, may Allah be pleased with her, asked the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, to take her back (after divorce) and she would make her day (of turn) for Aisha. And she has the right to revoke that, because she waived a right that was not yet due, so it is not dropped. Translation: And if one of the wives agrees to give her turn to her co-wife, it is permissible. Because Sawda bint Zam'a asked the Messenger of Allah to take her back, and she would give her turn to Aisha. And that woman has the authority to revoke it, because she waived a right that had not yet become due. Therefore it is not nullified. Commentary: And a woman who gave her turn to her co-wife may take it back, because she waived a right not yet due, so it is not dropped. So this revocation is merely refraining from giving, not taking back a dropped right.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a wife voluntarily giving her night to a co-wife. The ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz). The proof is the incident of Sawda bint Zam'a, who after being divorced, asked the Prophet to take her back and offered to give her turn to Aisha. The second part addresses revocation: the wife may revoke this gift before the turn becomes due, because she is only waiving a future right, and a future right cannot be permanently dropped. Thus, revocation is not taking back something already dropped, but simply deciding not to give it. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that rights not yet due can be waived but are revocable until they vest.

Key Terms
باری (bari): The assigned night of a wife for qism.
ساقط (saqit): Dropped or nullified (right).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a wife revoke her decision to give her turn to a co-wife according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Because she owns the night property absolutely.
B) Because she waived a right that was not yet due, so it is not dropped.
C) Because the husband can force her to revoke.
D) Because the co-wife must consent to the revocation.

Key Takeaway
A wife may revoke her gift of a turn because the right was not yet due, so the waiver is not final.

Prophet's Exemption from Qasm and Wife's Transfer of Turn
Ruling on qasm for the Prophet and transfer of turn by wives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and Hadith evidence for the Prophet's exemption from qasm and explain the Hanafi ruling on a wife transferring her turn to a co-wife, including the permissibility of revocation.

Core Idea
The Prophet was not obligated to divide nights equally; a wife may give her turn to a co-wife and revoke it before it becomes due.

This lesson examines two rulings from the Hanafi fiqh of marriage. First, the special exemption of the Prophet from the obligation of equal division of nights (qasm) among his wives, based on Quranic permission. Second, the general ruling that a wife may voluntarily transfer her turn to a co-wife, and that she retains the right to revoke that transfer before the night occurs. The proof for the latter is the well-known hadith of Saudah bint Zam'ah, demonstrating the application of Sunnah in deriving legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal issues
The passage addresses two distinct issues: (1) whether the Prophet was required to divide nights equally (qasm), and (2) whether a wife can transfer her turn to a co-wife. Recognize that the first is a special exemption for the Prophet, while the second is a general permissibility.
2
Locate the evidence for the Prophet's exemption
The author cites the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ahzab 33:51) which grants the Prophet the choice to keep away or draw near any of his wives. This indicates that qasm was not obligatory upon him. The author also mentions the observation of Hafiz al-Mundhiri that the Prophet actually kept some wives at a distance.
The exemption is specific to the Prophet; other husbands are required to divide nights equally.
3
Examine the hadith proof for the wife's transfer
The passage provides the hadith of Saudah. Read the narration carefully: Saudah, after being divorced, requests the Prophet to take her back and offers to give her night to Aisha. The Prophet's acceptance constitutes tacit approval (taqrir) of the transfer.
The hadith is a sahih narration, though the chain is not specified in the text.
4
Analyze the Hanafi legal reasoning
The author explains that the transfer is permissible because the right (the night) had not yet become due. Therefore, when the wife waives it, the waiver does not take effect until the turn actually arrives. This is why she can revoke it before that time.
This reasoning is based on the Hanafi principle that rights not yet vested can be withdrawn.
5
Note the practical consequence and difference of opinion
The Hanafi school holds this as mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). However, other schools may disagree. The practical consequence is that a wife may freely arrange turns with co-wives, but she retains the right to change her mind until the night arrives.
This ruling promotes harmony among co-wives while protecting individual rights.

Source Text
